[x] **Slice 8d — caller-side network-boundary intercept shipped 2026-05-18.** Hook in `compile_call` (immediately after the closure-call check, before the module symbol lookup) that intercepts calls to any callee in `state_machine_state_constructors` (slice 8c's table). The intercept emits the state-machine invocation shape:
       ```llvm
       %kara.state = call ptr @__kara_state_new_<name>()
       br label %kara.poll_loop
     kara.poll_loop:
       %kara.poll_result = call i8 @__kara_poll_<name>(ptr %kara.state, ptr null)
       %kara.is_pending = icmp eq i8 %kara.poll_result, 0
       br i1 %kara.is_pending, label %kara.poll_loop, label %kara.poll_done
     kara.poll_done:
       call void @free(ptr %kara.state)
       ; subsequent IR continues here
       ```
       The synchronous spin-loop is a v1 placeholder — slice 8e+ replaces it with a yield to the line-17 scheduler dispatcher so that a Pending observation parks the parent task until the event loop signals readiness. v1 args are silently dropped (test programs use no-arg shapes); a follow-on slice threads call-args through state-struct captured-local fields at constructor invocation time. The intercept fires only when the callee resolves to an `Identifier(name)` or single-segment `Path` whose name is in `state_machine_state_constructors` — generic / closure / `Type.assoc` shapes route through their existing paths, and the slice-4 presence rule guarantees network-boundary fns aren't generic at v1. Cancel arg is `ptr null` for now (line-17 slice 4's process-global cancel placeholder); future slice routes the dispatcher's cancel flag through here for cooperative cancellation propagation. Return value is `i64 0` — v1 network-boundary fns return unit; non-unit returns land via state-struct terminal field in a later slice. LLVM auto-disambiguates `kara.poll_loop` / `kara.poll_done` labels across multiple call sites in the same caller (appends `1`, `2`, … suffixes). **5 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: a caller (`main`) calling a network-boundary `driver()` emits the state-constructor call (not the direct `call void @driver()`); the intercept emits `kara.poll_loop:` block with the poll-fn call carrying state-ptr + null cancel and the `icmp eq i8 ..., 0` Pending compare; the `kara.poll_done:` block calls `@free` on the state struct; pure-helper calls in the same caller still lower to direct calls (intercept fires only for network-boundary callees); two call sites in the same caller produce two distinct ctor invocations + at least two poll-loop label occurrences. All 21 prior poll-fn / state-constructor tests stay green — slice 8d only adds caller-side IR, doesn't change the state-machine helpers themselves. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 43 test binaries (524 codegen E2E, 1078 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 5 new + 519 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (slice-8d intercept block before module symbol lookup, ~80 lines: state-constructor call + loop/done block creation + poll-fn invoke + Pending compare + free), `tests/codegen.rs` (5 new tests). **The end-to-end state-machine ABI is now wired:** caller invokes constructor → state machine loops through tag transitions via poll-fn → terminal arm returns Ready → caller frees state struct. The user code inside each state arm is still a stub (slice 7's switch + slice 8a's reload + slice 8b's tag-store, no actual user statements between), and the loop is synchronous. **Unblocks** slice 8e — replace the synchronous spin-loop with a runtime-scheduler yield on Pending observation so the parent task parks instead of busy-waiting, integrating with the line-17 dispatcher + event loop for cooperative cancellation and event-loop-driven resumption.

[x] **Slice 8e — cooperative yield on Pending shipped 2026-05-18.** Replaces slice 8d's busy-spin Pending-branch-to-loop with a third block that calls `sched_yield` before re-entering the poll loop. New `Codegen.sched_yield_fn: FunctionValue<'ctx>` field declared at module-build time alongside malloc / free / memcmp: `let sched_yield_type = i32_type.fn_type(&[], false); let sched_yield_fn = module.add_function("sched_yield", sched_yield_type, Some(Linkage::External));`. The intercept restructure splits the Pending path:
       ```llvm
       kara.poll_loop:
         %kara.poll_result = call i8 @__kara_poll_<name>(ptr %kara.state, ptr null)
         %kara.is_pending = icmp eq i8 %kara.poll_result, 0
         br i1 %kara.is_pending, label %kara.poll_yield, label %kara.poll_done
       kara.poll_yield:
         %kara.yield_result = call i32 @sched_yield()
         br label %kara.poll_loop
       kara.poll_done:
         call void @free(ptr %kara.state)
         ; subsequent IR continues here
       ```
       The cooperative yield matters because without it the parent thread busy-spins on poll-fn invocations, starving the line-17 dispatcher thread (and any other tasks on the same scheduler) of cycles to process event-loop readiness wakeups. With the yield, the OS scheduler gives other threads a quantum on every Pending observation — the dispatcher can run its `take_wakeups` drain, the event-loop poll can process fd readiness, and parked tasks can be resumed in their own time. The `sched_yield` return value (`i32` non-zero on catastrophic OS failure) is discarded — the linked libc on Linux / macOS always returns 0 in practice, and the not-recoverable failure path isn't actionable from the IR. Windows IOCP support (line 17 sub-item 7) will need a `SwitchToThread` analog; v1 targets Linux / macOS where sched_yield is available. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `kara.poll_yield:` block appears in the caller's IR; module declares `declare i32 @sched_yield()` extern AND the yield block invokes it via `call i32 @sched_yield()`; the Pending branch routes through `kara.poll_yield` (literal `br i1 %kara.is_pending, label %kara.poll_yield, label %kara.poll_done`); the yield block branches back to `kara.poll_loop`. All 5 slice-8d tests stay green — the new yield block is additive; the slice-8d Pending-loopback test was checking presence of the loop label, not the branch target. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 45 test binaries (528 codegen E2E, 1078 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 4 new + 524 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (new `sched_yield_fn` field + extern declaration in `Codegen::new` alongside malloc / free / memcmp + struct init wiring), `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (slice-8e restructure of the intercept block: split Pending branch into `kara.poll_yield` indirection, ~15 added lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** future slices — the cooperative yield gives the runtime dispatcher real cycles to drive parked tasks. Next sub-slices under line 26: thread call-args through state-struct captured-local fields at constructor invocation time; emit user-code statements between yield-points in each state arm (the body-splitting work deferred from earlier sub-slice discussions); error-path lowering integration through `?`; generics-in-yielding-function support.
  13. [x] **Slice 8f — caller-side arg-storing into state struct shipped 2026-05-18.** Threads call args into the state struct's captured-local fields ahead of the first poll-fn invocation. Without this, slice 8d's intercept silently dropped args — `driver(my_vec)` invoked the constructor + poll loop but `my_vec` never reached the callee. Slice 8f closes the loop: in the compile_call intercept, after the `__kara_state_new_<name>()` call, iterate `args[]` with index `i`, compile each arg expression via the existing `compile_expr` machinery, GEP into state struct field `i+1` (skipping the i32 tag at field 0), and store the compiled value. The mapping is direct because slice 4's layout puts parameters first in field order: layout slot `i` ↔ state struct field `i+1` ↔ call arg `i`. Slice-4 let-binding slots (positions K..N for the K-param case) stay uninitialized at construction — they're populated by the state-machine transform itself when execution reaches the let-site (future slice). The arg-store sites appear textually before the `br label %kara.poll_loop` entry branch, guaranteeing args are in place by the time the first poll-fn invocation runs. The IR shape after slice 8f for `fn driver(n: i64)` called via `main() { driver(42); }`:
       ```llvm
       %kara.state = call ptr @__kara_state_new_driver()
       %kara.arg0.field_ptr = getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.driver, ptr %kara.state, i32 0, i32 1
       store i64 42, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr
       br label %kara.poll_loop
       ```
       v1 scope restrictions: free-function calls only (method-call intercept lands alongside the method-call intercept itself in a follow-on slice); owned-arg semantics — `ref` / `mut ref` flagging through the state struct is deferred to the slice that handles cross-yield-point borrows; non-`Vec` complex types are passed as opaque LLVM values via the standard `compile_expr` + `build_store` pair, matching the slice-5 state struct's field types. **5 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: single-arg primitive `driver(42)` GEPs into field 1 and stores `i64 42`; two-arg `driver(1, 2)` GEPs into fields 1 + 2 and stores both literals; no-arg call emits no `kara.argN.field_ptr` sites; identifier arg `driver(x)` where `x: i64` is let-bound stores a loaded SSA value (not a literal) into field 1; arg-store sites appear textually before the `br label %kara.poll_loop` entry branch. All 9 prior caller-side / slice-8e tests stay green — slice 8f only adds IR between the constructor call and the poll-loop entry. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 45 test binaries (533 codegen E2E, ... all green; 5 new + 528 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (slice-8f arg-store loop in the intercept block, ~20 lines: state struct lookup + per-arg compile + GEP + store), `tests/codegen.rs` (5 new tests). **Unblocks** the user-code body-splitting work (the next major slice under line 26) — with args reachable in the state struct from arm 0 onward, the per-arm body lowering can reference the slice-8a reloaded slots as the canonical variable-lookup backing store for both parameters and let-bindings.

[x] **Slice 8g — method-call network-boundary intercept shipped 2026-05-18.** Mirrors slice 8d's free-function intercept (`compile_call`) for the `obj.method(args)` shape in `compile_method_call`. Hook fires ahead of every other method-call dispatch path (Option/Result `unwrap`-style shortcuts, indexed-receiver, field-receiver, entry-chain, clone-on-collection) so a network-boundary method's resolved `Type.method` key is never lost to a receiver-shape shortcut emitting an inappropriate direct call. The hook reads the slice-2-of-line-26 `method_callee_types` side-table for the resolved `Type.method` key and, when that key is in `state_machine_state_constructors`, emits the full state-machine invocation shape: compile receiver via `compile_expr`; call `__kara_state_new_<Type.method>()`; store the receiver SSA value into state struct field 1 (`self` is at slice 4's layout position 0, mapping to field 1 after the i32 tag at field 0); store each method arg into fields 2..=K via the existing slice-8f-style per-arg compile + GEP + store loop; emit the slice-8e poll loop with cooperative `sched_yield` on Pending; `free` the state struct on done. The IR shape after slice 8g for `impl Hub { fn run(self, n: i64) { ... } }` called via `main() { h.run(42); }`:
       ```llvm
       %recv = ...
       %kara.state = call ptr @__kara_state_new_Hub.run()
       %kara.self.field_ptr = getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.Hub.run, ptr %kara.state, i32 0, i32 1
       store %Hub %recv, ptr %kara.self.field_ptr
       %kara.arg0.field_ptr = getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.Hub.run, ptr %kara.state, i32 0, i32 2
       store i64 42, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr
       br label %kara.poll_loop
       ; ... slice-8d/8e poll-loop + yield + done blocks ...
       ```
       v1 scope: regular structs only — `shared struct` receivers are rejected by line 31 slice 1 (`E_RAII_ACROSS_YIELD`) before the codegen sees them; line 31 slice 2's `CancelSafe` marker will eventually allow user-extensible opt-in. Owned-receiver semantics — `ref self` / `mut ref self` receivers through the state struct are deferred to the same slice that adds ref-passing through arg-storing. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: method intercept emits state constructor + poll-loop block + poll-fn invocation for `h.run()` on a `struct Hub`; receiver stores into state struct field 1 via `%kara.self.field_ptr`; non-network methods (`h.pure_count()`) still use direct dispatch (`@__kara_state_new_Hub.pure_count` absent); multi-arg method `h.run(42)` stores receiver into field 1 + arg into field 2. All 15 prior caller-side / slice-8f tests stay green — slice 8g is purely additive for method-call paths. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (537 codegen E2E, ... all green; 4 new + 533 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (slice-8g intercept block at the top of `compile_method_call` after the cancel-check, ~110 lines: state-machine helper lookups + receiver compile + ctor call + receiver-store into field 1 + per-arg compile/GEP/store loop into fields 2..=K + poll loop + cooperative yield + done + free), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **End-to-end state-machine ABI now spans both free-function and method-call dispatch surfaces.** Next sub-slices under line 26: user-code body-splitting between yields (the big remaining piece); non-unit return values through the state-struct terminal field; error-path lowering through `?`; generics-in-yielding-function support; ref-passing for both arg-storing and method receivers.
  15. [x] **Slice 8h — body-splitting for void calls between yields shipped 2026-05-18.** First cut of the user-code lowering between yield points in each state arm. The poll-fn body now walks the user function's body AST, partitions statements at yield-point spans (via the slice-2-of-line-26 `yield_points` table), and emits `call void @<name>()` for each non-yield arg-less `Call(Identifier)` statement with a void-returning callee in the corresponding state arm. The call emission lands between the slice-8a reload prologue and the slice-8b tag-store / Ready return, so a `fn driver() { helper(); fetch(); }` now produces a `__kara_poll_driver` whose state_0 body is: reload prologue → `call void @helper()` → tag-store(1) → Pending return; state_1 (terminal): reload prologue → Ready return. v1 scope restrictions: only `Stmt::Expr(Call(Identifier(name), []))` shapes emit; method calls, args-bearing free-fn calls, let bindings, control flow (`if`/`while`/`match`/`for`), and non-void returns are silently skipped — the supported-statement set grows in subsequent slices as receiver-storing / arg-passing / typed-return / control-flow handling lands. **Compilation-order shift required for slice 8h to work:** the `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` call moved from its early position (alongside slice 5's `emit_state_struct_types`, line ~1688) to just before user body compilation (line ~1866, after `declare_function` for all user free fns and impl methods + `emit_provider_vtables` + `pre_emit_hot_swap_table`). The move was necessary because the poll-fn body emission now calls `self.module.get_function(callee_name)` to look up the LLVM `FunctionValue` for non-yield user-code callees — that symbol must be declared first. `emit_state_machine_state_constructors` stayed at the early position because it only references `state_struct_types` + `malloc` (both available early), not user fns. New module-level `find_function_ast` helper in `declarations.rs` resolves an `fn_key` (`"name"` for free fns, `"Type.method"` for impl methods) to its `&Function` AST node by scanning `program.items`. The walker categorises each top-level `Stmt::Expr(ExprKind::Call { callee, args })`: if `expr.span` matches the next pending `yield_points[fn_key][cur_arm].span` (yield_points entries are recorded in source order by slice 2's walker), the statement is a yield-point that advances `cur_arm += 1` without queuing; otherwise, if it's an arg-less bare-identifier call, queue the name into `per_arm_calls[cur_arm]`. Inside the per-arm loop, after the reload prologue, iterate the queued names and emit `call void @<name>()` for each callee that's declared with a void return type — non-void returns are skipped at v1 (a non-void call without a named SSA binding would produce malformed IR, and threading return values through the state struct's terminal field is a separate slice). **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: pre-yield `helper()` call appears in state_0 before the tag-store; post-yield `helper()` call appears in the terminal arm before `ret i8 1`; multi-yield case `{ a(); fetch(); b(); fetch(); c(); }` emits a/b/c in state_0/state_1/state_2 in the right order; trivial yield-only body (`fn driver() { fetch(); }`) emits no extra calls. All 17 prior poll-fn tests stay green — the move doesn't change the emission shape, and slice 8h's body-splitting only ADDS calls between the existing reload and tag-store / Ready return. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 47 test binaries (543 codegen E2E, ... all green; 4 new + 539 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (move `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` call from line ~1688 to ~1866), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (slice-8h body-splitting block in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` + new `find_function_ast` module-level helper, ~90 lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the next slice expansion: handling method-call statements between yields (mirrors slice 8h's free-function path but with receiver compilation); handling args-bearing calls (compile args + emit non-void calls); handling let-bindings (introduce local allocas in the appropriate state arm with proper scope tracking); handling control flow (`if` / `while` / `for` need per-arm-internal CFG construction); non-unit returns (terminal arm writes return value into a state-struct terminal field, caller-side loads after Ready observation).
  16. [x] **Slice 8i — non-unit return value through state struct terminal field shipped 2026-05-18.** Adds v1 support for network-boundary functions returning `i64`. Each affected fn's state struct gains a terminal `i64` field appended after the captured-local fields; the poll-fn's terminal arm writes a placeholder `i64 0` into that field before returning Ready; caller-side intercepts (free-function + method-call) load the terminal field after the `kara.poll_done` block and use that value as the call's return value, replacing the unconditional `i64 0` from earlier slices. New `Codegen.state_machine_return_types: HashMap<String, BasicTypeEnum<'ctx>>` side-table maps each fn_key whose return type matches the v1 supported set (`i64` only) to its LLVM type — populated by `emit_state_struct_types` (slice 5) while walking the user `Function` AST via the slice-8h `find_function_ast` helper. New module-level `is_i64_return_type` helper in `declarations.rs` matches `TypeKind::Path` whose single segment is `"i64"`. The terminal field's index in the state struct is `1 + N` (after the i32 tag at 0 and the N captured-local fields), so terminal arm and caller-side intercepts both compute `state_struct.count_fields() - 1` to find it. The load-before-free ordering on the caller side is load-critical: GEP-then-load runs in the `kara.poll_done` block, then `@free` releases the heap allocation — reversing the order would dereference freed memory. **Body-splitting handoff:** the terminal arm stores a constant `i64 0` placeholder rather than the user's actual final-expression value because the body-splitting work for non-trivial final exprs (anything beyond a literal — identifier references, binary ops, function calls returning values) requires variables-scope plumbing that the line-26 sub-slices haven't reached. The end-to-end shape is wired and tested with the placeholder; a follow-on slice replaces the placeholder with the actual return-expression value once body-splitting supports expressions that reach the function's final position. v1 scope: `i64` returns only; `i32` / `u32` / `bool` / `f64` / Vec / String / shared structs / user structs etc. stay on the unit-return path until follow-on slices widen the supported set. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: state struct for `fn driver() -> i64 with sends(Network) ...` shape is `{ i32, i64 }` (tag + terminal); poll-fn terminal arm stores `i64 0` into `%kara.return.field_ptr` before `ret i8 1`; caller-side intercept loads the terminal field via the named GEP before `@free`, with load-before-free ordering preserved; unit-returning callees keep existing behavior (no terminal field in state struct, no caller-side load). All 45 prior caller-side / poll-fn / state-constructor / body-splitting / method-intercept tests stay green. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen.rs` (new `state_machine_return_types` field + `HashMap::new()` init), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `is_i64_return_type` helper + slice-8i terminal-field append in `emit_state_struct_types` + terminal-arm placeholder store in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`), `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (slice-8d intercept loads terminal field before `@free`), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (slice-8g intercept mirror), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the user-level final-expression body-splitting: once a future slice handles expression statements + variable scope inside arm bodies, the terminal arm's placeholder `i64 0` becomes the user's actual final-expression value (tracked as slice 8ah). Also unblocks widening the supported return-type set (i32/bool/Vec/String/structs) — the slice-5/8b/8d/8g touch points are already structured for type-keyed dispatch through `state_machine_return_types` (tracked as slice 8ai).

[x] **Slice 8j — method-call body-splitting between yields shipped 2026-05-18.**  Extends slice 8h's free-function body-splitting (`Stmt::Expr(Call(Identifier, []))`) to also cover `Stmt::Expr(MethodCall { object, args: [], .. })` where the receiver is a captured layout-field (`SelfValue` → field `"self"` for impl methods, or `Identifier(name)` where `name` resolves to a slice-4 layout field) and the resolved `Type.method` LLVM function returns void. Per-arm queueing now uses a `BodySplitStmt` enum with two variants (`FreeFnCall(name)` for slice 8h shape, `MethodCall { receiver_field, callee_key }` for slice 8j) so a single walker handles both. Resolution of the `Type.method` callee key reads from `program.method_callee_types[(span.offset, span.length)]` — the same typechecker side-table the slice-2 yield-point walker uses, populated during `infer_method_call`. Emission: after the slice-8a reload prologue (which now also stashes each captured-local's `(slot_ty, slot_ptr)` into a per-arm `HashMap<String, (BasicTypeEnum, PointerValue)>` keyed by field name), iterate the arm's `BodySplitStmt` queue — for `MethodCall { receiver_field, callee_key }`, look up the slot pair, inspect the resolved method's first-param LLVM type to choose receiver ABI (pointer-typed → pass `slot_ptr` directly for `ref self` / `mut ref self`; value-typed → `build_load(slot_ty, slot_ptr)` for owned `self`), and `build_call(method_fn, &[recv_arg], "")`. The first-param ABI dispatch mirrors `compile_method_call`'s existing user-side discipline (`src/codegen/method_call.rs:543-548`), keeping the slice 8j path consistent with how methods are called everywhere else in the codegen. **v1 scope restrictions (carried forward from slice 8h):** receiver must be `SelfValue` or a captured-layout `Identifier`; args list must be empty; method must return void; non-yield method calls only (yield-point method calls advance the arm via the existing slice-8h span comparison). Method calls with non-captured receivers (chained `m.first().second()`, field-access receivers `obj.inner.method()`, literal receivers, etc.) are silently skipped at v1 — the body-splitting walker's coverage grows incrementally as receiver shapes get threaded through. **Tests use free-fn drivers with let-bound identifier receivers (`fn driver() { let h = Hub { count: 0 }; h.helper(); fetch(); }`) rather than impl-method bodies with `self.method()`,** because the codegen's user-side `compile_method_call` doesn't yet resolve `SelfValue` receivers via `inferred_receiver_type` (an existing limitation that's orthogonal to slice 8j — the body-splitting walker handles `SelfValue` correctly; the test source just can't trigger that path without first fixing user-side self-method dispatch). **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: pre-yield `h.helper()` emits `call void @Hub.helper(...)` in state_0 before the tag-store to state_1; post-yield `h.helper()` emits in the terminal arm before the Ready return; multi-yield case `let h = ...; h.a(); fetch(); h.b(); fetch(); h.c();` emits a/b/c in state_0/state_1/state_2 in the right order; pins that the receiver argument is the slice-8a `%h.slot` pointer (regression pin that the slot mechanic actually wires through). [x] **Slice 8k — args-bearing free-fn body-splitting between yields shipped 2026-05-18.** Extends slice 8h's free-function body-splitting (`Stmt::Expr(Call(Identifier, []))`) to accept zero-or-more args per call, where each arg is in a recognised v1 shape (`ExprKind::Integer(n, _)` → emitted as `i64` const; `ExprKind::Identifier(name)` where `name` resolves to a slice-4 layout field → loaded from the slice-8a reload-prologue slot). Any unrecognised arg shape (binary expressions, method-call args, field accesses, struct literals, etc.) causes the WHOLE call to be silently skipped — same conservative "non-emittable shape dropped" rule slice 8h established, mirrored at arg granularity. `BodySplitStmt::FreeFnCall` widened from `(String)` to `{ name: String, args: Vec<BodyArg> }`; new sibling enum `BodyArg { IntLit(i64), Slot(String) }` captures the recognised shapes; new module-level `recognize_body_arg(expr, layout_field_names) -> Option<BodyArg>` runs at walker time per arg. Per-arm emission compiles each `BodyArg` into a `BasicMetadataValueEnum`: `IntLit(v)` → `context.i64_type().const_int(v as u64, true)`; `Slot(name)` → looks up `slot_map[name]` (the per-arm `(slot_ty, slot_ptr)` map from slice 8j), emits `build_load(slot_ty, slot_ptr, "<name>.arg")` to pass the slot's stored value by value; vector is then handed to `build_call(callee_fn, &compiled, "")`. Defensive: if `slot_map` lookup fails for a `Slot(name)` arg despite the walker having pre-checked `layout_field_names`, the call is skipped via an `arg_ok = false` continue — guards against any future divergence between the walker's pre-classification and the emission-time slot map. **v1 type lowering is conservative `i64` for integer literals** (matches the state-struct primitive fallback in slice 5); narrower / signed-unsigned distinctions stay deferred until the typechecker's recorded callee param type starts flowing into the walker — a fine extension because most user network-boundary calls in v1 carry `i64` / `String` / `Vec[T]` shapes whose ABI is uniform at the slot level. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: integer literal arg `take(42)` emits `call void @take(i64 42)` before the state_0 tag-store; identifier arg `take(n)` (where `n` is a captured param) emits `load i64, ptr %n.slot` then `call void @take(i64 %n.arg)`; multi-arg `mix(n, 7)` mixes slot-loaded + literal in source order (`call void @mix(i64 %n.arg, i64 7)`); unrecognised arg `take(n + 1)` (binary op) is silently dropped — no `call void @take` in the poll-fn. All 21 prior poll-fn / slice-8h void-call / slice-8j method-call tests stay green; the `FreeFnCall { name, args: vec![] }` shape produced by an arg-less call still emits `call void @<name>()` exactly as slice 8h tests expect. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodyArg` enum + `recognize_body_arg` helper + widened `BodySplitStmt::FreeFnCall` + per-arm emission arg-compile loop, ~50 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the next slice expansions: args-bearing method calls between yields (mirror of slice 8j with the slice-8k arg-compile loop applied to `MethodCall.args`); typed-aware arg lowering (consume the typechecker's recorded param types so `i32` / `u32` / `bool` / pointer-typed args don't silently lower to `i64`); let-bindings introducing arm-local allocas (the slot map is already arm-scoped, so a let inside an arm just needs to register its alloca into the same map under the binding name).
  19. [x] **Slice 8l — args-bearing method-call body-splitting between yields shipped 2026-05-18.** Mirrors slice 8k's `BodyArg`-driven arg-compile loop onto `BodySplitStmt::MethodCall`. The MethodCall variant widens from `{ receiver_field, callee_key }` to `{ receiver_field, callee_key, args: Vec<BodyArg> }`; the walker drops slice 8j's `args.is_empty()` guard and runs `recognize_body_arg` on every arg, dropping the whole MethodCall if any arg falls outside the recognised set (same conservative skip rule as slice 8k for free-fn calls). The receiver claims call position 0; method args follow at positions 1..=N in source order. [x] **Slice 8m — arm-local let-bindings inside arm bodies shipped 2026-05-18.** First slice that adds first-class scope INSIDE per-arm emission (slices 8h-8l only handled statement-level call shapes; everything else was silently dropped). New `BodySplitStmt::Let { name, rhs: BodyArg }` variant. Walker arm: classify `StmtKind::Let { value, pattern, .. }` where `pattern.kind == PatternKind::Binding(name)` and `recognize_body_arg(value, &current_names)` returns `Some(rhs)`. Non-binding patterns (destructuring, struct patterns, etc.) and unrecognised RHS shapes are silently skipped — same conservative rule the call-classification arms established. **New `current_names: HashSet<String>` tracks visible bindings dynamically** through the walker: starts at `layout_names` (slice-4 captured-locals union), grows as let-statements introduce arm-local bindings, RESETS to `layout_names` at every yield boundary. The reset is correct because slice-8a's reload prologue reconstitutes all captured-locals at the start of every arm — but arm-local lets from prior arms aren't reflected in any reload (no state-struct field), so they must drop. `recognize_body_arg`'s signature widens from `&HashSet<&str>` to `&HashSet<String>` so the same call shape works for both static (layout-derived) and dynamic (let-extended) name sets. Per-arm emission: when `BodySplitStmt::Let { name, rhs }` is processed, alloca a fresh `i64` slot named `<name>.slot`, compute the RHS value (`IntLit(v)` → `i64.const_int(v)`; `Slot(src)` → `build_load(src_ty, src_ptr, "<src>.let_rhs")`), store the value into the slot, and `slot_map.insert(name, (i64.into(), slot))` so subsequent calls/lets in the same arm can reference the binding. **v1 type lowering: every let-binding slot is `i64`** — matches the state-struct primitive fallback, but means struct/Vec/String let-bindings can't flow through slice 8m yet (struct-literal RHS isn't in `BodyArg` recognised set, so the let is dropped; downstream method-call receivers on the would-be binding silently fall through). Cross-yield let preservation also stays deferred: a let introduced in arm 0 that's referenced in arm 1 would need state-struct write-back before the yield, which is a follow-on slice. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: terminal-arm `let x = 42; take(x);` emits `%x.slot = alloca i64`, `store i64 42, ptr %x.slot`, and `call void @take(i64 %x.arg)` in source order; identifier-RHS `let y = n;` loads `n` from its captured-local slot via `%n.let_rhs`, stores into `%y.slot`, and subsequent `take(y)` uses the new slot; struct-literal RHS (`let h = Hub { count: 0 }`) is silently dropped, and the downstream `h.helper()` also drops because `h` isn't in the slot map (regression pin for the v1 limitation); let-chains `let a = 7; let b = a; take(b);` flow through both lets, with `b.slot` carrying `a`'s loaded value. All 20 prior body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8m is purely additive (a new BodySplitStmt variant + a new walker arm + a new emission arm), the existing FreeFnCall / MethodCall paths are unchanged. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodySplitStmt::Let` variant + `current_names: HashSet<String>` tracking + walker `Let` arm + reset-on-yield + emission `Let` arm + widened `recognize_body_arg` signature, ~80 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the next slice expansions: cross-yield let-preservation (write-back to state-struct field before the yield when the let-binding is in slice-4's capture set; the slot map + slot pointer are already arm-scoped); typed-aware let lowering (consume the typechecker's recorded binding type so non-i64 lets actually have the right LLVM slot type); struct-literal / call-result RHS shapes (extend `BodyArg` with `StructLit` / `CallResult` variants for richer RHS coverage); control flow inside arms (`if` / `while` / `for` would build per-arm CFGs but inherit the same slot map for captured-local reads inside branch bodies).

[x] **Slice 8n — cross-yield captured-local writeback before each yield shipped 2026-05-18.** Closes the slice-8m correctness gap: an arm-local `let x = ...` that shadows a captured-local slot pointer in `slot_map` now actually survives across yields. Before each non-terminal arm's tag-store + Pending return, the poll-fn writes each captured-local's CURRENT slot value (which may be the slice-8a reload's original load, OR a slice-8m let-shadowed value) back into the corresponding state-struct field. Slice 8a's reload prologue in the next arm then reads the post-arm-body value rather than the stale field. **Where:** the writeback block lands inside the `if arm_idx < yield_count` branch of `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`, ahead of the slice-8b tag-store. Walks `layout.fields` (the slice-4 capture set) in order; for each field with name `field.name`, looks up `slot_map[&field.name]` (which is guaranteed to be `Some(_)` because slice-8a populated it during reload prologue, but the lookup uses `let-else continue` defensively against future divergence). `build_load(slot_ty, slot_ptr, "<name>.writeback")` reads the slot; `build_struct_gep` into field `field_idx + 1` (the same "skip i32 tag at 0" offset slice 8a uses); `build_store` writes the value back. SSA names: `<name>.writeback` for the load result and `<name>.writeback_field_ptr` for the GEP — LLVM auto-suffixes for repeat writeback sites across multi-yield arms (e.g. `%n.writeback4`), so tests that count writeback sites use the named-GEP substring rather than exact SSA names. **Terminal arm intentionally skips writeback** — it returns Ready and the caller's `@free` releases the state struct immediately after; persisting state into about-to-be-freed memory would be wasted work. **For captured locals untouched inside the arm body**, the writeback loads the slice-8a reload's stored value and stores the SAME bytes back into the same field — a value-equivalent no-op that LLVM's store-after-load redundant-store elimination optimizes away. The IR overhead is minimal (3 instructions per captured local per non-terminal arm), well worth the simplification of NOT having to track which slot_map entries were modified by slice 8m. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: writeback load + GEP + store appears in state_0 with `%n.writeback` / `%n.writeback_field_ptr` and precedes the tag-store; writeback skipped in terminal arm (single yield → exactly one writeback occurrence); slice-8m let-shadowed local (`let n = 99; fetch();`) has the let-store followed by writeback that loads from the shadowed slot — the runtime value 99 lands in the state-struct field, not the original `n` param; multi-yield case (two yields → two non-terminal arms) emits exactly two writeback sites (counted via the named-GEP `writeback_field_ptr` substring divided by 2 because LLVM emits the name in both the GEP-define and the store-use lines). All 20 prior body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8n adds IR ahead of the tag-store but doesn't remove or reorder any existing shape. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (slice-8n writeback block inside the non-terminal arm branch, ~35 lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the broader cross-yield correctness story: slice-8m lets that participate in slice-4's capture set (introduced before the last yield) now survive each suspension boundary; subsequent slices that mutate captured locals via `=` / `+=` / method calls will hook the same writeback path. The writeback also creates a natural integration point for the future "typed-aware lowering" slice — when a let's LLVM type stops being i64-conservative, the writeback already loads/stores via `slot_ty` from the slot map, so widening flows through with no IR-shape changes here.

[x] **Slice 8o — terminal-arm final-expression value through state-struct terminal field shipped 2026-05-18.** Replaces slice 8i's `i64 0` placeholder with the user's actual final-expression value when the trailing expression on the function body block is in the recognised `BodyArg` set. Body grammar: each `Block` carries `stmts: Vec<Stmt>` plus an optional `final_expr: Option<Box<Expr>>` (the trailing-expression-without-semicolon position). The walker, after processing all statements in source order, inspects `fn_ast.body.final_expr` via `recognize_body_arg(final_expr, &current_names)` — using the TERMINAL arm's `current_names` state (post-yield-reset, plus any terminal-arm-local let bindings introduced before the final expression), so a `let r = X; r` final shape sees `r` in scope. The recognised value lands in a new walker-scoped `terminal_return: Option<BodyArg>` field; terminal-arm emission consults it before falling back to slice 8i's `i64 0`. Emission: `IntLit(v)` → `i64.const_int(v)` stored into the terminal field; `Slot(name)` → `build_load(slot_ty, slot_ptr, "<name>.return")` from `slot_map`, then `store` into the terminal field. **Slice 8m + 8n compose cleanly:** a `let r = computed_value; r` terminal pattern (slice 8m emits the let-alloca + store, slice 8n is a no-op in the terminal arm) reads the let-stored value via slot map and stores into the terminal field — the end-to-end return path works for the entire integer-let-then-return shape. **v1 scope (carried forward from slice 8k):** only integer-literal and captured-local-identifier final exprs lower; binary operations, calls, struct literals, method-call results, etc. fall back to the slice-8i `i64 0` placeholder. Wider final-expr shapes will arrive when typed-aware lowering threads expression evaluation through the body-splitting walker. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: integer-literal final `fn driver() -> i64 ... { fetch(); 42 }` emits `store i64 42, ptr %kara.return.field_ptr`; captured-local final `fn driver(n: i64) -> i64 ... { fetch(); n }` loads `%n.return = load i64, ptr %n.slot` then stores it; arm-local let final `let r = 99; r` loads `%r.return` (the slice-8m let-alloca's stored value); unrecognised final `n + 1` (binary op) falls back to `store i64 0, ptr %kara.return.field_ptr`. The four existing slice-8i tests stay green — the placeholder-fallback path is preserved verbatim for unrecognised final-expr shapes, and the existing `0`-literal test program emits `store i64 0` because `0` is now recognised as `IntLit(0)` (value-equivalent to the old placeholder). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `terminal_return: Option<BodyArg>` walker field + final-expr classification at end of walker + terminal-arm emission dispatch on `terminal_return`, ~40 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the final remaining v1 functional gap on line 26: typed-aware lowering for primitive let-bindings, args, and final-expressions (currently every i64-sized slot is i64-typed; widening to i32 / u32 / bool / f64 would require slot-type lookup against `pattern_binding_types` + per-slot LLVM-type-aware load/store/const calls — the `slot_ty` plumbing through `slot_map` and `terminal_return` is already there waiting). After typed-aware lowering, the remaining line-26 surface is control flow inside arms (if/while/for with possibly-nested yields), error-path lowering through `?` (state-struct destructor invocation), and generics-in-yielding-function support.
  23. [x] **Slice 8p — assignment statements (`name = value`) inside arm bodies shipped 2026-05-18.** Pairs with slice 8m + 8n to make captured locals genuinely mutable across yields. New `BodySplitStmt::Assign { name, value: BodyArg }` variant. Walker arm: classify `StmtKind::Assign { target, value }` where `target.kind == ExprKind::Identifier(name)`, `current_names.contains(name)`, and `recognize_body_arg(value, &current_names)` returns `Some(body_value)`. Non-identifier targets (`obj.field = x`, `arr[i] = x`, etc.) and unrecognised RHS shapes silently drop — same conservative rule the call / let arms established. Per-arm emission: look up the binding's slot in `slot_map` (which slice 8a pre-populated for captured locals AND slice 8m extends with arm-local lets), compute the new value via the same `BodyArg`-driven dispatch as let RHS (`IntLit(v)` → `i64.const_int(v)`; `Slot(src)` → `build_load(src_ty, src_ptr, "<src>.assign_rhs")`), and `build_store` into the existing slot — does NOT alloca. The pre-existing slot is the key: the assignment's LHS already has memory backing from either slice 8a (param/captured-local-reload) or slice 8m (let-alloca), so slice 8p just overwrites the value. **Composition with slice 8n is what makes this load-bearing for cross-yield mutation:** an assignment to a captured local in a non-terminal arm leaves the new value in the slot; slice 8n's pre-yield writeback then transfers the slot's post-arm value to the state-struct field; arm K+1's reload prologue reads the updated value. Without slice 8n, the assignment would be invisible across the yield. The integration test for this — `fn driver(n: i64) with sends(Network) { n = 99; fetch(); ... }` — verifies the assignment-then-writeback sequence in IR. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: literal-to-captured assignment (`n = 99`) stores into existing `n.slot`, and slice 8n's `%n.writeback` follows in source order; captured-to-captured assignment (`b = a`) emits `%a.assign_rhs = load i64, ptr %a.slot` then `store i64 %a.assign_rhs, ptr %b.slot`; terminal-arm assignment (no following yield, no writeback) updates the slot which the slice-8o `%n.return` final-expression read then sees; field-assign target (`h.count = 7`) silently drops — non-identifier target rule. All 24 prior body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8p is purely additive (new BodySplitStmt variant + walker arm + emission arm), no existing path changes. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodySplitStmt::Assign` variant + walker `Assign` arm + emission `Assign` arm, ~55 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the broader "mutable state across yields" story: compound-assign (`+=` / `-=` / `*=` ...) maps directly to assign-after-binop and can land in a follow-on slice once `BodyArg` widens to recognise binary expressions; field-assign / index-assign require the walker to thread receiver/index resolution, which sits alongside the future struct-literal / call-result `BodyArg` extensions; typed-aware lowering is now the most strategically valuable next slice because all four mutation paths (let-init, let-shadow, assign, writeback) currently hardcode i64 — widening to consult `pattern_binding_types` and `state_struct_layouts[fn_key].fields[i].type_name` unlocks bool / i32 / f64 / Vec / String mutation through the same slot-and-writeback machinery.

[x] **Slice 8q — `BodyArg::Binary` for integer arithmetic in arm bodies shipped 2026-05-18.** Widens the body-splitting walker's `BodyArg` set to accept arithmetic binary expressions (`+` / `-` / `*` / `/` / `%`) in any position the prior slices reached: let-RHS (slice 8m), assign-RHS (slice 8p), free-fn call args (slice 8k), method-call args (slice 8l), and terminal-arm final expression (slice 8o). Picks the simpler of slice 8p's two named follow-on directions — compound-assign mechanically lowers to `Assign { name, value: Binary { op, lhs: Slot(name), rhs: <recognised> } }` once parser/walker threads the `+=` surface through, so this slice lays the binary-expression foundation that the compound-assign slice then composes onto. Typed-aware lowering (the other direction) stays deferred — slice 8q remains i64-conservative throughout. **Two coupled additions in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`:** (1) new `BodyArg::Binary { op: BinaryArithOp, lhs: Box<BodyArg>, rhs: Box<BodyArg> }` variant with companion `BinaryArithOp` enum (`Add` / `Sub` / `Mul` / `Div` / `Mod`); (2) new `Codegen::materialize_body_arg(arg, slot_map, name_hint) -> Option<BasicValueEnum>` helper that handles all three `BodyArg` variants in one place and is now the single materialisation point — the five emission sites (FreeFnCall args, MethodCall args, Let RHS, Assign RHS, terminal-return) collapsed from per-site `match arg` blocks into uniform `materialize_body_arg(...)` calls, deduplicating ~80 lines of repeated IntLit + Slot handling. **Recognition path matches the lowered shape, not the surface AST:** the `karac` lowering pass (`src/lowering.rs::rewrite_binary`) rewrites every primitive `Binary { Add, n, 1 }` into `Call { callee: Path { segments: ["i64", "add"] }, args: [n, 1] }` before codegen runs, so the walker matches on the two-segment-`Path`-callee Call form (segments[0] in `{i8, i16, i32, i64, u8, u16, u32, u64, usize, isize}`; segments[1] in `{add, sub, mul, div, rem}`). Comparison (`eq` / `ne` / `lt` / `le` / `gt` / `ge`), bitwise (`bitand` / `bitor` / `bitxor` / `shl` / `shr`), and float arithmetic stay outside the recognised set — `recognize_body_arg` returns `None` for those and the walker drops the whole statement, mirroring the conservative-skip rule the prior slices established. **Materialisation lowers to LLVM int arithmetic:** `BinaryArithOp::Add` → `build_int_add`; `Sub` → `build_int_sub`; `Mul` → `build_int_mul`; `Div` → `build_int_signed_div`; `Mod` → `build_int_signed_rem`. Operands recurse through `materialize_body_arg`; the helper bails (`None`) if either operand resolves to a non-`IntValue` (defensive against future `Slot` entries whose type isn't i64) so the caller skips emission rather than emitting ill-typed IR. The `name_hint` parameter — the suffix already in use by the per-site loads (`.arg` / `.marg` / `.let_rhs` / `.assign_rhs` / `.return`) — flows through unchanged: slot loads remain named `<slot>.<suffix>` (preserves existing test patterns), binary results name as `binop<suffix>`, and LLVM auto-suffixes for nested binaries (`%binop.assign_rhs1` for the outer of a nested binop). **7 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: let-RHS binary (`let m = n + 1`) emits `%n.let_rhs` load + `%binop.let_rhs = add i64 %n.let_rhs, 1` + store into `%m.slot`; assign-RHS binary (`n = n + 1`) emits `%binop.assign_rhs` and slice-8n's writeback follows in source order; call-arg binary (`helper(n + 1)`) threads `%binop.arg` into `call void @helper(i64 %binop.arg)`; terminal-return binary (`fn driver(n: i64) -> i64 { fetch(); n + 99 }`) stores `%binop.return` into `%kara.return.field_ptr`; all-five-ops sweep pins each LLVM int-arith op string (`add i64`, `sub i64`, `mul i64`, `sdiv i64`, `srem i64`); nested binary (`a = (a + b) * 2`) pins the recursive emission with the inner add and outer mul; unrecognised-binop-skips uses a comparison (`let cmp = a == b` post-yield) to confirm `==` stays unrecognised and the walker drops the let entirely. **3 prior tests updated** — `test_body_splitting_8k_skips_unrecognised_arg_shape`, `test_body_splitting_8l_skips_method_with_unrecognised_arg`, and `test_terminal_return_8o_unrecognised_final_expr_keeps_zero_fallback` originally used `n + 1` as their "unrecognised shape" example; slice 8q now recognises that shape, so the tests switched to a user-fn call shape (`ident(n)` with `fn ident(x: i64) -> i64 { x }`) which has an `ExprKind::Identifier` callee that doesn't match the `Path` recognition rule and stays outside the recognised set. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (597 codegen, all prior 590 + 7 new). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodyArg::Binary` variant + `BinaryArithOp` enum + `recognize_body_arg` Call arm + `materialize_body_arg` helper + 5 emission sites converted to call the helper, ~130 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (7 new tests + 3 updated). **Unblocks** compound-assign (`+=` / `-=` / `*=` / `/=` / `%=`) — the parser already produces `CompoundAssign { target, op, value }`; the body-splitting walker can lower it to `Assign { name, value: Binary { op, lhs: Slot(name), rhs: <recognised> } }` and reuse slice 8p + 8q emission verbatim. Typed-aware lowering (the other slice 8p hint) remains the next strategically valuable target — all four mutation paths still hardcode i64, but `materialize_body_arg`'s defensive `IntValue`-check on `Binary` operands means the helper is already structurally ready for the widening; only the `IntLit` arm and the `slot_ty.into()` insert in the Let path need to thread the actual binding type to unlock bool / i32 / f64 / Vec / String mutation.
  25. [x] **Slice 8r — compound-assign (`+= -= *= /= %=`) in arm bodies shipped 2026-05-18.** Closes out the user-visible "mutate captured locals across yields" surface for v1 integer arithmetic. The parser already produces `StmtKind::CompoundAssign { target, op, value }` end-to-end; the body-splitting walker now desugars this in-place to `Assign { name, value: Binary { op, lhs: Slot(name), rhs: <recognised> } }` so slice 8p's Assign emission + slice 8q's Binary materialisation handle the actual codegen unchanged. No new `BodySplitStmt` variant, no new emission path, no new helper — pure walker desugaring. **Walker arm** (in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`): a new `if let StmtKind::CompoundAssign { target, op, value }` branch immediately after the slice-8p `StmtKind::Assign` branch. Target restriction is identical to slice 8p (`ExprKind::Identifier(name)` already in `current_names`); non-identifier targets (`h.count += 1`, `arr[i] += 1`) silently drop. `CompoundOp` mapping picks up the same five arithmetic arms `BinaryArithOp` already lowers (`Add`/`Sub`/`Mul`/`Div`/`Mod`); the five bitwise / shift arms (`BitAnd`/`BitOr`/`BitXor`/`Shl`/`Shr`) return `None` and the walker drops the statement, mirroring slice 8q's "comparison / bitwise stay outside the recognised set" rule. RHS goes through `recognize_body_arg` like every other slice — IntLit / Slot / Binary recurse, anything else drops. **The lhs is always `BodyArg::Slot(name.clone())`** by construction: compound-assign's defining property is that the target is also the lhs of the binop, so the walker hands the binding's slot to the materialiser as the binary's left operand and the helper emits the slot load + int-arith op + store into the same slot. Composition with slice 8n's pre-yield writeback closes the cross-yield-mutation loop: `n += 1; fetch();` reaches the next arm's reload prologue with the post-op value, because the writeback loads the slot (now holding `n + 1`) and writes that into the state-struct field before the tag-store. **6 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `n += 1` desugars to `add i64 %n.assign_rhs, 1` + writeback observes the post-op value (assign_pos < writeback_pos); all-five-ops sweep pins `+= -= *= /= %=` against `add/sub/mul/sdiv/srem i64`; terminal-arm `n += 41; n` updates the slot which the slice-8o `%n.return` load then reads (no writeback because terminal); bitwise `n &= 1` silently drops (no `and i64` IR, no `%binop.assign_rhs`); field-target `h.count += 1` silently drops (non-identifier target); captured-to-captured `a += b` materialises both slot loads + an `add i64 %a.assign_rhs, %b.assign_rhs`. After typed-aware lowering, the remaining line-26 surface is control flow inside arms (if / while / for with possibly-nested yields), error-path lowering through `?` (state-struct destructor invocation on Err), and generics-in-yielding-function support.
