[~] **Slice 3 — flow-sensitive detection.** Slice 1 detects by surface-type identity (shared struct / shared enum); slice 3 detects by *binding state* at the yield point — `File` held with unflushed writes, `BufReader` with a non-empty buffer, database transaction handles before commit. Spec settled (the `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "<name>")]` attribute landed in slice 3a as the v1 declaration surface; flow-walker infrastructure is type-agnostic so each stdlib type lights up by adding the attribute to its soiling methods). Carry parent open while remaining stdlib prereqs (`BufReader[R]`) ship; sub-slices break out per stdlib type as it lands.
     1. [x] **Slice 3a — flow-sensitive infrastructure + File seeding shipped 2026-05-26.** Closes the design.md "File before fsync" pattern for the v1 `File` handle (phase-8 line 87, shipped 2026-05-26). **Attribute:** new `cancel_unsafe_until` bare-name registered in `attribute_validator::RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES`. Shape: `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "<clear>")]` on an impl method declares "calling this method on a receiver flips the receiver to a cancel-unsafe state until `<clear>` is called on the same receiver". Stdlib seeding: `File.write` in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` carries `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "flush")]` — clear method is `flush` (also `sync_all` once that ships; only `flush` is in the v1 surface). **Walker (`src/raii_check.rs`):** new `collect_cancel_unsafe_annotations` walks both user `program.items` AND every program in `crate::prelude::STDLIB_PROGRAMS` (the baked stdlib's impl blocks don't get spliced into `program.items` — `synthetic_prelude_items` clones the StructDef only, so the walker reaches into STDLIB_PROGRAMS explicitly to pick up `File.write`). Returns `HashMap<type_name, HashMap<soiling_method, clear_method>>`. **New `StateFlowWalker`** mirrors `cli::YieldPointWalker`'s structure — same scope-discipline (push on let / pattern binding, truncate on block exit), same network-yield detection via `method_callee_types` lookup, plus a per-binding-name `state: HashMap<String, BindingState>` threaded linearly through the walk. At each `MethodCall(object=Identifier(n)|SelfValue, method, ...)`, looks up `annotations[type_of(n)][method]` — if Some(clear_name), flips `state[n] = Soiled { soiling_method, soil_span, clear_method_name }`; if `state[n]` is `Soiled` and the called method matches the recorded `clear_method_name`, flips back to `Clean`. At each yield-point call site (Call or MethodCall where the resolved callee_key is in `callee_network_yield_effect`), iterates `state` and emits one `RaiiAcrossYieldError { state_violation: Some(_) }` per Soiled binding. **Diagnostic extension:** new `state_violation: Option<StateViolation>` field on `RaiiAcrossYieldError` (`StateViolation { soiling_method, soil_span, clear_method_name }`). `message()` / `help()` branch on `state_violation.is_some()`: message names the soiling method and the remediation call shape (`call `f.flush` before yielding...`); help points at the literal clear method (`call `f.flush()` before the suspension point...`) rather than the slice-1 `impl CancelSafe` fix-it. **cli.rs emission (three output paths):** plain text adds `note: soiled by `.write()` here at <span>` between the binding-declaration note and the help line when `state_violation` is `Some`; JSON `DiagEntry.extra_json` accumulates a `"state_violation":{"soiling_method":...,"clear_method_name":...,"soil_span":{...}}` block alongside the existing `"binding_span":{...}`; JSONL `diagnostic` event appends the same structured payload. **v1 implementation shape — linear forward flow, no branch merging:** every soiling call met in source-traversal order soils; every clearing call clears; irrespective of whether the call was in an `if` / `match` arm / loop body. Biased toward false positives over false negatives — a soil reachable in any walked branch propagates to the yield. Precise branch-merging is a follow-on sub-slice; the v1 surface catches the design.md flagship case and unblocks BufReader by plug-and-play attribute annotation. **Dedup contract:** one `RaiiAcrossYieldError` per `(binding, fn_key)` pair, even when the binding is held Soiled across multiple yield points — matches slice 1's per-binding emission shape (`emitted: HashSet<String>` in the walker). **8 new tests** in `tests/raii_check.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 155 slice 3a` section: `file_write_then_yield_rejected` (linear shape, asserts `state_violation.soiling_method == "write"` + `clear_method_name == "flush"`); `file_write_then_flush_then_yield_accepted` (clear closes the soil); `file_param_without_write_held_across_yield_accepted` (File alone is cancel-safe — soiling requires the call); `file_write_violation_carries_state_help_text` (pins the help text branching: contains `f.flush()`, contains `pending `write``, does NOT contain `impl CancelSafe` — guards against slice-3 errors regressing to the slice-1 help shape); `file_two_writes_then_one_flush_then_yield_accepted` (one clear closes all preceding soils — the OS flush semantic); `file_write_flush_write_then_yield_rejected` (re-soil after a clear triggers detection); `file_two_yields_emit_one_error_per_binding` (dedup contract); `user_annotated_type_participates` (user-defined `struct Tx { } impl Tx { #[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "commit")] fn put(...); fn commit(...); }` triggers the same diagnostic, pins the user-extensibility surface so future stdlib types plug in by annotation alone). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (raii_check 21 → 29; all other test binaries unchanged). Files: `src/attribute_validator.rs` (`cancel_unsafe_until` in `RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES`), `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` (`#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "flush")]` on `File.write`), `src/raii_check.rs` (new `StateViolation` + walker + collector; ~470 LOC net), `src/cli.rs` (state-violation `note:` line in two text-emission sites + state-violation JSON/JSONL serialization), `tests/raii_check.rs` (8 new tests + slice section comment). **What slice 3a does NOT cover:** (1) `BufReader[R]` — separate sub-slice (slice 3b below) blocked on the BufReader stdlib type itself; the walker infrastructure is type-agnostic so adding BufReader is purely a stdlib annotation. (2) Branch-precise merging — `if c { f.write(); } else { f.flush(); } yield` may miss the soil in the then-branch; the v1 simplification walks both arms in source order. (3) Soiling through non-identifier receivers — `record.handle.write(...)` / `files[i].write(...)` / complex receiver shapes; only `Identifier(name).M(...)` and `self.M(...)` participate. (4) Soiling propagation across function calls — a helper that takes `f: mut ref File` and writes to it is not re-walked from the caller's flow state; effect-typed propagation is a separate slice. (5) Stdlib `sync_all` as an alternative clear method — only one clear-method-name per soil at v1 (the attribute is `method = "flush"`, not `methods = [...]`); a multi-clear shape can land later if a stdlib surface needs it.

[ ] **Slice 3b — `BufReader[R]` flow-sensitive seeding.** **Type-dependency cleared 2026-06-06** — the `BufReader[R]` interpreter MVP shipped (phase-8-stdlib-floor.md "BufReader[R]" entry: `new` / `with_capacity` / `read_line` / `read_to_string` / `read`), but its `#[cancel_unsafe_until(...)]` cancel-safety annotation was *deliberately deferred to this slice* — the soiling-method set is genuinely TBD and a wrong clear-method semantic would mis-seed this walker (see that entry's deferral note). So slice 3b is now fully unblocked: the BufReader type + read methods exist and the walker infrastructure is in place after slice 3a; the remaining work is purely the annotation + tests. This sub-slice adds the `#[cancel_unsafe_until(...)]` annotation to BufReader's buffer-soiling methods (`fill_buf` once the buffer is non-empty; `read_line` / `read_to_string` between calls that leave residual bytes — exact soiling-method set TBD) and tests the same Soil→Clear→Yield round-trip shape from slice 3a. Likely also needs a "drain" clear method on BufReader if `consume`-then-`fill_buf` isn't a clean reset. **Surface-dependency cleared 2026-06-06** — `fill_buf` / `consume` shipped in phase-8 (the `lines()` + `fill_buf`/`consume` BufReader follow-on slices), so all candidate soiling/clear methods now exist to annotate; the remaining work is the annotation choice + tests.

[x] **Slice 4 — raw-pointer detection shipped 2026-05-26.** Closes the design.md v1 NOT-CancelSafe gap for `*const T` / `*mut T` — raw pointers carry no `Drop` hook, so a cancel during their live range leaks whatever they reference. **Path chosen:** option (a) from the pre-ship plan — extend the existing `pattern_binding_types` recorder rather than thread a parallel typechecker side-table. The recorder is already the canonical surface-name source for `raii_check`; adding one arm there keeps the data flow linear (typechecker → `pattern_binding_types` → state-struct layout → `is_not_cancel_safe`) and avoids splitting "what surface type is this binding?" across two tables. **Fix:** new `Type::Pointer { .. }` arm in `src/typechecker/patterns.rs::bind_pattern_types` (let / parameter side) AND in `check_pattern_against` (match-arm side) — both record `type_display(ty)`, which yields `*mut T` / `*const T` (matching the surface syntax users wrote). New `is_raw_pointer_surface_name(type_name: &str) -> bool` helper in `src/raii_check.rs` checks `starts_with("*const ") || starts_with("*mut ")` (the trailing space is load-bearing — nominal type names cannot begin with `*` per the lexer, so the prefix is unambiguous). `is_not_cancel_safe` consults the helper *before* the slice-2 opt-in check — raw-pointer rejection is unconditional, the opt-in does not apply (its walker only matches single-segment `TypeKind::Path` targets, so `impl CancelSafe for *const T` wouldn't register even if a user wrote one). **Help-text branching:** `RaiiAcrossYieldError::help()` now branches on raw-pointer-ness — for raw pointers, the message omits the misleading `impl CancelSafe for X` suggestion (raw pointers have no `Drop` to audit) and instead points at safe-handle conversion (`ref`/`mut ref` borrow, `Box[T]`, or a Kāra-side wrapper). **5 new tests** in `tests/raii_check.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 155 slice 4` section: `fn driver(p: *const u8)` held across yield → rejected; `fn driver(p: *mut u32)` → rejected; help-text class-branching → asserts the raw-pointer help does NOT contain "impl CancelSafe" AND DOES contain "safe handle"; named-type CancelSafe opt-in does NOT transitively cover raw pointers to that type (`impl CancelSafe for Cell {}` + `fn driver(p: *const Cell)` still rejects — pins the `is_raw_pointer_surface_name` check running before the opt-in check, and also documents that pointer-target opt-ins are not a slice-2 form); `Vec[*const u8]` is NOT in scope (binding type is `Vec`, the recorder doesn't recurse into element types — documents the scope limit). **Empirical verification:** smoke-tested `fn driver(p: *const u8) { fetch(); }` parses + typechecks cleanly before starting — confirmed raw-pointer parameters are usable in v1 (the slice isn't moot for lack of expressivity). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all test binaries (raii_check 16 → 21; all others unchanged). Files: `src/typechecker/patterns.rs` (~25 lines net — new `Type::Pointer` arm in two parallel sites, with cross-reference comments naming `raii_check` as the consumer), `src/raii_check.rs` (~30 lines net — new `is_raw_pointer_surface_name` helper, prefix check in `is_not_cancel_safe`, class-branched `help()` body), `tests/raii_check.rs` (5 new tests + slice section comment). **What slice 4 does NOT cover:** (1) transitive raw-pointer reachability — `Vec[*const T]`, `Box[*const T]`, struct fields of pointer type, etc.; the recorder doesn't recurse and `raii_check`'s walk only sees top-level binding surface names. A separate sub-slice would extend `is_not_cancel_safe` to walk `pattern_binding_inner_types` for element-typed containers AND walk struct definitions for pointer-typed fields. (2) function-pointer types (`fn(...) -> ...` / `Fn(...) -> ...`) — these are `Type::Function` / `Type::OnceFunction`, not `Type::Pointer`; the spec doesn't classify them as raw pointers and the v1 cancel-safety contract for closures lives in a separate slice if/when surfaced. (3) raw-pointer types constructed via `ptr.null()` / `ptr.const(value)` — only the parameter / let-binding shape was exercised; the let-binding path lights up automatically once `bind_pattern_types` records the type, but no end-to-end tests of raw-pointer construction were added.
  5. [x] **Slice 5 — precise binding-construction span anchoring shipped 2026-05-26.** Slice 1 anchored the diagnostic only at the yield-point span and named the binding in the message body, leaving users to scan upward for where `self` / `h` / `tx` was introduced. **Implementation:** `SpanKey` (`(offset, length)`) is lossy — line/column can't be reconstructed from it, so the walker carries the full `Span` in parallel rather than reconstructing from the existing `span_key`. New `binding_span: Option<crate::token::Span>` field on `ScopeEntry` (`src/cli.rs`), populated at every push site: param (line 1722), `let` pattern, `let-uninit` `name_span`, `let-else` pattern, `if-let` / `while-let` / `for` patterns via `walk_block_with_pattern`, match-arm body bindings via `walk_expr_with_pattern`, and match-arm guard bindings. `self` keeps `binding_span: None` — `SelfParam` is the `Owned`/`Ref`/`MutRef` enum with no Span, mirroring the existing `span_key: None` convention. `record_yield_point_capture` clones the span into a new `StateStructField.binding_span: Option<Span>` field; codegen's two fixed-shape `StateStructField` builders in `src/codegen/declarations.rs:58-66` (the `park_on_fd` synthesised layout) set `binding_span: None` — codegen ignores the field, it's diagnostic-only. `RaiiAcrossYieldError` gains `binding_span: Option<Span>`, populated from `field.binding_span.clone()` in `check_raii_across_yield`. **cli.rs emission (all three output paths):** plain text (post-typecheck error pass + `cmd_run` short-circuit) adds `eprintln!("  note: binding declared here at {filename}:{line}:{col}")` between the primary error line and the help line when `binding_span` is `Some`; JSON `DiagEntry` attaches `extra_json: Some("\"binding_span\":{...}")` via the existing `extra_json` infrastructure (the entry-object writer prepends the leading `,`); JSONL `diagnostic` event appends `,"binding_span":{file,line,column}` to the event payload when present. **4 new tests** in `tests/raii_check.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 155 slice 5` section: parameter shape (`fn driver(h: Hub)`) — span anchors at the `h` token, asserted by character-at-(line,column) lookup so the assertion stays robust against minor source rewrites; `let` shape (`let h: Hub = make()`) — span at the `h` in the `let` pattern; `self` receiver — `binding_span` stays `None` (synthetic-binding contract); match-arm shape (`Held(h) => { fetch(); }`) — span at the `h` in the arm pattern, with the outer `s: Slot` parameter producing a separate error filtered out via `binding_name` lookup. **Discovered constraints during test authoring:** (1) Kara match arms use bare-variant syntax `Held(h) => ...` not the qualified `Slot::Held(h) => ...` form; (2) `pub fn make() -> Hub` triggers `E_PRIVATE_TYPE_IN_PUBLIC_SIGNATURE` for a non-pub shared struct — tests use non-pub helper fns. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (raii_check 12 → 16; all other test binaries unchanged). Files: `src/ast.rs` (new `binding_span` field on `StateStructField`), `src/cli.rs` (`ScopeEntry.binding_span` + 7 push-site updates + 3 emission-site updates), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (2 fixed-shape builders updated to `binding_span: None`), `src/raii_check.rs` (`RaiiAcrossYieldError.binding_span` + populate from `field.binding_span`), `tests/raii_check.rs` (4 new tests + slice section comment). **What slice 5 does NOT cover:** binding-state-change spans for slice 3's flow-sensitive case (e.g. "last `.write()` was here, no `.flush()` before yield") — those land alongside slice 3 if at all; the diagnostic uses a `note:` line in plain output rather than a structured secondary-span highlight (no codebase-wide secondary-span infrastructure exists today, so the slice follows the existing `note:` convention).

- [ ] **P0 — Concurrency target staging — 100K → 250K → 1M+.** Public v1 launch gated on M3.
  1. [ ] **M1 — 100K stable idle connections.** Flagship demo (Parallax-shape) sustains 100K concurrent idle WebSocket connections under HTTPS on a single Linux box. CI benchmark gate added; first published number. The original accept-loop-wedge blocker is RESOLVED (2026-05-28). The slice-4 verification run (2026-05-29) established a clean **50K** baseline (0 failed, 7.9 KB/conn, connect p99 208 ms — `docs/investigations/demo1_m1_verification.md`) and surfaced an establishment-throughput collapse near ~70–77K; root-caused to a **server-side synchronous-handshake serialization defect, now FIXED** (concurrent handshake pool — see the resolved P0 entry below). Post-fix, the residual ~70K local ceiling is the **measurement rig** (co-resident tokio bench client saturating a 2-core box; the Kāra server is idle at the collapse), not a code defect. Stays `[ ]`: a real 100K number now requires a **separate, well-provisioned client machine** (the M3-plan rig), not further server fixes.
  2. [ ] **M2 — 250K stable idle connections.** Same demo, 2.5× scale, no P99 cliff. Polish layer 1 (timer-wheel implementation, allocator behavior under churn, fd-set primitives).
  3. [ ] **M3 — 1M+ stable idle connections, cross-platform parity.** Linux io_uring path for file I/O alongside epoll for sockets; macOS kqueue tuning; Windows IOCP parity. No regression vs. M2 baseline. v1 public launch unblocks.
  4. [ ] **CI benchmark gate on flagship demo.** P50 / P95 / P99 / P99.9 + connection-establishment cost tracked separately. >5% steady-state regression blocks merge without explicit override + justification.

- [ ] **P0 — Flagship Demo 1: minimal HTTP+WebSocket server.** Smallest possible HTTP server that holds 1M+ idle WebSocket connections under HTTPS. Used as the M1 / M2 / M3 verification gate (line 132 above — M1/M2/M3 sub-entries reference this demo as their verification artifact, and `CI benchmark gate on flagship demo` at line 136 wires CI against the bench harness from slice 3 below). Lives in `examples/ws_idle_holder/` (multi-file project shape — `kara.toml` + `src/main.kara`, mirroring `examples/parallax_lite/`); CI benchmark suite runs against the slice 3 bench harness.

  **Two hard prereqs, both tracked as their own entries below in this file:** the `spawn() / TaskGroup runtime + codegen + stdlib` entry (canonical accept-loop shape requires `loop { let conn = listener.accept()?; group.spawn(|| handle(conn)) }` per design.md § Explicit Concurrency), and the `TLS / HTTPS server-side stdlib` entry (the demo's spec says "under HTTPS" — plaintext `ws://` is acceptable for slice 1 to surface runtime issues early, but slice 2 ships TLS before any M1 number is published).

  **Sub-slices.**

  1. [x] **Slice 1 — skeleton kara program (plaintext `ws://`) shipped 2026-05-27.** Smallest viable demo source landed under `examples/ws_idle_holder/` (multi-file project shape mirroring `examples/parallax_lite/` — `kara.toml` + `src/main.kara` + `README.md`). The demo binds a `TcpListener` on `127.0.0.1:0` (ephemeral port via `BOUND_PORT=<n>` stdout convention from slice 8 of phase-6 line 17), allocates a `TaskGroup`, and runs the canonical accept-loop `loop { let ws = WebSocket.accept(listener); tg.spawn(|| handle_connection(ws)); }`. The per-task `handle_connection(ws: WebSocket)` reads frames in an `Array[u8, 4096]` buffer via `ws.recv_text(mut buf)` until the peer disconnects (`Ok(0)` clean EOF) or a protocol/IO error fires; the `Drop` impl on `WebSocket` (slice 9d of phase-6 line 17) closes the fd at scope exit. The recv loop is a pure "wait-and-wake" pattern — `karac_park_on_fd` suspends the per-connection task on read-readiness, so 100K idle connections occupy ~100K *parked* tasks in the scheduler's wait-set, not 100K *running* threads. **Workload-shaped pressure surfaced** (per `feedback_optimize_for_production_not_kata` — the demo IS the production workload): three prereq slices landed as direct unblockers during slice 1 implementation, all shipped 2026-05-27 and tracked under phase-6 line 218: (a) slice 8 (`spawn` slot widened from `Fn() -> T` to `OnceFn() -> T` so the move-capturing closure `|| handle_connection(ws)` typechecks); (b) slice 9 (stdlib struct-by-value param LLVM ABI — explicit arms in `llvm_type_for_name` for `TcpListener` / `TcpStream` / `WebSocket` so passing one by value produces a `{ i32 }` param signature rather than the i64 fall-through default); (c) cross-task-safe boundary check at the `tg.spawn` site (line 170 slice 3a) — pinned the design ahead of the demo's `ws` capture. **Smoke-test verified manually** via `nc` (`README.md § Manual smoke test`): binary binds, prints BOUND_PORT, accepts TCP connections, completes the RFC 6455 HTTP upgrade with the canonical `Sec-WebSocket-Accept: s3pPLMBiTxaQ9kYGzzhZRbK+xOo=` reference value, holds the connection until peer disconnect or process kill. Automated Rust-side e2e test deferred to slice 3 (bench harness) per the tracker — the harness already needs to open N concurrent connections, so single-connection acceptance is a degenerate case of the test infrastructure it builds. Files: `examples/ws_idle_holder/kara.toml` (~7 LoC project manifest), `examples/ws_idle_holder/src/main.kara` (~75 LoC kara source including extensive architecture comments), `examples/ws_idle_holder/README.md` (~150 LoC explaining the demo + how-to-run + smoke-test recipe + cross-refs). **Unblocks** Demo 1 slices 2 (TLS layer), 3 (bench harness), 4 (M1 100K verification) — the kara source they all consume now exists. **Cross-link**: the spawn/TaskGroup compiler+runtime stack (line 218 slices 1–9) is the prereq Demo 1 was carrying; with slice 1 shipped, the structural-correctness portion of the M1 milestone gate is complete.

  2. [x] **Slice 2 — TLS / HTTPS layer shipped 2026-05-27.** Wired the demo to `wss://`: `TcpListener.bind` → `TlsListener.bind_tls(addr, cert_pem, key_pem)`, `WebSocket.accept(listener)` → `WebSocket.accept_tls(listener)`. The per-connection handler is byte-for-byte unchanged from slice 1 — the `WebSocket` value-model shape is identical regardless of transport, and the framing FFIs auto-dispatch encryption through the per-fd rustls session. **Unblocked by** the `TLS / HTTPS server-side stdlib` entry (phase-6 line 236), whose 5 sub-slices all shipped 2026-05-27: slice 1 (rustls runtime FFI), slice 2 (`TlsListener` / `TlsStream` types + codegen), slice 3 (`WebSocket.accept_tls` + TLS-aware WS framing), slice 4 (test-cert fixtures), slice 5 (design.md + this demo wire-up — co-shipped). **End-to-end verified**: the demo binds, completes a real TLS handshake + WebSocket-over-TLS HTTP upgrade against a Python `ssl` client, returns `101 Switching Protocols` with a correct `Sec-WebSocket-Accept`. The cert is inlined as PEM literals pending the `FileSystem.read_to_string` codegen lowering (tracked as follow-on (a) under phase-6 line 236).
