README updated to a five-impl v7 table; `tests/parallax_bench.rs` smoke+dry-run green. Full Parallax (4 upstreams + provider story) if cost-model tuning resolves in time; Parallax-lite (single upstream + WebSocket fanout) is the conditional fallback that still proves the architecture. **Status as of 2026-05-30**: both halves landed in code by 2026-05-10 — `examples/parallax_lite/` (3-resource write-only fan-out; anchors auto-par IR shape via `tests/parallax_lite.rs`) and `examples/parallax/` (4-upstream fan-out + join with typed `Dashboard` return; 4-language bench at `examples/parallax/bench/README.md` across Kāra / Rust / Go / Node; cold-start + steady-state matrix across 3 conn counts × 3 runs). Load-bearing codegen prereq (`phase-7-codegen.md` "Par codegen: return values") `[x]` shipped. 2026-05-10 baseline headline: Kāra steady-state `p99` **2.7× lower than Rust** at `-c100`; `karac_par_run` work-helping wait loop is the design dividend. **Parent stays open pending two close-out gates:** (a) ~~two v1 codegen gaps + the example rewrite that block Kāra response-body parity~~ — **DONE 2026-06-05.** Both codegen gaps fixed (gap A `refs_in_expr` f-string arm verified present + tested; gap B f-string-accumulator double-free on move-out paths fixed, struct-field + explicit-return, with ASAN coverage — sub-entries below), AND `examples/parallax/bench/kara/server.kara::handle()` now serializes the actual `Dashboard` fields into the JSON body via an f-string — byte-for-byte the wire shape Rust/Go/Node emit (`{"profile":{"user_id":1,"name":"Alice"},"latest_order":{"order_id":<n>},"top_notification":{"kind":<n>},"top_recommendation":{"item_id":<n>}}`). Smoke-verified end-to-end: built the server, drove an HTTP request, got the real-data body with the three large busy_loop results woven in (e.g. `order_id:265066944`); the status-fold workaround is gone (status is a constant 200). `tests/parallax_bench.rs::test_kara_bench_server_smoke` exercises the rewritten handler (2xx + body contains `"profile"`) — green. The three larger i64 fetches now ride into the body and survive DCE; `fetch_profile_name`'s busy_loop stays discarded identically to Rust/Go (symmetric — apples-to-apples). **The ONLY remaining close-out gate is (b): the re-bench.** (b) post-2026-05-10 regression check — substantial compiler work since baseline (spawn/TaskGroup landed 2026-05-27, cross-task-safe walker, RAII flow-sensitive walker, binding-construction span anchoring, par-codegen return-values follow-ons) any of which could perturb auto-par grouping or codegen on the canonical fan-out + join shape. Closes once (a) ships and (b) re-bench matches the 2026-05-10 baseline within ±10% on `req/s` + `p99` at `-c100` (larger delta gets a `docs/investigations/` writeup before closure). **F5 deviation carries**: `sleep_ms` providers replaced with CPU-bound busy_loops at v1 (no `sleep_ms` in stdlib; Phase 11 long-tail per `docs/dogfooding.md § Slice E "Out of scope"`) — documented in `bench/README.md`; central fan-out + join capability claim still delivered; real-network-I/O providers lift "live" once `sleep_ms` lands. **Re-bench infrastructure already in place**: `bench.sh` + `--dry-run` CI gate via `tests/parallax_bench.rs`; M5 Pro is the documented v1-baseline rig; no new tooling needed.

  - [x] **Parallax codegen gap A — auto-par `refs_in_expr` `InterpolatedStringLit` arm — DONE (verified 2026-06-05).** The free-var collector `refs_in_expr` has the `ExprKind::InterpolatedStringLit` arm at `src/codegen/closures.rs:1004` (recurses into each `ParsedInterpolationPart::Expr` segment), so a captured binding read inside an f-string body that flows into a parallel-group statement IS visible to the conflict analyzer. Regression test: `tests/par_codegen.rs:1436::test_auto_par_fstring_tail_captures_par_group_bindings`. (The checkbox was left unflipped after the fix landed; verified present + tested on 2026-06-05 during the gap-B work below.) **Pairs with gap B** — both were needed before the Kāra bench impl can weave `Dashboard` data into the response body.

  - [x] **Parallax codegen gap B — f-string accumulator double-free on move-out paths — FIXED 2026-06-05.** An f-string accumulator buffer that moves out of its scope (into a returned struct field, or via an explicit `return f"..."`) was still freed by the accumulator's own scope-exit `FreeVecBuffer` — a **double-free that aborted under macOS malloc (exit 133)**, silent until reproduced. **Three sub-cases, status:** (1) **tail-expr `f"..."`** (function body ends in an f-string) — was already fixed (`functions.rs` zeros the acc cap when `final_expr` is an `InterpolatedStringLit`). (2) **f-string DIRECTLY as a struct-literal field value** (`Resp { body: f"..." }`) — the demo's exact shape — **fixed here**: `compile_struct_init` (both the non-shared stack-aggregate branch and the shared/par Arc-heap branch) now calls a new `suppress_fstr_acc_if_moved_out` after compiling each field value, which takes the staged `last_fstr_acc` and zeros its cap (`zero_vec_alloca_cap`) so the accumulator's free no-ops — the field now owns the buffer. (3) **explicit `return f"..."`** mid-function — **fixed here**: same helper called in the `ExprKind::Return` arm after `compile_expr` (the pre-compile `suppress_source_vec_cleanup_for_arg` is Identifier-only and runs before the acc is staged). All mirror the existing `Let`/`Assign` take points. The Identifier-named forms (`Resp { body: b }` / `return b`) were already covered. **Root cause:** `suppress_source_vec_cleanup_for_arg` early-returns for any non-`Identifier` expr, so a direct f-string at a move-out site never got its staged acc suppressed. **Reproduced first** (`feedback_reproduce_before_trusting_bug_diagnosis`): the struct-field and explicit-return forms both printed nothing / exit 133; a let-bound f-string into the same struct field worked (the `let` is a take point), isolating the gap. **String interpolation confirmed working** — `f"id={id} name={name}"` weaves both an i64 and a String correctly, so the demo can serialize `profile_name` too (removing the old "3-of-4 coverage" caveat). **Tests:** 2 codegen E2E (`tests/codegen.rs` — struct-field + explicit-return, each read multiple times by the caller) + 3 ASAN (`tests/memory_sanitizer.rs::asan_fstring_into_returned_plain_struct_field` / `_shared_struct_field` / `_explicit_return` — UAF/double-free coverage on both struct branches + the return path). Gates: fmt + clippy ×3; `--features llvm` codegen 1117/1117, memory_sanitizer 77/77, par_codegen 105/105 — zero regressions. Files: `src/codegen/exprs.rs` (~30 lines — helper + 3 call sites). **Unblocks** the Parallax body-weaving rewrite + re-bench close-out below; pairs with gap A.

  - [x] **Parallax re-bench — DONE 2026-06-06 (v7 five-impl single-session sweep).** Ran `bench.sh` defaults (k,r,g,n,p × {100,1000,5000} × 3 runs) on the M5 Pro after gaps A+B + the body-weave landed. **Acceptance results:** (i) regression check — Kāra clean (req/s 720→738 +2.5%, p99 300→272 ms −9.4%, within ±10%), Go clean (+3.0% / −4.3%), Node unchanged; Rust p99 −11.6% and Phoenix +22% req/s landed past ±10% but are *improvements* on untouched impls (tokio tail variance / cross-session BEAM drift), not regressions → documented inline in the README v7 row, no `docs/investigations/` writeup needed. (ii) Phoenix vs 2026-05-30 baseline: drift treated as machine-state signal (improvement). (iii) body-bytes parity EXACT (159 B across all five — wire shape aligned). (iv) `bench.sh` graceful-degrade smoke green. Headline holds: Kāra `-c100` p99 **2.6× lower than Rust**. README `## History` now has the `v7` five-impl row + updated cold-start/steady-state tables. Original spec retained below for reference. — Re-run `examples/parallax/bench/bench.sh` after gaps A + B ship; compare cold-start + steady-state to the 2026-05-10 baseline at `examples/parallax/bench/README.md` (the v6 cold-start + sweep table). **Cohort is now five impls** (kara / rust / go / node / phoenix) — Phoenix landed 2026-05-30 with a first-measurement baseline (commit `73eda0df` + bench.sh wiring `4f5e980`) and joins the apples-to-apples sweep; the close-out's `v7` README row captures all five impls in a single session rather than mixing 2026-05-10 numbers (four impls) with 2026-05-30 numbers (Phoenix solo), per [`feedback_v1_ship_reality_not_promises`](../../CLAUDE.md). **Acceptance criteria:** (i) regression check — Kāra/Rust/Go/Node current numbers within ±10% on `req/s` and `p99` at `-c100` vs the 2026-05-10 baseline (larger delta triggers a `docs/investigations/` root-cause writeup before close); (ii) Phoenix numbers within ±10% on `req/s` + `p99` at `-c100` vs the 2026-05-30 first-measurement baseline at `examples/parallax/bench/phoenix/bench-results.json` (no codegen-side perturbation risk on Phoenix — pure same-machine reproducibility check; treats deviation as machine-state drift signal); (iii) Kāra response body now serializes actual `Dashboard` data (gaps A + B verification — body bytes within ±30 B of Rust/Go/Node, confirming the wire shape is finally aligned); (iv) `bench.sh` still graceful-degrades when toolchains missing (existing CI smoke at `tests/parallax_bench.rs`). Updates README's `## History` section with a `v7` row capturing the post-gap-fix numbers. **Hardware**: same M5 Pro rig as the 2026-05-10 baseline (M5 Pro is the v1-baseline machine; x86 confirmation is the sibling entry below). No new tooling needed — `bench.sh` already supports the full five-impl sweep. **Flips parent entry to `[x]` on landing**; also flips the Phoenix comparator entry below to `[x]` since the close-out is its delivery moment.

- [ ] **P2 — Parallax Phoenix Bandit acceptor pool tuning.** At `-c5000` the Phoenix comparator reports 0 req/s in 2/3 measurement rounds because Bandit's default `num_acceptors` (~10) can't ingest 5000 concurrent connects in the 10 s measure window — a configuration artifact, not Phoenix's fundamental limit. Per the apples-to-apples discipline in [`feedback_per_conn_density_is_the_headline`](../../CLAUDE.md) + [`feedback_v1_ship_reality_not_promises`](../../CLAUDE.md), the Kāra-vs-Phoenix headline must compare each impl at its tuned best, not its default-config worst — otherwise the auto-par win is built on a misconfigured competitor. Scope: raise `num_acceptors` via the endpoint's `:thousand_island_options` config (~one-line change in `examples/parallax/bench/phoenix/lib/parallax_bench_web/endpoint.ex`), measure whether `-c5000` lifts above zero, and re-measure `-c100` + `-c1000` to confirm tuning doesn't regress the smaller-conn rows. Acceptance: either (i) `-c5000` row produces non-zero numbers in all three measurement rounds with no `-c100`/`-c1000` regression — land the config change, document the bumped value in `phoenix/README.md`; or (ii) tuning surfaces a deeper Phoenix-side bottleneck (BEAM scheduler saturation, ETS contention, etc.) — document the finding in `phoenix/README.md`'s deviations section and leave default-config numbers in place with the limitation explicitly called out. Gated on the Parallax re-bench close-out landing first (don't perturb Phoenix while the close-out cohort is being measured). Surfaced 2026-05-30 by the Phoenix comparator agent.

### Pre-existing Phase 6 work

- [x] **G8 — Effect inference compilation speed** (measured 2026-06-01). Benchmarked on four synthetic shapes (deep chain, broad mesh, mutually-recursive SCC clusters, wide multi-resource fan) at 500–4000 private functions / 250–4000 call depth via a new `#[ignore]`d harness `tests/effect_inference_bench.rs` (run: `cargo test --release --test effect_inference_bench effect_inference_speed -- --ignored --nocapture`). **Result: effect inference is LINEAR** — ~3 µs/private-fn, 2.0–2.2× time for 2× functions, no super-linear blowup through 4000 fns; single-digit ms in absolute terms (1.5 ms at 500 fns, 3.0 ms at 1000). The per-SCC O(k²) fixpoint adds no measurable penalty (monotone effects ⇒ ≤k passes per cycle). Where effectcheck nominally touches ~10–13% of the *measured front end* (mesh/wide/recursive-50×10), that is a denominator artifact: the front-end total is dominated by `ownershipcheck` (see new entry below), and against a codegen-inclusive total compile (codegen+LLVM-opt+link dominate real builds) effectcheck falls well under 10%. **Verdict: none of the three mitigations warranted** — (1) per-fn caching has no hotspot to cache in a ~3 µs/fn linear pass (measure-first, per [`feedback_measure_first_empirical`](../../CLAUDE.md)); (2) optional annotations would forfeit the "private effects are inferred" guarantee for no win; (3) there is no complexity cliff to warn about. Full methodology + numbers: [`docs/investigations/effect_inference_speed.md`](../investigations/effect_inference_speed.md). Revisit only if a real production corpus ever profiles effect inference as a hotspot, per [`feedback_optimize_for_production_not_kata`](../../CLAUDE.md).

- [x] **`ownershipcheck` super-linear (~quadratic) front-end scaling — RESOLVED 2026-06-02 (restored to linear, acceptance (i)).** Surfaced 2026-06-01 by the G8 benchmark (entry above; data + harness in [`docs/investigations/effect_inference_speed.md`](../investigations/effect_inference_speed.md) and `tests/effect_inference_bench.rs`). `ownershipcheck` was the dominant front-end phase and scaled ~quadratically with function count: **25.9 ms → 104.2 ms** for a chain of 500 → 1000 private fns (4.0× for 2× input, re-measured at fix time), vs effectcheck's clean 2× linear growth over the same step. At 1000 fns it was ~32× the effectcheck cost and ~95% of the measured front end — the real front-end scaling lever (far ahead of effect inference). **Root cause:** the use-classifier's `classify_function_body` rebuilt three whole-program tables (`collect_method_self_modes`, `collect_callee_param_modes`, `collect_unit_variant_names`) on *every* call, and the ownership pass classifies each function's body **twice** — once in the RC-predicate pre-pass (`run_predicate_for_function` → `classify_function_body`) and once in-place in `check_function`. For N functions that is O(N × program) = O(N²); the suspected "whole-program table re-traversed per function" was exactly it. **Fix:** hoist the three tables into a `ClassifierPrelude` built once per program (`src/use_classifier.rs`), borrowed by new `classify_function_body_with` / `run_predicate_for_function_with` entry points (`UseClassifier` now borrows the tables instead of owning per-call copies). `check_items` builds the prelude once and threads it through `check_function` → `populate_predicate_outputs`. The two whole-program predicate drivers (`predicate_rc_candidates_for_program`, `predicate_uam_candidates_for_program`) build the prelude once too, fixing the same O(N²) in their loops. Classifier output is byte-identical (only the build *site* moved), so RC/UAM/ownership/codegen decisions are unchanged — confirmed by full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` passing with zero regressions (sole red is a pre-existing, unrelated `tls_codegen` accept_tls park assertion that fails identically on baseline with this change stashed — tracked in its own entry below). **Result (M5 Pro, release): ownershipcheck at chain-1000 drops 104.2 ms → 1.41 ms (74×); scaling is now linear** (chain 500→1000: 0.89 → 1.41 ms, ~1.6× for 2× input — the residual is fixed per-program overhead, not per-function growth). Front-end total at chain-1000: 109.5 ms → 6.8 ms, hitting acceptance (i) ("toward the ~5 ms the other phases sum to"). Files: `src/use_classifier.rs`, `src/rc_predicate.rs`, `src/ownership.rs`. Full before/after table appended to [`docs/investigations/effect_inference_speed.md`](../investigations/effect_inference_speed.md).

- [x] **`tls_codegen` accept_tls park assertion — NON-ISSUE (stale-worktree-base artifact); already fixed on `main`. Closed 2026-06-02.** Originally logged while running the `--features llvm` gate during the `ownershipcheck` perf fix: the test `test_ir_websocket_accept_tls_parks_then_calls_runtime_ffi` asserted `WebSocket.accept_tls(listener)` codegen *parks* before calling `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls`, but the emitted IR called the FFI with no park. **Root cause of the observation: the ownership-fix worktree had branched from a stale base (`acd63e65`) that predated the relevant fix** — it was *not* actually current `main`, so the "red on main HEAD" call was a misread of which commit was main's tip (reproduce-before-trusting applies to one's own bug log too). The park was **deliberately dropped** by `c4c848bd` ("fix(codegen): drop redundant accept park → fix concurrent WS-over-TLS resume race (A2)"): `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls` self-waits (it drains the accept backlog into an async handshake pool and loops until a completed handshake is ready), so an inline park was redundant *and* harmful — a pending connection's handshake completion never makes the listener readable, so the inline park never resumed and the concurrent WS-over-TLS accept loop wedged. The park is now kept only when accept is lowered inside a coroutine body (`coro_ctx.is_some()`). The stale park-asserting test was replaced by `8bddf30f` with `test_ir_websocket_accept_tls_inline_omits_park_then_calls_runtime_ffi` (asserts inline accept_tls does NOT park but still calls the FFI), with behavioral coverage in `tests/coro_e2e.rs::coroutine_ws_over_tls_concurrent_handlers_all_execute`. **Verified 2026-06-02 on `main`: `cargo test --features llvm --test tls_codegen` is fully green (17 passed, 0 failed)** and the old test name no longer exists. No code change required.

- [x] **G13 — Work-stealing overhead on fine-grained tasks — RESOLVED 2026-06-02 (measure-first; existing cost-model calibration empirically validated, no code change warranted).** Measured the runtime scheduling primitives directly via a new `#[ignore]`d benchmark `scheduler::tests::bench_g13_scheduling_overhead` in `runtime/src/scheduler.rs` (run: `cargo test -p karac-runtime --release bench_g13_scheduling_overhead -- --ignored --nocapture`). Full methodology + numbers: [`docs/investigations/task_scheduling_overhead.md`](../investigations/task_scheduling_overhead.md). **Findings (M5 Pro, release, 18 workers):** (1) **spawn + join ≈ 16µs/task** one-in-flight, ~6µs amortized pipelined — the `<1µs` target is **not reachable** with the `Mutex`+`Condvar` global-queue design (two OS-thread hand-offs, each a µs-scale condvar wake) and **does not need to be** (point 2). (2) **Minimum task-duration threshold established and validated:** the empirical granularity crossover where `karac_par_run` beats running the branches in-thread is **~80µs of total group work** (≈20µs/branch at N=4; stable across runs), which **exactly matches** the pinned `REDUCE_DISPATCH_THRESHOLD_UNITS` = `DISPATCH_OVERHEAD_PER_CALL_UNITS`(10,000 ns) × `ASSUMED_WORKER_COUNT`(8) = 80,000 units ≈ 80µs in `src/codegen/reduce.rs`. The gate sits right at break-even on the conservative side. par_run dispatch overhead measured at ~10µs base + ~1µs/branch (N=2→16: 13.9→28.8µs), confirming the 10µs `DISPATCH_OVERHEAD_PER_CALL_UNITS` constant. The `PAR_RUN_DISPATCH_THRESHOLD_UNITS`=500 / `PAR_RUN_VISIBILITY_THRESHOLD_UNITS`=50 gate operates in the `CostEstimator`'s abstract per-statement units (not ns) and pairs a low dispatch floor with a visibility floor that keeps dispatch *on* for opaque impl-method bodies — its dispatch-cost model (~10µs) is consistent with the measurement. Explicit `spawn()`/`TaskGroup` is intentionally **ungated** (user chose the granularity; rule of thumb: ≫16µs work per task). (3) **Mixed same-/different-resource workloads resolve at analysis time:** `src/concurrency.rs` serializes same-resource (effect-conflicting) statements into one dependency group that never reaches `karac_par_run` (zero dispatch paid), while disjoint statements form parallel groups subject to the ~80µs crossover; the end-to-end disjoint fan-out wall-clock is already exercised by the Parallax bench (`examples/parallax/bench/`). **Verdict: none of the three constants need recalibration** — the 80,000-unit reduce gate lands on the measured crossover, the 10µs per-call model matches par_run dispatch. Work-stealing stays correctly deferred (single global queue sustains 4096-task fan-outs at ~6µs/task with no contention collapse — measurement 2). Revisit only if a production workload profiles spawn latency or queue contention as a hotspot, per [`feedback_optimize_for_production_not_kata`](../../CLAUDE.md) + [`feedback_measure_first_empirical`](../../CLAUDE.md).

- [x] **Cross-task-safe set + structural Send replacement at task boundaries — COMPLETE 2026-06-03.** Spec at `design.md § Structured Concurrency Lifetime Guarantees` (v60 item 48). The spawn / par {} / TaskGroup boundary check that rejects captures whose type reaches a not-cross-task-safe type. Replaces the deferred Send+Sync auto-trait approach with a closed structural list — no user-extensible auto-trait inference at v1. **All sub-slices landed:** 1+2 (closed enumeration + transitive walker, 2026-05-27), 3a (spawn / TaskGroup.spawn, 2026-05-27), 3b (`par {}`, 2026-06-03), 3c (`Channel.send` + `providers`/`with_provider`, 2026-06-03), 4 (three-line `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` diagnostic, 2026-06-03), 5 (borrow-rule verification, 2026-06-03), 6 (test coverage for the v1-reachable subset; remainder gated on `par struct` / the § 9476 model / `Rc`-`OnceCell`-`Arc` nameability — see slice 6). **Surfaced + tracked en route:** the `par struct` parser gap (entry directly below) and the design.md § 8506 vs § 9476 reconciliation (v1 follows the conservative § 8506 model; documented in design.md after the § 9476 borrow-rule table).

  1. [x] **Closed cross-task-unsafe enumeration + transitive walker shipped 2026-05-27.** Slices 1+2 landed together as standalone `src/cross_task_safe.rs` (~310 LoC) + 14 integration tests. **Scope correction**: original called for memoization (per type id). Shipped without — v1 types aren't interned (no stable id), so cache key would be `type_display(ty)` which costs more than the walker for small types. Measure-first; cache lands when profiling shows it. **Unsafe set (closed enumeration).** Five hardcoded shapes: `Type::Shared(_)` (any shared struct), `Type::Rc(_)`, `Type::Pointer { .. }`, `Type::Named { name: "OnceCell", .. }`, plus shared-enum via `enum_info.is_shared`. **Walker**: `is_cross_task_safe(ty, types) -> Result<(), CrossTaskUnsafePath>` walks depth-first into Tuple/Array/Slice elements, Named args (`Vec[Rc[T]]` catches the Rc), Arc inner (Arc safe but contents matter), Ref/MutRef/Weak inners, user struct fields via `struct_info`, user enum variant payloads via `enum_info` (Unit/Tuple/Struct variants). Does NOT recurse: Function/OnceFunction (closure captures checked at boundary site), TypeParam/TypeVar/AssocProjection/Existential (conservatively safe — check fires post-mono in slice 3). **`CrossTaskUnsafePath`** carries `{ root, path, unsafe_leaf, fix_it }` where `fix_it: CrossTaskUnsafeFixIt` is `RcToArc` / `SharedToPar` / `OnceCellToLock` / `RawPointer`; each variant has a `help_text(unsafe_leaf)` rendering for slice 4's diagnostic. **14 integration tests** in `tests/cross_task_safe.rs`: primitives safe; Vec[i64]/Arc[i64]/TypeParam safe; direct-hits Rc/shared/raw_ptr/OnceCell with correct fix-it; Vec[Rc[T]] path through arg; Arc[Rc[T]] still unsafe via inner; user `shared struct`/`shared enum` rejected; ref-to-unsafe-inner unsafe; fix-it help text per variant. **2 tests deferred to slice 3** (boundary integration): user struct with `Rc[T]` field, user enum variant with `Rc[T]` payload — `Rc[T]` isn't directly nameable in user kara source at v1 (emerges via typechecker-internal ownership analysis on shared-struct values). Slice 3 will exercise transitivity through user types via real spawn-site captures. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test` passes with zero regressions (14 new tests). Files: `src/cross_task_safe.rs` (new, ~310 LoC), `src/lib.rs` (`pub mod cross_task_safe;`), `tests/cross_task_safe.rs` (new, ~230 LoC). **Unblocks** slice 3 (boundary-site enforcement), slice 4 (diagnostic), and slice 6 of the line-218 entry.
  2. [x] **Transitive type-tree walker shipped 2026-05-27** — consolidated with slice 1 above.
  3. [x] **Boundary-site enforcement.** Five concrete check sites; v1 ships these sequenced as 3a → 3b → 3c so each landing is verifiable in isolation. **All five shipped (3a 2026-05-27, 3b + 3c 2026-06-03).**
     - **3a.** [x] **`spawn(closure)` + `TaskGroup.spawn(closure)` shipped 2026-05-27.** The two new boundary sites introduced by the line-218 `spawn() / TaskGroup` work. Hook lives in a new `src/typechecker/cross_task_check.rs` (~470 LoC) and fires inline from `infer_call` (bare-identifier `spawn` with 1 arg) and `infer_method_call` (receiver type's `Type::Named { name: "TaskGroup", .. }` with `method == "spawn"`). Each hook snapshots the outer local scope via `flatten_local_scope_snapshot()` *before* the closure body's params get pushed, walks the closure body collecting identifier references that resolve to outer bindings (mirrors `src/codegen/closures.rs::refs_in_expr` at the typechecker layer; tracks body-local `let` / `for` / `if let` / `while let` / `match` arm shadows + nested-closure params), then runs `is_cross_task_safe_with` (sibling to the public `is_cross_task_safe`; takes `&HashMap<String, StructInfo>` + `&HashMap<String, EnumInfo>` directly so it works mid-typecheck against `env.structs` / `env.enums` before `TypeCheckResult` is materialised) against each capture's declared type. The diagnostic anchors at the *first reference* inside the closure body (capture-leak site), not the closure literal itself, so the user sees where the unsafe value flows across the boundary. New `TypeErrorKind::CrossTaskUnsafeCapture` variant + `E0254` error code (`E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` in the user-visible message). Free-fn `spawn` check is gated on `self.local_scope.lookup("spawn").is_none()` so a user-defined local shadow of `spawn` bypasses the boundary hook (matches the existing `tcp_listener` / `ws` shadow precedent). **8 new tests** in `tests/typechecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 170 slice 3a: cross-task-safe boundary check` section: `spawn_capturing_primitive_only_accepted` + `taskgroup_spawn_capturing_primitive_only_accepted` + `spawn_with_no_captures_accepted` + `spawn_with_vec_of_primitive_capture_accepted` (positives — every reachable leaf is safe); `spawn_capturing_shared_struct_rejected_with_par_fix_it` + `taskgroup_spawn_capturing_shared_struct_rejected_with_par_fix_it` (direct shared-struct rejection with SharedToPar fix-it text); `spawn_capturing_raw_pointer_rejected_with_atomic_or_channel_fix_it` (`*mut u8` rejection); `spawn_capturing_vec_of_raw_pointers_rejected_transitively` (transitive — `Vec[*mut u8]` rejected via `\`Vec\` arg 0` path); `spawn_capturing_struct_with_shared_field_rejected_through_field_path` (transitive through struct field — `Holder { cache: Cache, count: i64 }` rejected at `field 'cache'`); `local_binding_shadowing_captured_outer_skips_check` (regression guard — body-local `let` shadows outer name, walker drops the outer binding from capture set). **Refactor of slice 1+2's walker**: split `is_cross_task_safe(ty, types)` into a thin delegator + a new `is_cross_task_safe_with(ty, struct_info, enum_info)` so the in-progress typecheck path can call it without a materialised `TypeCheckResult`. The slice-1 public API is unchanged (existing 14 tests in `tests/cross_task_safe.rs` all pass). **Scope correction from the original slice 3 spec**: the five-site bundle was split into 3a (this ship — the two new spawn-shaped sites) + 3b (`par {}` block — additive layer on existing ownership-phase rules) + 3c (`Channel.send` across boundary + `with_provider[R]` — needs par-region escape analysis touching) per the "blockers get their own tracker entries" feedback. Each remaining site is its own `[ ]` entry below so the integration sequencing is visible at the index level. **Diagnostic shape**: single-line `error[E_NOT_CROSS_TASK]: capture of \`name\` (type \`T\`) cannot cross a {spawn|TaskGroup.spawn} task boundary -- type \`T\` reaches \`<unsafe-leaf>\` at <path>; help: <fix-it>`. The slice 4 entry's three-line shape (separate `error` / `note` / `help` lines) is a v1 follow-on — the cli aggregator at `src/cli.rs` renders TypeError variants as a single message string today; splitting into multi-line shape requires the slice-4 diagnostic-builder refactor (carries below). **What slice 3a does NOT cover** (carried to 3b / 3c): (1) `par {}` block boundary — every captured binding read into any branch body; the boundary fires at the typecheck layer's `ExprKind::Par(block)` visit (slice 3b); (2) `Channel.send(val)` when the channel is used to transfer ownership across a `par {}` / `spawn` boundary — requires the existing par-region escape analysis from `src/provider_escape.rs` to detect "this Sender flows into a spawn / par branch" (slice 3c); (3) `with_provider[R](provider, closure)` call — walk the concrete `provider` type at the call site (replaces the deferred Send+Sync auto-trait check; slice 3c). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test` and `cargo test --features llvm` pass with zero regressions (typechecker 1270 → 1278; all other binaries unchanged). Files: `src/cross_task_safe.rs` (refactor — adds `is_cross_task_safe_with` + `use` for `StructInfo` / `EnumInfo`), `src/typechecker.rs` (~15 lines net — `mod cross_task_check;` + new `CrossTaskUnsafeCapture` variant + diag-class arm), `src/typechecker/cross_task_check.rs` (new, ~470 LoC: hook method + standalone capture walker covering every `ExprKind` / `StmtKind` shape), `src/typechecker/expr_call.rs` (~12 lines — bare-`spawn` intercept), `src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs` (~17 lines — `TaskGroup.spawn` intercept), `src/cli.rs` (~7 lines — `E0254` error-code mapping), `tests/typechecker.rs` (~165 lines net — 8 new tests under the slice-3a section comment). **Unblocks** slice 6 of the line-218 entry (the integration step now has the typechecker-layer hook ready; codegen-side integration may not even be needed since the typechecker rejects unsafe captures before codegen sees them).
     - **3b.** [x] **`par {}` block boundary — shipped 2026-06-03.** Hook added at the `ExprKind::Par(block)` arm in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs` (was a pass-through `self.infer_block(block)`): it calls a new `check_cross_task_safe_par_block` *before* `infer_block` pushes the par block's own scope, so the `flatten_local_scope_snapshot` captures the enclosing scope. The check reuses the slice-3a `collect_captures_block` walker (no visibility change needed — the new method lives in the same `cross_task_check.rs` module as the walker, and is `pub(super)` so the `exprs.rs` sibling submodule can call it) and the `is_cross_task_safe_with` predicate. Bindings introduced inside a branch (`let` in the par body) are shadow-tracked by the walker, so only values flowing in from outside are flagged. Diagnostic reuses `emit_cross_task_unsafe` with site label `par {}` → `error[E_NOT_CROSS_TASK]: capture of \`p\` (type \`*mut u8\`) cannot cross a par {} task boundary …`.

       **Scope corrected from the original sketch ([[reproduce_before_trusting_bug_diagnosis]] / design.md authority).** The sketch's negative test — reject a `shared struct` capture in a par block with the `SharedToPar` fix-it — is **wrong**: it conflicts with design.md § Rc vs Arc — Two-Phase Algorithm (line 8181), which gives `shared struct` / `shared enum` a **sole-ownership carve-out** at a par-block boundary (a value moved into *exactly one* branch is safe; only multi-branch sharing is an error). A naive type-only check fired on the sole-branch case, breaking the shipped `tests/ownership.rs::test_concurrent_shared_struct_silent_when_only_one_branch_uses` (caught it on the first full-suite run). The branch-precise determination already belongs to the **ownership phase**'s `E_CONCURRENT_SHARED_STRUCT` / `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` pass (`src/ownership/concurrent_shared.rs`), which counts per-branch uses. So 3b **defers** any unsafe path rooted at a shared struct/enum leaf (`fix_it == SharedToPar`) to that pass, and catches only the leaves with **no** carve-out: `Rc[T]`, `OnceCell[T]`, raw pointers (design.md line 1407 for OnceCell, line 8197 for the Rc / par-region-escape pass; design.md lines 3505 / 8845 list par-block as one of the five check sites). Division of labor: shared struct/enum → ownership phase (aliasing-aware); Rc/OnceCell/raw-ptr → 3b (categorical, type-only). Rc/OnceCell aren't directly nameable in user kara at v1, so the user-nameable negative is a raw pointer.

       **5 tests** in `tests/typechecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 170 slice 3b` section: `par_block_capturing_primitive_only_accepted` + `par_block_two_readers_of_vec_capture_accepted` (positives — safe types, incl. one binding read by two branches); `par_block_capturing_raw_pointer_rejected` (negative — `*mut u8` → `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK`, `par {}` site label, Atomic/channel fix-it); `par_block_sole_branch_shared_struct_deferred_to_ownership_phase` (layering guard — sole-branch `shared struct` type-checks clean, pinning the deferral); `par_block_local_let_shadows_outer_capture` (regression — inner `let p` shadows an outer `*mut u8`, walker drops it from the capture set). Files: `src/typechecker/cross_task_check.rs` (new `check_cross_task_safe_par_block` method + `CrossTaskUnsafeFixIt` import + sole-ownership-carve-out gate), `src/typechecker/exprs.rs` (Par-arm hook), `tests/typechecker.rs` (5 tests + section comment). Gates: typechecker 1396/1396, ownership 275/275, cross_task_safe 14/14, full non-codegen suite green; fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs: default / llvm / lljit_prototype, `--all-targets`) clean.
     - **3c.** [x] **`Channel.send` across boundary + `with_provider[R](provider, closure)` — shipped 2026-06-03.** Both sites reject the concrete value/provider type via `is_cross_task_safe_with`, sharing a new `emit_cross_task_unsafe_value` helper (`cross_task_check.rs`) that renders the same `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` type-path/fix-it diagnostic as the spawn/par sites but for value-transfer sites with no captured binding name.

       **Design call — reject-on-type, NOT flow-gated (the open question from the 3b summary, resolved by design.md authority).** The original entry bundled the two sites as "both need par-region escape analysis." Reproduction + design.md make that unnecessary: design.md line 1407 (a value "sent through a `Channel[OnceCell[T]]`" is rejected) and line 7213 ("a `with_provider[R](provider, …)` call where the concrete `provider` value's type contains any not-cross-task-safe type … is rejected at the call site") both specify a **type-only** rejection on the element/provider type — no Sender-flow tracking. And unlike a `par {}` branch, **neither site has a sole-ownership carve-out**: a channel hands its value to an unknown receiving task (and may send repeatedly), and a provider is shared with a closure body that may run across spawned tasks. So both reject the **full** cross-task-unsafe set — `shared struct` / `shared enum` included (no `SharedToPar` deferral, in contrast to 3b). This also matches the precedent already at the `Sender.send` arm (the slice-2 `ScopeLocalEscape` check is itself unconditional/type-only).

       **`Channel.send`** (`src/typechecker/stdlib_io.rs::infer_channel_method`): after the existing `ScopeLocalEscape` (`TaskHandle`) check, run `is_cross_task_safe_with` on the channel element type; on failure emit via `emit_cross_task_unsafe_value("value sent across a channel", …)`. **`with_provider`** (`src/typechecker/expr_call.rs::infer_call`): the common surface is the **call form** `with_provider[R](provider, closure)`, which parses as `Call(Index(Ident|Path("with_provider"), R), [provider, closure])` — NOT `ExprKind::Providers` (that variant is the `providers { R => p } in { body }` *block* form). The original entry's "hook `infer_method_call`" sketch was wrong about the AST shape; the recognizer mirrors the interpreter's `match_with_provider` and runs at the top of `infer_call` alongside the 3a `spawn` check. The block form is also covered (the `ExprKind::Providers` arm in `exprs.rs`), replacing the historical "Send + Sync on the provider type" deferral comment there (the closed enumeration is the v1 mechanism — no auto-trait infrastructure to wait on, per design.md line 7213 / `docs/deferred.md`).

       **6 tests** in `tests/typechecker.rs` (slice-3c section): `channel_send_safe_element_accepted`; `channel_send_shared_struct_element_rejected` (E_NOT_CROSS_TASK + `channel` + `par` fix-it); `channel_send_vec_of_shared_struct_rejected_transitively`; `with_provider_plain_struct_provider_accepted`; `with_provider_shared_struct_provider_rejected` (names `provider for resource \`UserDB\``); `with_provider_provider_with_raw_pointer_field_rejected` (transitive raw-ptr field). Files: `src/typechecker/cross_task_check.rs` (`emit_cross_task_unsafe_value`), `src/typechecker/stdlib_io.rs` (channel element check), `src/typechecker/expr_call.rs` (with_provider call-form recognizer + check), `src/typechecker/exprs.rs` (Providers block-form check + import). Gates: typechecker 1402/1402, full non-codegen suite (62 binaries) green; under `--features llvm` / `lljit_prototype`: full cli 333/333 (build-E2E with_provider paths), codegen provider 19, provider_escape 8, lljit_prototype 16, lljit_e2e 15, repl 134, plus full codegen suite; fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs, `--all-targets`) clean. **Closes the boundary-site enforcement entry (all five sites live).**
  4. [x] **Diagnostic shape (`E_NOT_CROSS_TASK`) — multi-line refactor — shipped 2026-06-03.** The single-line shape now renders as the design.md three-line shape: an `error` line (site-specific lead clause + `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` code), a `note` line (`type \`T\` reaches \`<leaf>\` at <path>` — the type-path location of the unsafe leaf), and a `help` line (the type-swap fix-it). Implemented via approach (b) — a shared `format_cross_task_diagnostic` helper in `src/typechecker/cross_task_check.rs` newline-joins the three lines into the existing `TypeError.message` string, so **no diagnostic-carrier refactor across the ~315 `type_error` call sites was needed**: the cli text renderer (`print_text_diagnostics`) prints embedded newlines as-is, and the JSON renderer escapes them, so downstream consumers still pivot on the `E0254` code + fix-it text. Both the capture sites (`emit_cross_task_unsafe`, with the `{spawn|par {}|TaskGroup.spawn}` lead) and the value-transfer sites (`emit_cross_task_unsafe_value`, with the channel-send / provider lead) route through the shared helper. All slice 3a/3b/3c tests pass unchanged (every asserted token preserved across the reflow); 2 new tests pin the three-line structure (`cross_task_diagnostic_renders_error_note_help_lines`, `cross_task_diagnostic_value_site_renders_three_lines`). The rustc-style `-->` source-caret block (design.md line 9507) is a separate rich-renderer concern out of scope here — the labelled error/note/help lines are the v1 shape. The fix-it replacement table is the one in `src/cross_task_safe.rs::CrossTaskUnsafeFixIt::help_text`: `Rc[T]` → `Arc[T]`, `shared struct/enum X` → `par struct/enum X`, `OnceCell[T]` → `OnceLock[T]`, raw pointers → "wrap in `Atomic[*mut T]` or transfer through a channel".
  5. [x] **Borrow-rule consolidation at spawn boundaries — verified 2026-06-03 (within the v1 § 8506 model).** Confirmed the existing live-range / concurrency analysis produces the right diagnostics for the par-boundary borrow cases — no new borrow-checker pass added. **Scope correction surfaced during verification (important):** the four-case borrow rule's "shared ref" row (design.md § 9476: *multiple sibling tasks may simultaneously hold `ref T`*) is the **target** model, NOT v1 behavior. v1's ownership phase implements the stricter design.md § 8506 rule: a non-`par` struct reachable from 2+ `par {}` branches is rejected (`E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` / `…SHARED_STRUCT`) **regardless of borrow mode** — two shared `ref` reads of a struct binding across siblings are rejected, not accepted. Deliberate + tested (`tests/ownership.rs::test_concurrent_plain_struct_fires_via_inline_closure` uses `ref Counter` and expects the error to fire). Reconciled in design.md with a "v1 implementation status" note after the § 9476 borrow-rule table. The permissive shared-`ref`-reader model is gated on `par struct` landing (see the `par struct`-parser-gap entry below — not implemented at v1). **Verified diagnostics** (`tests/ownership.rs`, new `Phase 6 line 170 slice 5/6` section): sole-branch `mut ref` use accepted (`par_sole_branch_mut_ref_use_accepted`); `mut ref` write + `ref` read across siblings rejected, firing `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` (`par_mut_ref_plus_read_across_siblings_rejected` — NOT the standalone "cannot borrow as immutable in branch 2" wording the slice-6 sketch predicted; the conservative concurrent-struct rule is the operative diagnostic, pinned so a future move to the § 9476 model is a visible change); primitives read in both branches accepted (`par_primitive_used_in_both_branches_accepted`). Owned-move-into-two-branches + sole-branch-move + closure-mediated cases were already covered by the existing `test_concurrent_{plain,shared}_struct_*` cluster.
  6. [x] **Test coverage — completed 2026-06-03 for the v1-reachable subset; remainder gated (tracked).** The slice-6 matrix as originally sketched presupposes (a) the § 9476 permissive model (two `ref` readers *accepted*) and (b) types not constructible at v1 — so it cannot be asserted verbatim. **What IS covered now:** cross-task-safe *capture/transfer* sites — `spawn` / `TaskGroup.spawn` (slice 3a), `par {}` (3b), `Channel.send` + `providers`/`with_provider` (3c) — with positive (primitive, Vec[primitive]) + negative (shared struct, raw pointer, transitive `Vec[*mut u8]` / struct-field) cases and the three-line diagnostic (slice 4), all in `tests/typechecker.rs`; plus the par borrow-rule cases in slice 5 above (`tests/ownership.rs`) and the pre-existing `test_concurrent_{plain,shared}_struct_*` cluster (owned-move conflicts fire, sole-branch accepts, fix-diffs). **Gated rows (NOT asserted; each blocked on a missing feature, not on this slice):** "two `ref` readers accepted" + `par struct` accept → blocked on the § 9476-model decision and `par struct` implementation (design.md note + parser-gap entry below); `spawn(|| use_arc(arc))` / `Arc[T]` accept → `Arc` has no constructible stdlib surface at v1 (the walker treats `Arc[T]` inner as safe — covered structurally in `tests/cross_task_safe.rs`, just not via user source); `Rc[Cache]` / `OnceCell[i32]` / `Box[Rc[i32]]` rejection → `Rc` / `OnceCell` are not directly nameable in user kara source at v1 (per the slice-1 deferred-test note; the walker's transitive rejection of these is covered structurally in `tests/cross_task_safe.rs`). When `par struct` + the § 9476 model land, the "multiple readers" + `par struct`-accept rows become assertable; when `Rc` / `OnceCell` / `Arc` gain user surface, their source-level rejection/acceptance rows do too. No silent gap — every unasserted row maps to a named blocker.

  **Phase target:** Phase 6 (alongside the `spawn() / TaskGroup runtime + codegen + stdlib` entry directly below — the typechecker check has a stub in Phase 5.2 that fires `error[E_NOT_CROSS_TASK_SPAWN_NOT_YET]` until Phase 6 ships the full check). Bidirectional reference: the spawn entry's slice 6 cites this entry as the cross-task-safety boundary check that fires on every `TaskGroup.spawn(closure)` site. No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 48 ships the full structural-list at v1; user-defined cross-task-unsafe types via an explicit marker is a v2 RFC if a workload demands it.

- [x] **`par struct` / `par enum` — the type kind is COMPLETE; shipped 2026-06-03 across Slices A–D.** Parses → typechecks (field constraints + `mut self`) → cross-task-safe-by-definition (incl. § 9476 multi-reader) → compiles to running binaries with atomic refcount → formats + catalogs. **The *concurrent-mutation* use case depends on a separate feature, not `par struct` itself** — the concurrency-primitive surface, tracked as its own entry below ("Concurrency-primitive construction + usability"). Progress there (all 2026-06-04): `Atomic.new` in general position + `Atomic`-field load/store/`fetch_add`/`fetch_sub` on a `par`/`shared` field receiver all work — so the **lock-free concurrent counter is fully realized**: `par struct Counter { count: Atomic[i64] }`, `self.count.fetch_add(1, MemoryOrdering.SeqCst)` in a `ref self` method, incremented from two `par {}` branches 50_000× each → exactly 100_000, no lost updates. The full atomic RMW family is now done too (`swap` / `fetch_and|or|xor` / `compare_exchange` — incl. a CAS-loop lock-free counter, 2026-06-05). What remains for the `Mutex` half of concurrent mutation: `Mutex.new` + `lock` blocks. An *immutable-field* `par struct` was already fully usable. Surfaced while verifying the cross-task-safe slice 5/6 above. `parse_item` (`src/parser/items.rs`) has a `Token::Shared` arm (→ `shared struct`/`shared enum`) but **no `Token::Par` arm**: a leading `par` at item scope falls through to the `_ => None` fallback, which returns no item *and emits no error* (the guard only errors when attributes/`pub`/`private` precede it). The item loop then re-dispatches on the following `struct`/`enum` token, so **`par struct Foo { … }` silently parses as a plain `struct Foo { … }`** — the `par` keyword is dropped with no diagnostic. (`StructDef.kind_keyword_span`'s doc already anticipates a "future `par`" keyword; the AST/typechecker carry no `is_par` flag, and `StructInfo` has only `is_shared`.) **Impact:** `par struct` — the design's mechanism for *intentional* concurrent struct sharing (Arc + `Atomic`/`Mutex` fields, always cross-task-safe per design.md § 9498) — does not exist at v1, which is *why* the conservative § 8506 concurrency model (reject any non-`par` struct reachable from 2+ `par {}` branches) is the operative one and the § 9476 "multiple sibling `ref` readers" allowance is unreachable (see the design.md reconciliation note + slice 5/6 above). **Minimum fix — SHIPPED 2026-06-03 (`fc680120`), SUPERSEDED by Slice A.** The first landing added a `Token::Par` arm to `parse_item` that emitted a loud `par struct`/`par enum` not-yet-supported error (anchored at the `par` keyword via a new `Parser::error_at`) and recovered by parsing the body as a plain definition. Slice A (below) replaced that error arm with a real `par`-definition parse + `is_par` flag, so the not-supported error and its `error_at` helper no longer exist; the four interim `tests/parser.rs` § 2.4b tests were rewritten to assert real parsing (see Slice A). **Full feature** (a `par struct` kind through parser → `is_par` on `StructDef`/`StructInfo` → Arc-always + `Atomic`/`Mutex` field constraints → codegen → exempt from `E_CONCURRENT_*` + cross-task-safe-by-definition → mode-aware § 9476 borrow refinement) is the multi-slice effort below, a prerequisite for the permissive concurrent-read model. Tracked per [`feedback_surfaced_bugs_tracked_or_fixed`](../../CLAUDE.md) + [`feedback_blockers_get_own_tracker_entries`](../../CLAUDE.md).

  **Sub-slices.**

  - **A.** [x] **Slice A — definition-site guarantee (typechecker-only) shipped 2026-06-03.** The structural compile-time guarantee that is `par struct`'s entire value proposition (design.md § "Part 5b: Concurrent Shared Types (`par struct`)"). **Parser + AST:** the `Token::Par` arm (which the minimum fix added as a loud not-supported error) now parses a real definition — `is_par: bool` added to `StructDef` / `EnumDef` (mutually exclusive with `is_shared`; the `par` keyword span threads into `kind_keyword_span`), `parse_struct_def` / `parse_enum_def` gain an `is_par` parameter, the `Token::Par` arm mirrors `Token::Shared`. The minimum fix's `Parser::error_at` helper is removed (its only consumer was the now-replaced error arm). **Typechecker threading:** `is_par` flows onto `StructInfo` / `EnumInfo` (all 6 `env_build.rs` construction sites; the 2 stdlib-default sites carry `false`). `par struct` / `par enum` values lower to `Type::Shared(name)` — same as `shared`, because both are reference-semantics handle types with identical type-system treatment (pass-by-handle-clone, no exclusive ownership; design.md § Part 5b "Passing to functions"). The Rc-vs-Arc and cross-task distinctions are made via `StructInfo.is_par` in later slices, **not** a new `Type::Par` variant — avoiding churn across every `Type` match site. (`fields.rs` construction-site + `lowering.rs` annotation-site twins both gate on `is_shared || is_par`.) **Field-constraint check** (`typechecker/items.rs::check_par_field_constraints`, run from the `StructDef` / `EnumDef` arms of `check` for `is_par` types only): every `mut` field must be `Atomic[...]` or `Mutex[...]` (final-path-segment match, generic args not inspected — the wrapper provides the sync); a bare `mut val: i64` is rejected with `ParFieldNotConcurrent` (`E0257`) anchored at the `mut` keyword span; immutable fields are unrestricted; `par enum` runs the check once per struct-shaped variant (mut variant fields parse + are checked). **`mut self` rejection** (`check_impl_block`): an inherent-impl method on a `par` type declaring `mut ref self` is rejected with `ParMutSelfReceiver` (`E0258`) — `par` values are always Arc with potential multiple holders, so the exclusive mutable borrow is never available; `ref self` and consuming `self` stay legal (trait impls are exempt — their receiver shape is fixed by the trait decl). **New `Mutex[T]` stdlib stub** (`runtime/stdlib/mutex.kara`, type-shape only like `atomic.kara`; wired into `STDLIB_SOURCES` / `PRELUDE_TYPES` / `stub_generics`) so the field constraint can name a real type; `lock`-block typecheck + `Mutex.new` land in Slice D. **Tests:** 5 parser tests (`tests/parser.rs` § 2.4b — par struct/enum parse with `is_par`, `pub par struct`, plain/shared-are-not-par regression, `par fn` still errors) + 10 typechecker tests (`tests/typechecker.rs` § par struct slice A — Atomic/immutable/Mutex accept, bare-mut struct + enum-variant reject, `mut ref self` reject, `ref self`/consuming-`self` accept, shared/plain-struct regression that the check is par-only). Gates: parser 642/642, typechecker 1418/1418, full non-codegen suite (62 binaries) + `--features llvm` (62 binaries) green; fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs, `--all-targets`) clean. **No codegen** — `par struct` values reaching codegen would currently take the plain-stack-struct path (`is_shared=false`); no codegen test exercises them, and Slice C wires always-Arc lowering. **Cross-slice note:** because par values lower to `Type::Shared`, the cross-task-safe pass (`cross_task_safe.rs`) would currently *reject* a par value at a task boundary — Slice B teaches it to exempt `is_par`; until then no test puts a par value across a boundary.
  - **B.** [x] **Slice B — concurrency integration shipped 2026-06-03.** `par struct` / `par enum` are now exempt from the concurrency rules, so they cross parallel-region boundaries freely (design.md § Part 5b > "Crossing parallel region boundaries"). **`E_CONCURRENT_*` exemption** (`ownership/concurrent_shared.rs::classify_binding_type`): an `is_par` struct / enum returns `None` (untracked) — a `par` binding reachable from 2+ sibling `par {}` branches is safe by definition, not an `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` / `…SHARED_STRUCT` error. The `is_par` check precedes the `is_shared` branch (the two are mutually exclusive; ordering makes the exemption explicit). **Cross-task-safe-by-definition** (`cross_task_safe.rs::walk`): the early-hit `Type::Shared(name)` arm — which par values reach because Slice A lowers them to `Type::Shared` — now returns `Ok` when the named type `is_par` (looked up in `struct_info` / `enum_info`), and only `Err(SharedToPar)` for a genuine single-task `shared` type. Returns `Ok` explicitly (the recursive match marks `Type::Shared` `unreachable!()`, so fall-through would panic). Defensive `is_par` guards also added to the transitive `Type::Named` struct/enum branches (par types normally arrive as `Type::Shared`, but the guard keeps the invariant explicit). This is the cross-slice fix the Slice A note flagged (par values were lowering to `Type::Shared` and would otherwise have been rejected at every task boundary). **Tests:** 3 ownership (`tests/ownership.rs` — par struct + par enum reachable-from-2-branches accepted, shared-struct-still-fires regression) + 2 typechecker (`tests/typechecker.rs` — par struct accepted at `spawn` + `TaskGroup.spawn`, alongside the existing shared-struct rejection) + 2 walker (`tests/cross_task_safe.rs` — `par struct` / `par enum` via `Type::Shared` is safe). Gates: ownership 283/283, typechecker 1422/1422, cross_task_safe 18/18, full non-codegen (62 binaries) + `--features llvm` (62 binaries) green; fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs, `--all-targets`) clean. **Known gap (not Slice B's scope):** `par enum` values move on reuse rather than clone-on-pass — `shared enum` has the same pre-existing limitation (clone-on-pass reference semantics for enums isn't wired in the move checker); the par-enum exemption test uses `ref` params to be reachable-from-2-branches without move. Full enum reference semantics ride along with Slice C's codegen. **Blocked-by:** Slice A. ✓
  - **C.** [x] **Slice C — codegen (always-Arc) shipped 2026-06-03.** `par struct` / `par enum` now compile to running binaries. **Key realization** (much smaller than the original estimate): a `par` type reuses the *entire* shared-struct codegen machinery — identical `{ i64 refcount, … }` heap layout, `malloc`, field access, method dispatch, construction, pattern match, drop — because both lower to `Type::Shared`. The **only** semantic difference is that the refcount header is mutated **atomically** (`atomicrmw`, via the already-existing `emit_arc_inc` / `emit_arc_dec`) instead of plain load/add/store. **No new runtime symbols** — the refcount is inlined LLVM IR. **Edits:** (1) `is_par: bool` on `SharedTypeInfo` (`codegen/state.rs`); (2) the `shared_types` registration gate widened to `s.is_shared || s.is_par` for structs (`declarations.rs` ~303) and `e.is_shared || e.is_par` for enums (~2744), capturing `is_par`, with `EnumLayout.is_shared` set to `is_shared || is_par` (it means "reference-semantic heap pointer" at its read sites); (3) `heap_type_is_par(heap_type)` helper + the name-keyed `emit_refcount_inc` / `emit_refcount_dec` dispatchers route to the atomic path for par types (`runtime.rs`); (4) new **by-type** dispatchers `emit_refcount_inc_by_type` / `emit_refcount_dec_by_type` for the sites that hold a heap pointer but no binding name — the drop-walk inner-handle decs (`synth_drop.rs` ×3), the `Option`-inner / field-store refcount ops (`expr_ops.rs` ×6), and the `Map` value-half dec (`runtime.rs`). **The inner-handle routing is a real correctness fix, not just symmetry:** the drop walk of a `par` object decrements the inner handles it owns, and a `par` inner may still be live in another task even when the outer object hit refcount 0 — so that inner dec MUST be atomic. **`par` gets conventional `Option` layout (no niche)** — niche is a `shared`-only optimization at v1; conventional layout is always correct (niche-for-`par` is a Slice D follow-up). **Tests (`tests/codegen.rs`, 9):** IR-level — par struct inc is `atomicrmw add` (not `add i64 %rc`), par struct dec is `atomicrmw sub` + `@free`, par enum emits `atomicrmw`, **shared struct stays non-atomic (regression)**; E2E (real compiled binaries) — par struct basic / aliased+passed-to-fn / across-`par {}`-block / par enum tuple-variant / **recursive par struct (inner-handle atomic drop)**. Gates: codegen + all `--features llvm` binaries green; fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs, `--all-targets`) clean. **Parity notes (pre-existing, not par-specific):** `Enum.Variant(args)` qualified construction + struct-variant literals are broken for *all* enum kinds (plain / shared / par) — par enum reaches exact parity with shared enum (bare variant names work). `par`/`shared` enum values still move-on-reuse (the Slice B reference-semantics gap). **Blocked-by:** Slice A. ✓
  - **D.** [x] **Slice D — § 9476 borrow refinement + polish shipped 2026-06-03.** **§ 9476 permissive concurrent-read model — now LIVE for `par`** (and confirmed): multiple sibling `ref` readers of the *same* `par struct` binding across `par {}` branches are accepted. This needed no new code — Slice B's blanket `E_CONCURRENT_*` exemption for `par` types already delivers it (a `par` binding is untracked, so any borrow mode across siblings passes). Pinned by `tests/ownership.rs::par_struct_multiple_sibling_ref_readers_accepted`; the design.md § 8506/§ 9476 reconciliation note (design.md ~line 9482) is updated to record the model as live for `par` while the stricter § 8506 rule keeps governing non-`par` structs. **Formatter** (`src/formatter/items.rs`): the `format_struct` / `format_enum` `is_shared` arms gained an `else if is_par` branch — `karac fmt` was silently dropping the `par` keyword (a *semantics-changing* rewrite of `par struct` → plain `struct`); 2 round-trip tests in `tests/parser.rs`. **Catalog** (`src/catalog.rs`): `render_struct` / `render_enum` emit a `"par": true` kv alongside the existing `"shared": true`. Gates: full non-codegen (62 binaries) + `--features llvm` green; fmt + clippy (×3 cfgs) clean. **Deferred to their own entries (NOT `par struct`-owned):** (1) **`lock`-block typecheck + codegen + `Mutex.new` + `Atomic.new` in general expression position** — the construction/usability surface for `Atomic`/`Mutex` *fields*; this is the concurrent-mutation blocker, tracked as the "Concurrency-primitive construction" entry below. (2) **`weak par` references** — `weak par Foo` syntax (parallel to `weak shared Foo`); an extension, deferred (no workload yet). (3) **niche optimization for `par` `Option` fields** — `par` uses conventional `Option` layout; niche is a `shared`-only optimization, a perf follow-up (conventional layout is always correct). **Blocked-by:** Slices A–C. ✓

- [~] **Concurrency-primitive construction + usability (`Atomic.new` / `Mutex.new` / `lock` blocks / atomic RMW / `MemoryOrdering`) — the *concurrent-mutation* `par struct` enabler (surfaced 2026-06-03).** This is the **concurrency-primitive** surface, orthogonal to `par struct` (which owns the *type kind*, now complete) — `par struct` consumes these for its `mut` fields. `Atomic[T]` / `Mutex[T]` are nameable field types (Slice A baked the `Mutex[T]` shape; `Atomic[T]` predates it). Tracked per [`feedback_blockers_get_own_tracker_entries`](../../CLAUDE.md). **Bidirectional ref:** the `par struct` entry above cites this as the concurrent-mutation enabler; this entry's primary consumer is `par struct` `Atomic`/`Mutex` fields. **Memory-ordering note:** the atomic ordering enum is `MemoryOrdering` (`Relaxed`/`Acquire`/`Release`/`AcqRel`/`SeqCst`), distinct from the comparison `Ordering` (`Less`/`Equal`/`Greater`) — `x.load(MemoryOrdering.SeqCst)` is the form.

  - [x] **`Atomic.new` in general expression position — shipped 2026-06-04.** `Atomic.new(v)` is now recognized as a constructor in general expression position (struct-field-init, local `let`, call args), not just module-binding init — so `par struct Counter { count: Atomic[i64] }` can be *constructed* via `Counter { count: Atomic.new(0) }`. Typechecker-only fix: a new arm in `src/typechecker/expr_call.rs::infer_call` (next to the `Vec.filled` arm) returns `Type::Named { name: "Atomic", args: [type_of(arg)] }`; codegen already handled `Atomic.new` (transparent wrapper → lowers to the inner value, `Atomic[bool]`→i8) at `assoc_call.rs`. `Mutex.new` is deliberately NOT included — it has no codegen yet (rides with the `lock`-block item below), and typechecking it without codegen would turn a clean typecheck error into a codegen failure (guarded by `mutex_new_in_general_position_still_rejected`). Tests: 3 typechecker (`tests/typechecker.rs`) + 1 codegen E2E (`tests/codegen.rs` — par struct with an `Atomic` field constructs + runs). Gates: full non-codegen (62) + `--features llvm` (62) green; fmt + clippy ×3.
  - [x] **Atomic method dispatch on a `shared`/`par` struct *field* receiver — shipped 2026-06-04.** `self.count.load(MemoryOrdering.SeqCst)` / `.store(v, ..)` where `self.count` is an `Atomic` field of a `shared`/`par` struct now works. Previously failed codegen with `struct '<T>' has no LLVM type (shared structs not supported as Atomic field receivers)` — `resolve_atomic_storage`'s `FieldAccess` arm (`src/codegen/method_call.rs`) only looked in `struct_types` (plain structs); shared/par structs live in `shared_types` with a `{ i64 refcount, fields... }` heap layout. **Fix:** a shared/par branch at the top of that arm uses `shared_type_for_expr(inner)` + `compile_expr(inner)` (which yields the heap pointer, correctly handling the `ref self` ptr-to-heap-ptr load — reusing the *proven* shared field-read deref from `expr_ops.rs::compile_field_access`, so no segfault-prone hand-rolled self-ptr dance) + `build_struct_gep` at `idx + 1` (index 0 is the refcount). **Pre-existing and shared-wide** — the same fix lights up `shared struct` Atomic fields too (the identical error fired there). Tests (`tests/codegen.rs`, 3 E2E): par struct Atomic field set/get round-trips 10→42; shared struct Atomic field load (the shared-wide regression); par struct Atomic field read across a `par {}` block. Gates: non-codegen (62) + `--features llvm` green; fmt + clippy ×3.
  - [x] **Atomic read-modify-write ops — COMPLETE (`fetch_add`/`fetch_sub` 2026-06-04; `swap`/`fetch_and`/`fetch_or`/`fetch_xor` 2026-06-05; `compare_exchange` 2026-06-05).** **Single-operand family** — `fetch_add`/`fetch_sub`/`fetch_and`/`fetch_or`/`fetch_xor`/`swap` each lower to one LLVM `atomicrmw` (`add`/`sub`/`and`/`or`/`xor`/`xchg`, via `inkwell`'s `build_atomicrmw`) and return the **previous** value. Integer-only except `swap` (also works on `Atomic[bool]` via the i1↔i8 widen/trunc dance). **`compare_exchange(old, new, success, failure) -> Result[T, T]`** (deferred.md § Atomic Operations line 311) — lowers to LLVM `cmpxchg`, which returns `{ T, i1 }` (loaded value + success flag). The Kāra surface returns `Ok(prev)` on a successful swap / `Err(actual)` otherwise. **Key trick:** both Result arms carry the *same* payload (the loaded value) and differ only in tag, and Result's tags (`Ok=1`/`Err=0`) equal `zext(success_i1)` exactly — so the `Result[T,T]` aggregate is built directly with no branch: `tag = zext(success)`, payload word 0 = loaded value (zero-filled tail). **Typechecker** special-cases `compare_exchange` in `infer_method_call` to return `Result[inner, inner]` (the other atomic methods stay on the lax `Type::Error` path; `compare_exchange` can't, since a `match`-able `Result` scrutinee is needed); checks the 4-arg shape. **failure ordering** rejects `Release`/`AcqRel` (LLVM forbids them on the no-store path). v1 restricts `compare_exchange` to non-bool integer `T` (bool-CAS Result round-trip is a noted follow-on). Interpreter parity for all ops in `src/interpreter/method_call_optres.rs`. **Two lock-free counters proven end-to-end:** the direct `fetch_add` counter and a `load`+`compare_exchange` **CAS retry loop**, each run concurrently from two `par {}` branches 50_000× → exactly 100_000, no lost updates. Tests: codegen IR (each op → its `atomicrmw`/`cmpxchg`) + E2E (counter accumulate; concurrent no-lost-updates for both `fetch_add` and CAS-loop; bitwise/swap semantics; `Atomic[bool]` swap latch; CAS success/fail via `match Ok/Err`); typechecker (`compare_exchange` → `Result[i64,i64]`, binds to annotation, wrong-arg-count rejected). Gates: non-codegen (62) + `--features llvm` green; fmt + clippy ×3. **Atomic RMW is done** — `fetch_nand`/`fetch_max`/`fetch_min` are the only LLVM `atomicrmw` opcodes not surfaced, additive if a workload needs them.
  - [~] **`Mutex.new` + `lock`-block typecheck + codegen — Slices 1–2 shipped 2026-06-05 (standalone Mutex + par-struct Mutex FIELD locking, spinlock, straight-line); ref-param/early-exit follow-ons remain.** A real `Mutex[T]` now exists: layout `{ i64 lockflag, T value }` (`llvm_type_for_type_expr`), `Mutex.new(v)` general-position constructor (typecheck arm shared with `Atomic.new` in `expr_call.rs`; codegen builds the `{0, v}` aggregate in `assoc_call.rs`), and `lock m [alias] { body }` (`ExprKind::Lock`) fully wired: **typecheck** (`exprs.rs` — resolves `m` to `Mutex[T]`, binds the alias / shadows the mutex name as the inner `T`, rejects early exits + non-Mutex + borrowed-Mutex targets); **codegen** (`method_call.rs::compile_lock_block` — a **TAS spinlock**: acquire by `atomicrmw xchg`-ing field 0 to 1 and spinning until the prev value was 0, expose field 1 as a `mut ref T` body binding via a `VarSlot` whose ptr is the value field, release by atomic-storing 0); **interpreter** parity (new `Value::Mutex`; `lock` binds the inner value + writes back). **Both `lock m x { … }` (alias) and `lock m { … m … }` (mutex-name-shadows-inner) forms work.** **Proven concurrent:** a standalone local `Mutex[i64]` shared across two `par {}` branches (par captures the local by reference to the same aggregate) — 2×50_000 `lock`-guarded increments → exactly 100_000, no lost updates. **Slice-1 deferrals (each rejected cleanly at typecheck, or tracked):** (a) **early `return`/`break`/`continue` in a lock body** — rejected with `E0259 LockEarlyExit` (slice 1 emits the release only on the straight-line fall-through; release-on-all-paths needs the scope-exit-cleanup hook, a follow-on); panic is moot under `panic = "abort"` (process dies, no unwind). (b) **`lock` on a borrowed `ref`/`mut ref Mutex` parameter** — rejected (`LockTargetNotMutex`, "borrowed"); needs ref-indirection + the value-type at the lock site. (c) **`lock self.field`** — **SHIPPED in Slice 2 (below).** (d) **spinlock** — correct but burns CPU under contention; a blocking/futex mutex is a perf follow-on. Tests: typechecker (alias binds inner, no-alias shadows, early-exit/non-Mutex/borrowed rejected, `Mutex.new` accepted) + codegen IR (`atomicrmw xchg` + `store atomic`) + E2E (single-threaded alias+no-alias 10→30; concurrent Mutex counter 100_000). Gates: non-codegen (62) + `--features llvm` green; fmt + clippy ×3.

    **Slice 2 — `lock` on a place expression (par-struct Mutex FIELD locking) shipped 2026-06-05.** `ExprKind::Lock.mutex` changed from a bare `String` to a place expression `Box<Expr>`, so `lock self.state s { … }` now locks a `Mutex` field of a `par`/`shared` struct — the canonical concurrent-mutation pattern. **Parser** (`parser/exprs.rs`): parses the base (`self` or an identifier) + a `.field` chain, then the optional alias (a trailing IDENT with no leading `.` disambiguates `lock a.b c` from `lock a.b.c`). **Resolver / typechecker / formatter / interpreter / free-ident collector** updated for the Expr-shaped place (most of the ~50 `ExprKind::Lock` match sites use `{ body, .. }` and were untouched). **Typechecker:** infers the place type → `Mutex[T]`; a **field place requires an alias** (no name to shadow) — `lock self.state { }` is rejected. **Codegen** (`compile_lock_block` + new `resolve_mutex_storage`): an `Identifier` place uses the var slot (the aggregate); a `FieldAccess` place reuses the atomic-field deref (`shared_type_for_expr(inner)` + `compile_expr(inner)` heap ptr + GEP `field_idx+1`) to reach the `Mutex` aggregate stored inline in the par struct's heap layout, then spinlocks as before. **Proven concurrent:** a `par struct Counter { total: Mutex[i64] }` passed by value (Arc-shared) into two `par {}` branches, each `lock self.total`-incrementing 50_000× → exactly **100_000, no lost updates**. Also fixed a pre-existing formatter bug (`lock` emitted a bogus `as` keyword). Tests: parser (place forms — identifier/field/no-alias) + typechecker (field-place-with-alias accepted, field-without-alias rejected) + codegen E2E (sequential `lock self.total` → 42; concurrent field counter → 100_000). Gates: non-codegen (62) + `--features llvm` green; fmt + clippy ×3. **Interpreter gap — now FIXED** (par-struct field mutation via `ref self` persists in `karac run` too; see the standalone entry below). **Sequential ref-param locking SHIPPED 2026-06-05:** `lock m` where `m: ref`/`mut ref Mutex[T]` is now accepted — codegen loads through the reference (recovering the `{ lockflag, value }` struct type from `ref_params`, which stores the pointee `BasicTypeEnum` for ref params) then spinlocks; the typechecker unwraps the borrow to the inner `T`. Verified E2E (`fn bump(m: mut ref Mutex[i64], n) { lock m x { x = x + n; } }` → 15). Tests: typechecker (accept) + codegen E2E (15). **Remaining `lock` follow-ons:** (i) **concurrent standalone-Mutex** — a bare `Mutex` local shared across `par {}` branches: the ownership checker's `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` rule treats `Mutex`/`Atomic` as plain structs (should EXEMPT them — they are cross-task-safe), and it is currently *inconsistent* (a direct `lock m` in two branches slips through and runs; `bump(mut m)` in two branches is rejected); even if accepted, par doesn't share a local borrowed by `mut` into a branch-called fn (a separate par-capture gap). The clean concurrent path is a **`par struct` Mutex field** (Slice 2, works). Tracked as its own entry below. (ii) **early-exit-in-body** (release-on-all-paths) — **investigated 2026-06-05; deliberately kept as the clean `E0259 LockEarlyExit` rejection.** The natural implementation is a `CleanupAction::ReleaseMutex { flag_ptr }` pushed onto the lock body's `compile_block_with_frame` cleanup frame: on normal fall-through `drain_top_frame_with_emit` releases it, and an early `return` releases it because the return path runs `emit_scope_cleanup` (full-stack walk). **The blocker:** `compile_break` / `compile_continue` (`src/codegen/control_flow.rs`) do **NOT** emit scope cleanup — they branch straight to the loop's break/continue target. So a `break`/`continue` out of a lock body inside a loop would skip the release → **deadlock** for the next acquirer. This is a *broader* pre-existing gap (break/continue also skip RC-dec / Vec-free cleanup, leaking heap on loop exit); release-on-all-paths for `lock` requires fixing break/continue cleanup emission generally — its own slice. A `return`-only partial implementation would be a deadlock footgun for `break`/`continue`, so the clean rejection (with the trivial "compute inside the lock, exit after" workaround) is the correct v1 posture. (iii) **blocking mutex** (spinlock → futex, perf).

- [x] **Interpreter: par-struct field mutation via `ref self` now persists — fixed 2026-06-05.** Surfaced while verifying the `lock self.field` slice: `karac run` of `let c = C { n: Atomic.new(0) }; c.add(42); c.get()` returned `0` (silently un-mutated). **Two root causes, both fixed (`src/interpreter.rs` + `interpreter/method_call_optres.rs`):** (1) the struct-literal evaluator gated `SharedStruct` (Arc-backed, reference-semantic) construction on `def.is_shared` only — a **`par struct` (`is_par`) fell through to a value-copied `Value::Struct`**, so each `ref self` call mutated a throwaway copy. Widened to `def.is_shared || def.is_par`. (2) a par struct's `Atomic`/`Mutex` fields are NOT declared `mut` (the primitive provides interior mutability), so they landed in `immutable_fields` (no cell) — added `is_interior_mutable_field_type` so `Atomic[..]`/`Mutex[..]` fields are stored in `mut_fields` (`RwLock` cells) regardless of the `mut` keyword. (3) the `Atomic`-method write-back (`store`/`fetch_*`/`swap`/`compare_exchange`) only wrote back for an `Identifier` receiver — added `atomic_write_back` which routes a `FieldAccess` receiver (`self.n`) through `set_field` so the write lands on the shared cell; the `lock` write-back (already via `set_field`) persists too once the field is a cell. **Verified via `karac run`:** par-struct Atomic field (`fetch_add`/`store`), par-struct Mutex field (`lock`), and the `shared struct` `mut`-field regression all persist. Tests: 4 in `tests/interpreter.rs`. Gates: non-codegen (62) + `--features llvm` green; fmt + clippy ×3. The compiled path was already correct; this brings the interpreter to parity. (Other `shared struct` interpreter-parity gaps — aliased / recursive / field-held — are separate, pre-existing, untouched.)

- [ ] **Ownership: `Mutex[T]` / `Atomic[T]` should be exempt from `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` (standalone concurrent use); + par-capture of a `mut`-borrowed local (surfaced 2026-06-05).** Surfaced while shipping ref-param `lock`. A bare `Mutex`/`Atomic` **local** shared across `par {}` branches is treated by the ownership checker (`ownership/concurrent_shared.rs`) as a plain struct subject to `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` — but `Mutex`/`Atomic` are **cross-task-safe synchronization primitives** and should be exempt (the way `par struct` is, Slice B). Today the rule is **inconsistent**: `par { lock m {…}; lock m {…} }` (direct lock in two branches) *slips through* and runs correctly — `lock` isn't classified as a conflicting reach — but `par { bump(mut m); bump(mut m) }` (the same mutex via a `mut`-ref fn arg) IS rejected, because the `mut`-ref argument is counted as a reach. **Two coupled gaps:** (1) the exemption — add `Mutex`/`Atomic` to the cross-task-safe set in `classify_binding_type` so a standalone concurrency-primitive local crossing `par {}` is allowed consistently; (2) **par-capture of a `mut`-borrowed local** — even with the exemption, `par` does not share a local that a branch passes by `mut` into a function (each branch operates on a copy → updates lost; the `par`-capture classifier captures by value through the `mut`-arg path). **Impact:** concurrent locking of a *standalone* `Mutex` local is unreachable (the idiomatic concurrent path — a **`par struct` Mutex field** — works correctly and is the recommended pattern; see the `lock`/`Mutex` entry above). Sequential ref-param locking works. **Note:** the direct-`lock`-in-`par`-branch slip-through means `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_concurrent_mutex_counter_no_lost_updates` exercises a program `karac check` does not currently reject — once the exemption lands cleanly, that test's program becomes well-formed under `check` (it already produces the right answer via `karac build`, which bypasses the ownership pass). Tracked per [`feedback_surfaced_bugs_tracked_or_fixed`](../../CLAUDE.md) + [`feedback_blockers_get_own_tracker_entries`](../../CLAUDE.md). **Reproduced + re-scoped 2026-06-05 (do not ship gap 1 alone):** ran all three forms against the current `karac`. Direct `lock m {…}` in two `par` branches: `check` passes, runtime prints `100000` over 3 runs — **fully correct** (the existing `test_e2e_concurrent_mutex_counter_no_lost_updates` is non-vacuous). `par struct` Mutex field: correct. The `bump(mut m)` standalone form: `check` rejects it today, and when forced through `karac build` (which bypasses the ownership pass) it prints **`0`** — every update lost. **This is the load-bearing finding: the two gaps are coupled, and the exemption (gap 1) is UNSAFE in isolation** — it would turn today's loud `E_CONCURRENT_PLAIN_STRUCT` rejection into a silent print-`0` miscompile for the `bump(mut m)` form. Gap 1 must NOT land without gap 2. **Gap 2 root cause (located):** `src/codegen/par_blocks.rs:~553` captures *every* outer binding **by value** (`build_load` the binding into the per-branch env-struct), so a `Mutex` reached through a `mut`-ref fn arg inside a branch operates on a per-branch copy — neither write reaches the original `m`. Direct in-branch `lock m` works precisely because that path resolves the mutex storage differently (not through the by-value `mut`-arg capture). **Fixing gap 2 = changing par-capture semantics** (selectively capture mutated/locked primitives by pointer), which is the capture path *every* `par` program depends on → high regression blast-radius for a niche payoff: the `bump(mut m)` standalone form is the ONLY thing gated, and the two idiomatic concurrent paths (direct in-branch `lock`, par-struct Mutex field — the design's recommended pattern) already work. **Disposition: deferred, not a quick win.** Correct ship order when picked up: gap 2 (par-capture-by-pointer for locked/mutated cross-task-safe primitives) FIRST and proven via the `bump(mut m)` E2E returning the right count, THEN gap 1 (the `classify_binding_type` exemption) so `check` accepts it. The current loud rejection is the safe interim posture.

- [x] **P0 — `spawn() / TaskGroup` runtime + codegen + stdlib — COMPLETE 2026-06-05 (all sub-slices landed).** v1 launch-gating prereq for the two server-shaped v1 flagship demos — `Flagship Demo 1` (idle-holder) and `Flagship Demo 2: Parallax` (complete). (The data-engineering pipeline, once "Flagship Demo 3", is still V1-scope but not runtime-gating in the same way — its design now lives in the roster at `docs/dogfooding.md § Weave`.) **Status as of 2026-05-27**: slices 1–5 + slice 7 shipped end-to-end (stdlib surface → ScopeLocal enforcement → runtime scheduler pool → codegen spawn-call lowering → TaskGroup.drop wait-for-children → E2E smoke). **Slice 6 closed 2026-06-05** — its integration was already delivered by the line-170 `Cross-task-safe set + structural Send replacement` entry's slice 3a (shipped 2026-05-27, that whole entry COMPLETE 2026-06-03): the `spawn` / `TaskGroup.spawn` cross-task-safe boundary check fires at the *typechecker* layer (`src/typechecker/cross_task_check.rs`), which strictly subsumes the codegen-side hook this slice originally imagined — unsafe captures are rejected before codegen runs. Verified 2026-06-05 in both `karac check` AND `karac build` (a `TaskGroup.spawn(|| use_it(c))` capturing a `shared struct` is rejected with the three-line `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` diagnostic; no binary emitted). The "multi-week effort" framing predated line-170's completion; the integration is 0 new LoC + the existing 8 slice-3a typechecker tests, plus one build-pipeline defense-in-depth regression test added here (`tests/spawn_e2e.rs::test_spawn_unsafe_capture_rejected_before_codegen` — pins that the rejection survives the exact phase chain codegen runs, guarding against a future refactor moving the check to a pass `build` skips, cf. the line-390 ownership-bypass footgun). Parent now flips to `[x]`. **End-to-end working today**: `let mut tg = TaskGroup.new(); tg.spawn(|| worker()); /* tg drops, joins worker */` compiles + runs + produces correct stdout in `tests/spawn_e2e.rs`. Design spec lives at `design.md § Explicit Concurrency: par {} and spawn()` (lines 9273–9377). The seven sub-slices below take the design from spec to shipped — sequenced so each landing point is verifiable in isolation. **The work is multi-week — no shortcut path; "build a `WebSocket.serve(addr, handler)` builtin that hides the multiplexing in Rust" was explicitly considered and rejected per `feedback_no_workarounds_fix_compiler` — the demo's purpose is to prove the Kāra story holds, not to wrap a Rust runtime in Kāra syntax.**
