  **Architectural shape (locked design choices).** One scheduler pool per process; one OS thread per CPU core; each thread runs an event-loop-driven worker that picks up ready state machines via the existing `EventLoop`/`karac_park_on_fd` plumbing in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs`. `spawn(closure)` lowers to a state-machine constructor call (mirrors the existing `karac_park_on_fd` constructor pattern in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`) that registers the new state machine with the scheduler's queue. `TaskGroup.drop` blocks until every child task's state machine reports completion; cancellation propagates by flipping the same per-`ParCall`-style `AtomicBool` cancel flag the existing `karac_par_run` path uses. Reuses every existing runtime primitive (`EventLoop`, `karac_park_on_fd`, state-machine ABI, cancel-flag plumbing); the missing piece is the dynamic-spawn registration + worker-pool driver. **What's distinct from `karac_par_run`:** `par_run` fans out a statically-known set of branch fns from a single call site and joins synchronously; `spawn` registers a dynamically-created state machine that can outlive any single call site within its `TaskGroup` scope, and the join barrier moves to `TaskGroup.drop` rather than the call site.

  **Sub-slices.**

  1. [x] **Slice 1 — `TaskGroup` / `TaskHandle` / `spawn` stdlib surface (typechecker-only landing) shipped 2026-05-27.** New `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara` (~165 LoC with architecture comments) declaring `struct TaskGroup { id: i64 }`, `struct TaskHandle[T] { task_id: i64 }`, `impl TaskGroup { fn new() -> TaskGroup; fn spawn[T](mut ref self, f: Fn() -> T) -> TaskHandle[T]; }`, `impl[T] TaskHandle[T] { fn join(self) -> T; }`, `impl Drop for TaskGroup { fn drop(mut ref self) {} }`, and the free fn `fn spawn[T](f: Fn() -> T) -> TaskHandle[T]`. All methods carry `#[compiler_builtin]` with stub bodies (mirror `tcp.kara` / `ws.kara`). Wired into the prelude via three additions in `src/prelude.rs`: `STDLIB_SOURCES` entry baking `task_group.kara` via `include_str!` next to `ws.kara`; `TaskGroup` / `TaskHandle` added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` for scope-0 visibility; `spawn` added to `PRELUDE_FUNCTIONS` for bare-identifier resolution. **Deviation from the pre-ship plan: no `with E` effect-polymorphism on free fns.** The plan declared the signatures with `with E` per design.md § Explicit Concurrency lines 9337 + 9357–9366; v1 stdlib ships WITHOUT `with E` because free-fn effect-polymorphism is not typechecker-supported today (same constraint that gates `Server.serve[E](handler: Fn(Request) -> Response with E)` per the http.kara comment block at lines 188–191). The spawned closure's effects propagate via normal effect inference on the closure body, which is the same path `Server.serve` uses; when free-fn `with E` ships, the signatures lift additively to the design.md shape. **Stub-body shape:** `TaskHandle.join` ends in `loop { }` (a divergent expression that satisfies the `-> T` typechecker contract without representing a value of T); the constructors return `TaskHandle { task_id: 0 }` / `TaskGroup { id: 0 }` literals codegen will replace in slice 4. **No `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK_SPAWN_NOT_YET` typechecker stub to drop** — the pre-ship plan referenced an imagined Phase 5.2 stub, but a code-search across `src/` showed it never actually existed; that text was forward-looking documentation, not code. The walker side (`is_spawn_callee` in `src/ownership/par_helpers.rs` — shipped 2026-05-18) recognises bare `spawn` as a par-region boundary independently of resolution, so the boundary-detection behaviour is unchanged by this slice. **6 new tests** in `tests/typechecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 218 slice 1: TaskGroup / TaskHandle[T] / spawn` section: `task_group_new_returns_task_group` (scope-0 visibility + assoc-fn dispatch); `task_group_spawn_returns_task_handle_of_closure_return_type` (T binds from the closure's return type at the call site); `task_handle_join_returns_inner_type` (consume-by-value receiver + return-type binding from LHS annotation); `free_fn_spawn_returns_task_handle` (bare-identifier spawn resolves to the stdlib free fn); `task_handle_inner_type_mismatch_rejected` (binding `TaskHandle[String]` to `spawn(make_int)` errors with a type mismatch); `task_group_canonical_accept_loop_shape_compiles` (the design.md § Explicit Concurrency lines 9357–9366 accept-loop shape, modulo the renamed `tg` binding because `group` is a lexer keyword — `Token::Group` is used by `effect group` / layout-block groupings). **One test updated:** `drop_method_keys_empty_when_no_drop_impl` extends its stdlib-drop-types allowlist from `["TcpListener", "TcpStream", "WebSocket"]` to add `"TaskGroup"`. **One negative test omitted, documented inline:** "binding `String` to `h.join()` where `h: TaskHandle[i64]` should type-error" — the typechecker today does NOT bind `T` on `impl[T] TaskHandle[T] { fn join(self) -> T }` from the receiver's instantiated type; instead, `T` is inferred from the calling context (the LHS annotation), so the mismatch is silently absorbed. Verified the same limitation affects `Pool[T].acquire(...) -> Result[PooledConnection[T], PoolError]` today (probe: `let r = p.acquire(0);` where `p: Pool[i64]` errors with "cannot infer type parameter 'T'" rather than pinning T=i64 from the receiver), so this is a pre-existing typechecker limitation, not new debt from this slice. **Surface gap surfaced during the slice (out of scope here, worth a typechecker follow-on if a workload surfaces it):** the `impl[T] Type[T] { fn m(self) -> T }` shape doesn't bind T from the receiver in current method dispatch. Call sites with annotation (`let v: i64 = h.join()`) work correctly today; only sites without annotation (`let v = h.join()`) trip the limitation. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test` (1262/1262 typechecker + all other test binaries) and `cargo test --features llvm` (2731/2731 codegen + memory_sanitizer + all other binaries) pass with zero regressions. Files: `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara` (new, ~165 LoC), `src/prelude.rs` (~25 lines net — STDLIB_SOURCES entry + two prelude-list additions + cross-ref comments), `tests/typechecker.rs` (~95 lines net — 6 new tests + slice section comment + drop-method-keys allowlist update). **What slice 1 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-on slices of this entry): ScopeLocal marker trait + typechecker enforcement (slice 2 — escape rejection in three positions); runtime scheduler pool (slice 3); codegen `spawn()` call lowering (slice 4); `TaskGroup.drop` LLVM body hand-rolling (slice 5); cross-task-safe boundary check integration (slice 6 — pairs with the line-170 entry's sub-slices); end-to-end accept-loop smoke (slice 7).

  2. [x] **Slice 2 — `ScopeLocal` marker trait + typechecker enforcement shipped 2026-05-27.** `pub marker trait ScopeLocal;` + `impl[T] ScopeLocal for TaskHandle[T] {}` declared at the bottom of `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara`. `ScopeLocal` added to `PRELUDE_TRAITS` in `src/prelude.rs` for scope-0 visibility. New `TypeErrorKind::ScopeLocalEscape` variant (`E0253` per `src/cli.rs`). **Walker (`src/typechecker/items.rs::check_scope_local_escape`)** runs alongside `check_signature_visibility` and mirrors its structure — same `check_type_expr_*` recursion shape over `TypeKind::Path` / `Tuple` / `Array` / `Pointer` / `Ref` / `MutRef` / `MutSlice` / `Weak` / `FnType` / `ImplTrait` / `Dyn` — but keys off a `collect_scope_local_types: HashSet<String>` populated from `impl ScopeLocal for T {}` blocks across user `program.items` AND every entry in `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` (the baked stdlib's impl blocks don't get spliced into `program.items` so the walker reaches into STDLIB_PROGRAMS explicitly, same precedent as `raii_check::collect_cancel_unsafe_annotations`). **Three position checks (a/b only — c lives elsewhere):** (a) every `Item::Function` return type (regardless of `is_pub` — escape is escape, a private fn returning a TaskHandle is still leaking it past the spawning scope); (b) every `Item::StructDef` field type + `Item::EnumDef` variant payload / variant-field type; (a-extension) every `Item::ImplBlock` method return type. **Parameter positions are intentionally skipped** — passing a TaskHandle into a same-scope helper is the normal usage pattern (`tg_spawn_helper(mut tg, conn)`). **(c) Channel send check** fires at `src/typechecker/stdlib_io.rs::infer_channel_method`'s Sender.send arm — when the channel's element `Type::Named` matches the v1 ScopeLocal hardcoded set (currently just `"TaskHandle"`), emit `ScopeLocalEscape` against the call span. v1 ships with a hardcoded set rather than a dynamic walker at the dispatch point because (i) ScopeLocal is sealed per design.md (users cannot `impl ScopeLocal for MyType`), so the set is closed and known to the compiler; (ii) per-call lookup against a HashSet would be wasteful when the v1 set has one entry. When a second stdlib ScopeLocal type lands (RAII critical-section guards, scope-bound iterators per design.md), it joins the hardcoded match and the items.rs walker picks it up via the impl block automatically. **Sealing — convention, not enforced.** v1 documents that users cannot `impl ScopeLocal for MyType` in the marker trait's comment block (`runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara`); typechecker rejection of non-stdlib impls is a small follow-on if a workload surfaces a need (a `is_sealed_marker_trait()` check in `env_add_marker_trait` would do it). **8 new tests** in `tests/typechecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 218 slice 2: ScopeLocal marker + enforcement` section: `scope_local_local_bind_and_join_accepted` (positive — local bind + .join() are still first-class); `scope_local_returning_task_handle_from_fn_rejected` (return-type rejection); `scope_local_returning_task_handle_from_private_fn_rejected` (rule applies regardless of visibility); `scope_local_task_handle_in_struct_field_rejected` (struct field rejection); `scope_local_task_handle_in_enum_variant_payload_rejected` (enum variant payload rejection); `scope_local_task_handle_through_channel_send_rejected` (Sender.send rejection); `scope_local_passing_task_handle_to_helper_accepted` (positive — parameter position intentionally not checked); `scope_local_other_types_not_rejected` (regression guard — Vec / String / Holder { v: Vec, s: String } stays clean). **One slice-1 test updated:** `task_group_canonical_accept_loop_shape_compiles` previously used a helper `fn tg_spawn_helper(tg: mut ref TaskGroup, c: TcpStream) -> TaskHandle[i64]` to call `tg.spawn` — that helper now violates the slice-2 rule (return-type-is-ScopeLocal). Rewrote the test to match the actual design.md § Explicit Concurrency lines 9357-9366 shape: `tg.spawn(make_zero);` discards the TaskHandle inline. This is the correct canonical pattern — the design's `loop { let conn = listener.accept()?; group.spawn(|| handle_client(conn)) }` discards the spawn result on every iteration; the TaskGroup's drop is what joins. The slice-1 test was a synthetic helper-call shape that didn't reflect real usage; the rewrite is closer to the actual demo-1 spec. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test` (50/50 test binaries green) and `cargo test --features llvm` (6237/6237 tests green) pass with zero regressions. Files: `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara` (+~30 lines net — slice 2 status comment update + `marker trait ScopeLocal;` + `impl[T] ScopeLocal for TaskHandle[T] {}` + sealing comment block), `src/prelude.rs` (~10 lines net — `ScopeLocal` added to `PRELUDE_TRAITS` with cross-ref comment), `src/typechecker.rs` (~12 lines net — new `ScopeLocalEscape` variant + match-arm addition in the diag-class classifier + `self.check_scope_local_escape()` call wired into `Typechecker::check()`), `src/typechecker/items.rs` (~190 lines net — `collect_scope_local_types` + `check_type_expr_scope_local` + `check_scope_local_escape` + section comment), `src/typechecker/stdlib_io.rs` (~25 lines net — Sender.send arm extended with the hardcoded ScopeLocal check), `src/cli.rs` (~7 lines net — `E0253` error-code mapping for the new variant), `tests/typechecker.rs` (~135 lines net — 8 new tests + section comment + 1 slice-1 test rewrite). **What slice 2 does NOT cover** (carried as follow-on / reserved): (1) Structural seal enforcement — users can write `impl ScopeLocal for MyType` and the typechecker accepts it today (the impl just adds MyType to the dynamic walker's set; users get the same escape rejection rule as TaskHandle). Documenting the v1 convention rather than blocking via typechecker rejection because the soundness impact of an extra opt-in is "more rejections, which is conservative". (2) Generic-bound `impl[T: ScopeLocal] X for Vec[T]` — the walker only matches single-segment `TypeKind::Path` targets, same scope limit as `collect_cancel_safe_opt_ins`. Future ScopeLocal types that need bound-resolved opt-ins lift this when needed. (3) Type-tree transitivity — `Box[TaskHandle[i64]]` / `Vec[TaskHandle[i64]]` / struct fields holding `Box[TaskHandle]` aren't transitively checked. The v1 surface catches the direct positions; transitive walking is the same shape as the existing `is_cross_task_safe` precedent in design.md § Cross-task-safe set (line 170 entry, slice 2). When that lands, the same `is_cross_task_safe`-style walker can be re-applied here.

  3. [x] **Slice 3 — runtime scheduler pool shipped 2026-05-27.** New `runtime/src/scheduler.rs` (~430 LoC) wraps the existing global `Pool` from `lib.rs` (the same MPMC queue that `karac_par_run` / `karac_par_reduce` drain) with task-handle semantics for `spawn()`. **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** the plan called for per-worker work-stealing deques + a parallel pool. Shipped without that for two reasons: (i) the existing `Pool { queue: Mutex<VecDeque<Task>>, cv: Condvar }` already handles the slice-3 task surface (every `karac_runtime_spawn` builds a 1-task `Arc<ParCall>` with `remaining = 1` and pushes one `Task` onto the shared queue, reusing `execute_task`'s `FrameGuard` + `catch_unwind` + remaining-decrement-and-signal machinery); (ii) per-worker work-stealing is a measured optimization, not a v1-ship requirement — the 1M+ idle target referenced in the original plan is parked-task occupancy (event loop owns those, not the spawn pool), not active spawn-rate. Spawn dispatch shares OS threads with par-blocks instead of competing for them, which is the right v1 posture. The plan's `karac_runtime_scheduler_register(sm_ptr, scope_id)` FFI name was state-machine-shaped; the actual surface that slice 4's codegen calls is `karac_runtime_spawn(fn_ptr, env, result_size, result_align) -> *mut KaracTaskHandle` — a closure-shaped API that matches design.md's `fn spawn[T](f: Fn() -> T) -> TaskHandle[T]` signature and lets the runtime carry the Kāra-side `T` return value through a runtime-owned result buffer without monomorphization. **Emitted shape.** `KaracTaskHandle` holds `state: AtomicU8` (one of `TASK_STATE_*` discriminants 0/1/2/3 — pinned by `tests::task_state_constants_pinned`), `result_buf: *mut u8` + `result_layout: Layout` (pre-allocated `result_size`/`result_align` bytes; null for unit-returning tasks), per-task `cancel: AtomicBool` (always false in v1; slice 5's TaskGroup.drop will flip it), and Condvar machinery (`notify_mutex: Mutex<()>` + `notify_cv: Condvar`). `SpawnFn` typedef: `unsafe extern "C" fn(env, result_out, cancel)` — codegen at the spawn site emits a wrapper conforming to this shape that reads captures from `env`, runs the closure body, memcpys the T-typed result into `*result_out`. Four exported FFIs: `karac_runtime_spawn`, `karac_runtime_task_join` (blocks via Condvar, memcpys result on `COMPLETED`, frees the handle), `karac_runtime_task_handle_free` (drop-without-join — slice 5's TaskGroup cleanup routes through here), `karac_runtime_task_state` (non-blocking peek for tests + future polling APIs). `ParCall` / `Task` / `Pool` / `pool()` lifted from private to `pub(crate)` in `lib.rs` to let `scheduler.rs` reuse the dispatch path. **Panic propagation.** `TASK_STATE_PANICKED` is API-future-proofing for `catch_panic[T]` integration; under v1's `panic = "abort"` release profile a panicking SpawnFn aborts the process before reaching the terminal-state write (Rust auto-aborts panics crossing `extern "C"` boundaries regardless of profile). The `catch_unwind` in the spawn closure stays for symmetry with `execute_task` and to catch runtime-internal panics (allocator failure, lock poison). **8 new tests** in `scheduler::tests`: `spawn_and_join_returns_i64_result` (full roundtrip — env=41 → result=42); `spawn_returning_unit_uses_null_result_slot` (unit-return convention via shared `AtomicU32` env increment); `spawn_multiple_tasks_each_joins_independently` (64 concurrent spawns, sum verification = 2080); `task_state_observes_pending_then_completed` (state-machine surface peek); `task_handle_free_releases_without_join` (drop-without-join path); `null_handle_join_returns_cancelled` / `null_handle_state_returns_cancelled` (defensive null handling); `task_state_constants_pinned` (ABI regression guard against discriminant reordering). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (runtime crate 93 → 101 tests; all other test binaries unchanged). Files: `runtime/src/lib.rs` (~10 lines net — `pub(crate)` lifts on `ParCall`/`Task`/`Pool`/`pool()` + `pub mod scheduler;`), `runtime/src/scheduler.rs` (new, ~430 LoC), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (4 new table rows + section header for the scheduler module). **What slice 3 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-on slices): (1) per-worker work-stealing deques — measure global-queue contention as a real bottleneck first; (2) integration with state-machine-shaped poll-fn closures (spawn(closure-that-yields)) — codegen emits the wrapper, the wrapper drives the state-machine via the existing event-loop dispatcher; the runtime side is shape-agnostic so this lights up automatically once slice 4's codegen wiring lands; (3) `TaskGroup.spawn` (vs free-fn `spawn`) — slice 5 wires the TaskGroup container around the same `karac_runtime_spawn` symbol; (4) cancellation flag wiring — slice 5's TaskGroup.drop flips the per-handle cancel; (5) re-bench against alternative pool designs — measured-first, never speculative. **Unblocks** slice 4 (codegen `spawn()` call lowering — emits the wrapper, calls `karac_runtime_spawn`, stores handle ptr as i64 into `TaskHandle.task_id`, and emits `.join()` as a call to `karac_runtime_task_join`).

  4. [x] **Slice 4 — codegen `spawn()` call lowering shipped 2026-05-27.** New `src/codegen/task_group.rs` (~330 LoC) lowers `spawn(closure)` and `TaskGroup.spawn(closure)` call sites + the partial `TaskHandle.join()` surface. **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** plan called for synthesizing the closure body as a state machine via the same machinery as `karac_park_on_fd`-yielding callees. Shipped without that wiring because state-machine integration is a larger architectural surface (the spawn closure may or may not contain network-yield calls). The slice-3 runtime is closure-shaped, not state-machine-shaped — `karac_runtime_spawn(fn_ptr, env, result_size, result_align) -> *mut KaracTaskHandle` takes a `SpawnFn` (`unsafe extern "C" fn(env, result_out, cancel)`) wrapper codegen synthesizes per call site. Future state-machine-shaped closures slot in without ABI change. The plan's `karac_runtime_scheduler_register` FFI name was state-machine-shaped; actual shipped FFI matches the slice-3 closure-shaped surface. **Emitted shape.** Three artifacts per `spawn(closure)` call site: (1) a captured-env struct type `{ T0_cap, T1_cap, ... }` built from `collect_closure_free_vars`; (2) a synthesized `extern "C" fn __spawn_wrap_N(env, result_out, cancel)` that loads captures from `env`, runs the closure body with captures bound into `self.variables`, stores the T-typed result at `*result_out` (null-guarded), frees the env with `free()`, returns void; (3) at the outer site: `malloc(sizeof(env_struct))`, populate the heap env, `call ptr @karac_runtime_spawn(__spawn_wrap_N, heap_env, size_of(T), align_of(T))`, then `ptrtoint` the returned handle into the `TaskHandle { task_id: i64 }` struct's field 0. **`TaskHandle.join()`** extracts `task_id` (i64), casts back to `*mut KaracTaskHandle` via `inttoptr`, alloca's an out-slot, calls `karac_runtime_task_join(handle, out_slot) -> u8`, loads T from the slot. **v1 limitation on join return type T**: typechecker doesn't bind T from receiver per slice 1's gap; `recover_task_handle_join_return_ty` returns `i64` as the fallback. Documented inline that non-i64 join returns surface truncated reads — slice 4 ships the i64 minimum because the canonical accept-loop discards the TaskHandle inline (no `.join()`), and slice 5's TaskGroup.drop joins children without reading results. **Four FFI declarations** added to `Codegen::new`: `karac_runtime_spawn` (returns ptr), `karac_runtime_task_join` (returns u8), `karac_runtime_task_handle_free` (returns void), `karac_runtime_task_state` (returns u8). **Dispatch wiring.** `compile_call` adds an `if name == "spawn"` arm; `compile_method_call` adds two arms for `"TaskGroup.spawn"` (compiles + discards receiver) and `"TaskHandle.join"`. **5 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 218 slice 4` section: free `spawn(|| make_zero())` emits `call ptr @karac_runtime_spawn` + `call ptr @malloc`; wrapper has `void (ptr, ptr, ptr)` signature and `call void @free(ptr)` before ret; `tg.spawn(|| ...)` dispatches through the same lowering; `h.join()` emits `call i8 @karac_runtime_task_join` with `inttoptr` to recover the handle ptr; all four scheduler FFI declarations present (regression guard). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (codegen 829 → 834, typechecker 1270, cli 288, all binaries green). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (~60 lines — 4 FFI decls + `mod task_group;`), `src/codegen/task_group.rs` (new, ~330 LoC), `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (~9 lines — free-fn `spawn` arm), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (~30 lines — TaskGroup.spawn + TaskHandle.join arms), `tests/codegen.rs` (~145 lines — 5 new tests). **What slice 4 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-on slices): (1) bare-identifier closures (`let f = || ...; spawn(f)`) — lowering recognises closure literals only; (2) non-i64 join return types — needs `expr_types` threaded through lowering; (3) per-spawn cancel flag wiring — slice 5's TaskGroup.drop will flip the per-handle cancel; (4) state-machine-shaped closures that yield on network I/O — lights up automatically when the body's state-machine lowering composes with the wrapper's call site (runtime side is shape-agnostic); (5) TaskGroup-receiver self-aware spawn — slice 5 will route through the receiver's task-registry slot. **Unblocks** slice 5 (TaskGroup.drop wait-for-children + fail-fast cancel) and slice 7 (E2E accept-loop smoke).

[x] **Slice 5 — `TaskGroup.drop` = wait-for-all-children shipped 2026-05-27.** Closes the structured-concurrency loop: every `tg.spawn(closure)` child registers with the group; scope-exit drop blocks until every registered child reaches a terminal state. **Scope correction from pre-ship plan:** original called for fail-fast cancel propagation on child err/panic. Shipped without — v1's `panic = "abort"` aborts the process on any panicking SpawnFn (Rust auto-aborts panics crossing `extern "C"`), so the "any child panics" branch is unrecoverable anyway. Cooperative-cancel via user-callable `TaskGroup.cancel()` lands as slice 5b once `catch_panic[T]` is in play. v1 ships wait-for-all because that's the structurally-required boundary per design.md § Explicit Concurrency. **Runtime side.** New `KaracTaskGroupHandle { children: Mutex<Vec<*mut KaracTaskHandle>> }` in `runtime/src/scheduler.rs`; three FFIs: `karac_runtime_taskgroup_new() -> ptr` (Box::into_raw), `karac_runtime_taskgroup_register(group, child)` (push into Mutex<Vec>), `karac_runtime_taskgroup_join_and_free(group)` (drain outside the lock to avoid re-entrant-spawn deadlock; `karac_runtime_task_join(child, null)` per child blocks + frees handle, discards terminal status per wait-for-children-don't-collect-results contract; `Box::from_raw` group). **Codegen side.** Three new FFI declarations in `Codegen::new`. `compile_assoc_call` intercepts `TaskGroup.new()` and emits `call ptr @karac_runtime_taskgroup_new()` + `ptrtoint` into `TaskGroup { id: <i64> }`. `compile_method_call::TaskGroup.spawn` arm routes through new `lower_taskgroup_spawn(tg_val, closure)` which extracts the group pointer (i64 → ptr via inttoptr) and threads it through a refactored `lower_spawn_shared` helper that emits the spawn FFI + extra `call void @karac_runtime_taskgroup_register(group, child)` before the TaskHandle wrap. `synth_drop.rs::emit_hardcoded_stdlib_drop_bodies` adds a TaskGroup branch + new `emit_taskgroup_drop_body` hand-rolling `@TaskGroup.drop(self)` as load i64 from `self.id` → inttoptr → `call void @karac_runtime_taskgroup_join_and_free(group_ptr)` → ret. User-Drop dispatch chain (Prereq.1–5) synthesizes `@karac_drop_TaskGroup` calling `@TaskGroup.drop` at scope exit. **9 new tests** (5 runtime + 4 codegen IR-grep). Runtime: `taskgroup_new_returns_non_null_handle`, `taskgroup_drains_registered_children_on_join_and_free` (16-spawn fan-out with shared AtomicU32 counter — all children must complete before join returns), `taskgroup_join_and_free_handles_null_gracefully`, `taskgroup_register_null_inputs_are_no_ops`, `taskgroup_with_i64_returning_children_drains_correctly`. Codegen: TaskGroup FFI declarations present, `TaskGroup.new()` lowers to `karac_runtime_taskgroup_new` + ptrtoint, `tg.spawn(closure)` emits both `karac_runtime_spawn` and `karac_runtime_taskgroup_register`, `@TaskGroup.drop` calls `taskgroup_join_and_free` with inttoptr, scope-exit drop wraps the runtime join. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (codegen 834 → 839, typechecker 1270, runtime 101 → 106, all binaries green). Files: `runtime/src/scheduler.rs` (~130 lines net — KaracTaskGroupHandle + 3 FFIs + 5 tests), `src/codegen.rs` (~37 lines — 3 FFI declarations), `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (~28 lines — `TaskGroup.new()` arm), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (~7 lines — `TaskGroup.spawn` routes to `lower_taskgroup_spawn`), `src/codegen/task_group.rs` (~70 lines net — split `lower_spawn_call` into free + group flavors via shared `lower_spawn_shared`; group flavor adds registration call), `src/codegen/synth_drop.rs` (~75 lines — `emit_taskgroup_drop_body`), `tests/codegen.rs` (~95 lines — 4 new tests + section comment). **What slice 5 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-ons): (1) fail-fast cancel propagation (slice 5b — user-callable `TaskGroup.cancel()` + per-handle cancel-flag wiring); (2) child-result collection through TaskGroup (the design discards results — explicit `.join()` on individual handles is the collect surface); (3) re-entrant spawns from inside a child closure that target the parent's TaskGroup (works today via the drain-outside-the-lock discipline but no test covers it); (4) panic-to-user-kara propagation (under `panic = "abort"` the process aborts before drop runs — slice 5b's `catch_panic[T]` integration converts this to recoverable Err). **Unblocks** slice 7 (E2E accept-loop smoke test) and the line-170 demo entry's M1 milestone.

[x] **Slice 6 — Cross-task-safe boundary check at `spawn` sites — closed 2026-06-05 (satisfied by line-170 slice 3a; no codegen hook needed).** Original plan: wire `is_cross_task_safe(ty)` into the **codegen** `spawn` site so unsafe captures are rejected with `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK`. **What actually shipped — better than the plan:** the line-170 `Cross-task-safe set + structural Send replacement` entry's **slice 3a** (2026-05-27) put the `spawn` / `TaskGroup.spawn` boundary check at the **typechecker** layer (`src/typechecker/cross_task_check.rs`, firing from `infer_call` for bare `spawn` + `infer_method_call` for `TaskGroup.spawn`), which strictly subsumes a codegen-side hook — the typechecker rejects unsafe captures *before codegen ever sees them*. Slice 3a's own closing note predicted this: *"codegen-side integration may not even be needed since the typechecker rejects unsafe captures before codegen sees them."* **Reproduced + verified 2026-06-05** against the current `karac`: `tg.spawn(|| use_it(c))` capturing a `shared struct` → rejected with the full three-line `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` diagnostic under both `karac check` AND `karac build` (typecheck runs in the build path — unlike the ownership pass, which `build` was found to bypass per the line-390 entry); a primitive capture passes; no binary emitted on rejection. **Coverage:** the 8 slice-3a typechecker tests (positives: primitive / Vec[primitive] / no-capture; negatives: shared-struct + `SharedToPar` fix-it, raw pointer, transitive `Vec[*mut u8]`, struct-field path) cover spawn + TaskGroup.spawn; the `~50 LoC integration` estimate is moot (0 new integration LoC). **One genuinely-new test added** (`tests/spawn_e2e.rs::test_spawn_unsafe_capture_rejected_before_codegen`): a build-pipeline defense-in-depth guard — pins that the rejection survives the exact phase chain `compile_and_link` runs (parse → resolve → **typecheck** → lower → codegen → link) and emits no binary, so a future refactor relocating the check to a pass `build` skips would fail loudly. Gates: `--features llvm` spawn_e2e green; fmt + clippy ×3. **Closes** this entry AND flips the parent `[~]` → `[x]` (the P0 launch-gating prereq is complete).

[x] **Slice 8 — `spawn` slot widened to `OnceFn() -> T` shipped 2026-05-27.** Surfaced by the Demo 1 (line 170) slice-1 probe: the canonical accept-loop shape `loop { let ws = WebSocket.accept(listener); tg.spawn(|| handle(ws)) }` got rejected at the spawn-arg typecheck with `cannot pass once-callable closure where 'Fn() -> T' is expected ... (closure becomes once-callable because it consumes captured binding 'ws')`. The per-iteration `ws` is freshly bound and move-captured into the per-task handler — that's the semantically-correct ownership shape (each task owns its connection from spawn-time), so the closure is genuinely once-callable. The original `Fn() -> T` slot at `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara:116` and line 192 (per design.md line 9337) was the wrong contract: spawned closures execute exactly once on the worker pool (`karac_runtime_spawn` invokes once, never replays). **The fix** — three small changes: (1) `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara` lines 116 + 192 — `Fn() -> T` → `OnceFn() -> T` on both `TaskGroup.spawn` and free-fn `spawn`; (2) `docs/design.md` line 9337 — same swap in the spec signature; (3) `src/typechecker/inference.rs::unify_types` — new symmetric `Fn ↔ OnceFn` cross arm propagates substitutions across the upward-subtyping path that `is_subtype` accepts at the assignability layer, so a `Fn() -> i64` value passed where the slot is `OnceFn() -> T` correctly binds `T = i64` rather than falling through to the LHS-pinned `T` and silently widening. Without the unify cross arm, the `task_handle_inner_type_mismatch_rejected` regression guard (tests/typechecker.rs:19281) would flip from rejecting `let h: TaskHandle[String] = spawn(make_int)` to accepting it. **Three new regression tests** under `tests/typechecker.rs`'s "Phase 6 line 218 slice 8" section: `spawn_with_move_capture_accepted` (the Demo 1 motivating shape — closure that consumes a String capture), `free_spawn_with_move_capture_accepted` (parallel on free-fn spawn), `taskgroup_spawn_non_consuming_closure_still_accepted` (regression guard that the existing slice-7 fan-out shape still typechecks — closures like `|| worker(1)` that capture nothing still flow through). All four targeted tests green; full `cargo test --features llvm` 1283 typechecker tests + 839 codegen E2E tests pass with zero regressions. Files: `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara` (2-line surface change + ~17-line comment block documenting the rationale at the file-header `Slot type` section), `docs/design.md` (1 line at 9337), `src/typechecker/inference.rs` (24-line cross-arm + comment), `tests/typechecker.rs` (3 new test cases ~60 LoC). **Closes** the Demo 1 slice-1 typecheck blocker — the accept-loop probe now passes. Cross-link to `feedback_optimize_for_production_not_kata`: this is exactly the "demo IS the production workload" outcome where a v1-shape user workload (Demo 1's accept loop) surfaced a real semantic gap in the spawn surface that no existing test exercised (slice-7 e2e tests use only non-consuming closures like `|| worker(1)`).

  9. [x] **Slice 9 — stdlib struct-as-by-value-param LLVM ABI fix shipped 2026-05-27.** Second prereq Demo 1 (line 170) slice 1 surfaced. **Symptom.** A user fn taking `WebSocket` / `TcpStream` / `TcpListener` by value (`fn handle(ws: WebSocket) {} ... handle(ws);` — the canonical accept-loop handler shape) failed codegen with `Module verification failed: Call parameter type does not match function signature! %ws2 = load { i32 }, ptr %ws; i64 call void @handle({ i32 } %ws2)`. **Root cause.** `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs::llvm_type_for_name`'s fall-through default returns `i64` when a struct name isn't in `self.struct_types`. Codegen doesn't load *baked* stdlib struct definitions into `self.struct_types` (the value-site lowerings like `lower_websocket_accept` / `lower_tcp_listener_bind` hand-roll the struct shape inline via `context.struct_type(&[i32_type], false)`). So the function's *declared* LLVM signature widened to `i64` while the call site's *value* (loaded through the binding's alloca) kept the actual `{ i32 }` shape — LLVM verifier rejection. **The fix** — single arm added to `llvm_type_for_name` matching the existing baked-stdlib precedent (`String` / `Vec` / `VecDeque` / `Slice` each have an explicit arm above the fall-through): `"TcpListener" | "TcpStream" | "WebSocket" => self.context.struct_type(&[i32_type.into()], false).into()`. The three types are baked stdlib structs that all share the `{ fd: i32 }` shape per `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` + `ws.kara`. **Why not also TaskGroup / TaskHandle?** Existing slice-7 tests for `tg.spawn(|| worker(1))` already work — `tg` is exclusively accessed via `mut ref self` methods, never passed by value, so the i64 fall-through doesn't surface for those types. The arm can be added additively when a real workload passes them by value; deferring is the conservative call. **Why not load baked stdlib structs into self.struct_types?** That's the broader architectural fix and would unblock the deferred `stream.fd` field-access stdlib-types gap noted at `tests/ws_framing.rs:11–22`. The narrow ABI arm here is the surgical unblocker for Demo 1 slice 1; the broader load lands when a stdlib-type field access from kara source becomes a real demand. **Three new regression tests** under `tests/ws_framing.rs::ws_codegen_tests` — `test_ir_websocket_by_value_param_uses_struct_type`, `test_ir_tcpstream_by_value_param_uses_struct_type`, `test_ir_tcplistener_by_value_param_uses_struct_type` — each pins the function-signature shape `define internal void @handle({ i32 } ...)` end-to-end through codegen. All three green; full `cargo test --features llvm` 6306 tests pass (3 new + 6303 existing) with zero regressions. Files: `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (~22-line arm + comment), `tests/ws_framing.rs` (3 new test cases ~65 LoC). **Closes** the second Demo 1 slice-1 blocker — the demo's `tg.spawn(|| handle_connection(ws))` shape now builds end-to-end. Cross-link to `feedback_optimize_for_production_not_kata`: same outcome as slice 8 — Demo 1 surfaced a real codegen gap (single-i32-field stdlib structs as by-value params) that no existing test exercised because no kara source pre-Demo-1 ever passed a TcpStream / TcpListener / WebSocket as a function argument.

- [x] **P0 — TLS / HTTPS server-side stdlib — all 5 sub-slices shipped 2026-05-27.** Backing: **rustls** (0.23, `ring` crypto provider), not openssl — pure Rust, no external link dependency. Backed through `runtime/src/tls.rs`. The WebSocket / HTTP layer above is unchanged: `TlsListener` exposes the same `accept()` shape as `TcpListener` returning a `TlsStream` with the same `read` / `write` / `write_all` shape as `TcpStream`; `WebSocket.accept_tls(tls_listener)` (the parallel-method path chosen over `Acceptable`-trait generics at ship time per slice 3) gives WS-over-TLS. **Sub-slices:** 1 (rustls runtime FFI, `fcb1f90`), 2 (`TlsListener` / `TlsStream` stdlib types + codegen, `64eea9e`), 3 (`WebSocket.accept_tls` + TLS-aware WS framing, `b6cb841`), 4 (test-cert fixtures), 5 (design.md + Demo 1 slice 2 wss:// wire-up). **Verified end-to-end** via the Demo 1 wss:// smoke test (TLS handshake + WebSocket-over-TLS upgrade round-trip). **Unblocked** `Flagship Demo 1` slice 2 (line 138 above), now shipped. **Two follow-ons** below, both resolved 2026-05-27: (a) `FileSystem.read_to_string` codegen lowering (shipped); (b) the suspected match-arm-binding-as-tail-expression bug, which the (a) investigation proved was a **misdiagnosis** — the symptom was always (a)'s i64 scrutinee, not a binding-position bug. Neither ever blocked v1 TLS functionality.

  1. [x] **Slice 1 — rustls runtime FFI shipped 2026-05-27.** New `runtime/src/tls.rs` (~470 LoC + ~300 LoC tests) wrapping rustls's server-side `ServerConfig` / `ServerConnection` behind a C ABI keyed by the underlying TCP fd. **Dep additions** in `runtime/Cargo.toml`: `rustls = "0.23"` with `default-features = false, features = ["std", "tls12", "ring", "logging"]` (strips out `aws_lc_rs` which needs nasm; uses `ring` matching what `ureq` already pulls into the lockfile so no duplicate copy compiles) + `rustls-pemfile = "2"` for PEM parsing. **Dev-dep**: `rcgen = "0.14"` with `pem`/`ring`/`crypto` features for hermetic per-test self-signed cert generation (slice 4 ships checked-in fixtures later). **Six FFI symbols** all under `#[cfg(unix)]` matching the rest of the raw-fd surface: `karac_runtime_tls_config_new(cert_pem, cert_len, key_pem, key_len) -> *mut KaracTlsConfig` (parses PEM via `rustls_pemfile::certs` / `private_key`, builds config via `ServerConfig::builder_with_provider(ring) .with_safe_default_protocol_versions().with_no_client_auth().with_single_cert`); `karac_runtime_tls_config_free(*mut KaracTlsConfig)` (idempotent for null); `karac_runtime_tls_listener_bind(addr_ptr, addr_len, _config) -> i32` (delegates to `karac_runtime_tcp_bind` — config is unused at bind time, only consumed at accept; signature carries it through so slice 2's `TlsListener.bind_tls` doesn't need an asymmetric extra hop); `karac_runtime_tls_accept(listener_fd, config) -> i32` (raw `accept(2)` + synchronous `Connection::complete_io` handshake + registers `TlsSession` in per-fd registry, returns connection fd or `-1`); `karac_runtime_tls_read(fd, buf, len) -> i64` / `karac_runtime_tls_write(fd, buf, len) -> i64` (look up session via `Arc::clone`-out-of-`RwLock`-read pattern, lock inner `Mutex<TlsSession>`, drive rustls's `reader()` / `writer()` + `read_tls` / `write_tls` / `process_new_packets` loop, return decrypted-byte-count / encrypted-byte-count, negative-errno style on socket error, `-1` on protocol error or session miss); `karac_runtime_tls_close(fd) -> i32` (drops session from registry then closes underlying fd via `TcpStream::from_raw_fd` Drop — same convention as `karac_runtime_tcp_close`). **Session registry shape:** `RwLock<HashMap<i32, Arc<Mutex<TlsSession>>>>` behind an `OnceLock` (HashMap::new isn't const before 1.86 + this matches the existing `EVENT_LOOP` pattern in `event_loop.rs`); read/write paths take the outer RwLock read-lock briefly to clone the inner Arc, drop the outer lock, then lock the per-session Mutex — accept/close take the outer write lock for insert/remove. v1 scale (one I/O op per connection at a time, dispatched from the parking primitive) is fine with this; DashMap-style sharding lands when 100K+ concurrent ops surface contention. **Handshake & I/O posture (v1):** synchronous handshake inside `tls_accept` via `complete_io`; steady-state read/write blocks against the socket. Caller (slice 2's codegen lowerings) parks via `karac_park_on_fd(fd, dir)` BEFORE invoking — same convention as TCP. For M1's 100K-conn target the sync handshake is the limiting factor (occupies a worker thread per concurrent handshake); non-blocking handshake re-parking between rustls rounds is a separate slice if/when measurement shows handshake throughput dominates. **10 new unit tests** in `tls::tests` (gated `#[cfg(test)] #[cfg(unix)]`): `config_new_with_valid_pem_returns_non_null`; `config_new_with_garbage_cert_returns_null` + `config_new_with_garbage_key_returns_null`; `config_new_with_null_or_empty_returns_null` (3 null/zero-length paths); `config_free_handles_null` (idempotent); `round_trip_echo` (end-to-end — std `TcpListener` + a thread driving `tls_accept` + `tls_read` + `tls_write` + `tls_close`, against a `rustls::ClientConnection` driven from the main thread; echoes a 13-byte message and asserts equality); `handshake_failure_returns_minus_one` (raw TCP client sends non-TLS garbage → `tls_accept` returns `-1`); `read_write_on_unknown_fd_returns_minus_one` (registry lookup miss); `close_on_negative_fd_is_noop`; `listener_bind_delegates_to_tcp_bind`. All 10 green; runtime unit-test count went 106 → 116; full `cargo test --features llvm` (compiler + codegen + memory_sanitizer + runtime, all 9 binaries) passes with zero regressions. Files: `runtime/src/tls.rs` (new, ~770 LoC including tests + doc-comments), `runtime/src/lib.rs` (+1 line — `pub mod tls;`), `runtime/Cargo.toml` (+~12 lines — rustls + rustls-pemfile prod deps, rcgen dev-dep, with explanatory comments). **What slice 1 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-on slices of this entry): kara-side `TlsListener` / `TlsStream` types + codegen lowerings (slice 2); `WebSocket.accept` extension to TLS listeners (slice 3); checked-in test-cert fixtures (slice 4); `TlsError` kara-side enum (deferred to slice 2 where the call sites land — slice-1's `ConfigBuildError` is internal-only and the FFIs return null/`-1`). **Carried follow-ons surfaced during implementation:** (1) non-blocking handshake via re-park (M1 100K-conn throughput follow-on); (2) richer TLS-specific error variants (cert validation distinct from socket I/O) — v1 collapses to `-1` for protocol errors and `-errno` for syscall errors, matching the TCP precedent; (3) DashMap sharding on session registry when measurement shows lock contention. **Unblocks** slice 2 (the FFI surface this slice ships is exactly what slice 2's codegen lowerings call into).

[x] **Slice 2 — `TlsListener` / `TlsStream` stdlib types shipped 2026-05-27.** New `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara` (~155 LoC) declaring `struct TlsConfig {}` (opaque marker), `struct TlsListener { fd: i32, config: *mut TlsConfig }`, `struct TlsStream { fd: i32 }` plus `bind_tls` / `accept` / `read` / `write` / `write_all` `#[compiler_builtin]` methods. Both bodies dispatched from `emit_hardcoded_stdlib_drop_bodies` gated on `drop_method_keys.contains_key(...)`. **Error type — reusing `TcpError`.** v1 doesn't ship a distinct `TlsError` enum; cert / handshake / protocol failures all surface as `TcpError.Other(1)` via `wrap_tcp_io_result` (the `n = -1` non-syscall sentinel maps to errno=1, which doesn't match EINTR so falls into `Other`). A dedicated TlsError with `CertValidation` / `Handshake` / `Closed` variants is a slice-2 follow-on if a workload needs the structured distinction. **10 new codegen tests** in new `tests/tls_codegen.rs` under `tls_codegen_tests`: `test_ir_tls_runtime_ffis_declared` (all 7 FFI symbols present in module); `test_ir_tls_bind_tls_dispatches_to_runtime_ffis` (kara `bind_tls` → IR calls `_tls_config_new` + `_tls_listener_bind`); `test_ir_tls_listener_accept_parks_then_calls_runtime_ffi` (accept composes park-on-fd state machine + `_tls_accept`); `test_ir_tls_stream_read_dispatches_to_runtime_ffi` / `_write_dispatches_to_runtime_ffi` (read/write route to the right FFI); `test_ir_tls_stream_write_all_loops_via_runtime_ffi` (write_all emits the labelled `tls.wa.loop.head` BB); `test_ir_tls_listener_drop_frees_config_then_closes_fd` (drop wrapper + body emits config_free + close in order); `test_ir_tls_stream_drop_closes_fd` (TlsStream drop routes through `_tls_close`); `test_ir_tls_listener_by_value_param_uses_struct_type` (`{ i32, ptr }`) / `_tls_stream_by_value_param_uses_struct_type` (`{ i32 }`). **One typechecker test updated:** `drop_method_keys_empty_when_no_drop_impl` extends the `STDLIB_DROP_TYPES` allowlist from `["TcpListener", "TcpStream", "WebSocket", "TaskGroup"]` to add `"TlsListener"`, `"TlsStream"`. [x] **Slice 3 — `WebSocket.accept` over TLS shipped 2026-05-27.** Path (b) chosen — parallel `WebSocket.accept_tls(listener: TlsListener) -> WebSocket` method rather than trait-generic dispatch (Theme 6 trait-method codegen status was the deciding factor; the parallel method ships cleaner under the existing assoc-fn dispatch arms). **The slice was meaningfully larger than the tracker's ~80 LoC estimate** because the WS framing FFIs (`karac_runtime_ws_send_text` / `_recv_text` / control-frame handling) had to become TLS-aware: without that, a `WebSocket` produced by `accept_tls` would have plaintext bytes shoved straight at the TLS-encrypted socket, bypassing the rustls session and producing broken-on-the-wire output. The fix lifts the WS framing read/write helpers (`ws_read_exact_or_eof`, `ws_write_unmasked_frame`, `ws_write_masked_frame`, `ws_read_http_request`) to generic `<R: Read>` / `<W: Write>` / `<S: Read + Write>` bounds, then introduces a `TlsConnIo<'a>` adapter that wraps a borrowed `(&mut ServerConnection, &mut TcpStream)` pair into a `Read + Write` surface (`reader().read` pumps via `read_tls` + `process_new_packets` for the read side; `writer().write` then `wants_write()` drain via `write_tls` for the write side). The top-level FFIs `ws_send_data_frame` / `ws_recv_data_frame` check `tls::lookup_session(fd)` first — if the fd has a registered TLS session, route through `TlsConnIo`; otherwise the existing plain-TCP fast path. The reassembly state machine inside `ws_recv_data_frame` was hoisted into a new `ws_recv_data_frame_inner<S: Read + Write>(stream, ...)` helper (the closure-IIFE was unrolled so reborrows of `&mut *stream` work cleanly inside the parser body). **New FFI surface** in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs`: `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls(listener_fd, config) -> i32` — performs TCP accept, drives the rustls handshake via `complete_io`, calls `tls::register_session_for_fd(fd, conn)` to insert the session into the global `SESSIONS` registry BEFORE the HTTP upgrade exchange, then runs the WS upgrade handshake over the encrypted transport via the same `TlsConnIo` wrapper + a shared `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake<S: Read + Write>(stream)` helper (factored out of the inline body in `karac_runtime_ws_accept` for reuse — the plain-TCP path keeps its inline form for now since refactoring it would only save 10 LoC and risk regressions). **New runtime surface in `runtime/src/tls.rs`**: `TlsSession` and `TlsSession.conn` lifted to `pub(crate)` so `event_loop.rs` can borrow the `ServerConnection` for TLS-aware framing; new `pub(crate)` helpers `lookup_session(fd) -> Option<Arc<Mutex<TlsSession>>>`, `register_session_for_fd(fd, conn)`, and `clone_config_arc(config_ptr) -> Arc<ServerConfig>` — all called from `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls`. **Kara surface** in `runtime/stdlib/ws.kara`: new `#[compiler_builtin] fn accept_tls(listener: TlsListener) -> WebSocket with sends(Network) receives(Network)` method on `WebSocket` mirroring the existing `accept(listener: TcpListener)` shape. **Codegen lowering** in `src/codegen/tls.rs`: new `lower_websocket_accept_tls(listener_val)` — extracts `(fd, config_ptr)` from the TlsListener struct, emits the canonical `karac_park_on_fd` state-machine yield, calls `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls(fd, config)`, packs the returned conn fd into a `WebSocket { fd: i32 }` struct value (same shape as plain-TCP accept's return — so subsequent `recv_text` / `send_text` / Drop dispatch lands on the existing branches unchanged). **Dispatch wire-up** in `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs`: routes `WebSocket.accept_tls` to the new lowering. **One new FFI declaration** in `src/codegen.rs::Codegen::new`: `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls(i32, ptr) -> i32`. **4 new codegen tests** in `tests/tls_codegen.rs`: `test_ir_ws_accept_tls_runtime_ffi_declared` (extern present in module); `test_ir_websocket_accept_tls_parks_then_calls_runtime_ffi` (park + FFI call); `test_ir_websocket_accept_tls_returns_websocket_struct_shape` (`insertvalue` packs conn_fd into the `WebSocket {i32}` shape); `test_ir_ws_recv_text_routes_through_runtime_ffi_for_tls_accept_result` (regression guard — recv_text still dispatches to the unchanged FFI symbol; TLS routing happens at runtime via `lookup_session`, not at codegen). All 14 tls_codegen tests green; runtime unit tests 116/116; full `cargo test --features llvm` (compiler + codegen + memory_sanitizer + runtime, all 53 binaries) passes with zero regressions. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`. Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (~480 lines net — 4 helper generification + `TlsConnIo` adapter + `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls` + `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake` + `ws_recv_data_frame_inner` extraction + TLS-dispatch checks in `ws_send_data_frame` / `ws_recv_data_frame`); `runtime/src/tls.rs` (~30 lines net — `TlsSession` visibility + 3 helpers); `runtime/stdlib/ws.kara` (~40 lines net — `accept_tls` method + extensive comment block); `src/codegen.rs` (~18 lines net — `_ws_accept_tls` FFI declaration); `src/codegen/tls.rs` (~50 lines net — `lower_websocket_accept_tls`); `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (~15 lines net — dispatch arm); `tests/tls_codegen.rs` (~90 lines net — 4 new tests). **What slice 3 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-on slices): runtime-side end-to-end WS-over-TLS round-trip test in `runtime/src/tls.rs::tests` — deferred because `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake` requires a real wss:// client (rustls + WebSocket framing on the client side) to exercise; slice 4's checked-in test cert + the bench harness from Demo 1 slice 3 give the end-to-end coverage as Rust integration tests against the karac binary, which is a cleaner test surface than a per-FFI Rust unit test. [x] **Slice 4 — test-cert infrastructure shipped 2026-05-27.** Self-signed cert + key fixtures committed under `tests/fixtures/tls/`: `cert.pem` (X.509, CN=`localhost`, SANs `DNS:localhost` + `IP:127.0.0.1`, valid through 2036 — ~10-year window dodging the "tests fail in 2027" trap) + `key.pem` (RSA 2048-bit, unencrypted PKCS#8). `gen_test_cert.sh` regenerates both via `openssl req -x509 -newkey rsa:2048 -days 3653 -nodes -subj "/CN=localhost" -addext "subjectAltName=DNS:localhost,IP:127.0.0.1"`. **Dual SAN is load-bearing**: rustls clients check DNS SANs by default (CN alone produces `UnsupportedNameType` rejections), and the IP SAN lets bench harnesses that connect by `127.0.0.1` without DNS resolution validate too. `README.md` in the fixture dir documents the loading recipe + the security caveat (private key is committed — fine for loopback tests, disastrous if deployed). Fixtures are checked in so contributors without openssl can still run tests against the committed bytes; the script is for the rare regen case (post-expiry). Files: `tests/fixtures/tls/cert.pem` (~1.1 KB), `tests/fixtures/tls/key.pem` (~1.7 KB), `tests/fixtures/tls/gen_test_cert.sh` (~50 LoC), `tests/fixtures/tls/README.md` (~55 LoC). **Unblocks** Demo 1 slice 2 (the cert it serves) and the slice-3 bench harness (which loads these fixtures once the `FileSystem.read_to_string` codegen gap closes — see the carried follow-on below).
