  - [x] **Follow-on (a) — `FileSystem.read_to_string` codegen lowering shipped 2026-05-27.** Was: `FileSystem.read_to_string(path) -> Result[String, IoError]` is a `#[compiler_builtin]` stub in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` with no codegen lowering — the call returned `i64 0` (the fall-through default) instead of a `Result` aggregate. **Fix.** New runtime FFI `karac_runtime_file_read_to_string(out, path_ptr, path_len)` in `runtime/src/file.rs` slurps the file via `std::fs::read_to_string` and returns the UTF-8 bytes through the existing `KaracIoResult` buffer fields (`error_msg_ptr` / `error_msg_len`) on the success path (`error_kind == 0`) — **no ABI change**: the Ok payload is a `String` (3 words) that doesn't fit the single-i64 `value` field, so it reuses the same owned-buffer fields the `IoError.Other(String)` message path already uses (freed through the same kara `String` drop, `cap == len`). Codegen: new `FileOkKind::StringPayload` arm in `lower_kara_io_result` packs `{ptr, len, cap=len}` into Result payload words 0/1/2 (the `ok.str.ptr` / `ok.str.len` / `ok.str.cap` GEPs); new `compile_file_read_to_string` lowering mirrors `compile_file_constructor`; `assoc_call.rs` dispatch arm routes `FileSystem.read_to_string(path)` (distinct from the no-arg `Stdin.read_to_string`, still a placeholder); the FFI symbol is declared in the open-family loop in `Codegen::new`. **Tests:** 3 runtime unit tests (`runtime/src/file.rs` — contents-in-buffer, empty-file → null/zero, nonexistent → NotFound) + 7 codegen tests (`tests/codegen.rs` — FFI dispatch, String-payload aggregate GEPs, match-binding compiles, 2 regression guards [see (b)], and 2 E2E: real temp-file round-trip prints contents, nonexistent → `IoError.NotFound` match arm). All gates green (fmt + clippy `--all-targets --features llvm` + full `cargo test --features llvm`, 53 binaries, zero regressions). Files: `runtime/src/file.rs`, `src/codegen.rs`, `src/codegen/file.rs`, `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs`, `tests/codegen.rs`. **Unblocks** disk-based cert loading for the Demo 1 bench harness (slice 3); the Demo 1 slice-2 wss:// example can now drop its inlined-PEM workaround when the bench harness lands (left as-is for now since it's verified and the path-loading strategy belongs with the harness).

  - [x] **Follow-on (b) — match-arm pattern-binding as arm tail expression: MISDIAGNOSIS, subsumed by (a), 2026-05-27.** There was **no separate match-arm codegen bug.** Reproductions (run before fixing, per `measure_first_empirical`) proved a real `Result` scrutinee binds correctly whether the pattern binding is the bare arm tail (`Ok(b) => b`) **or** inside a block body (`Ok(b) => { b }`) — both compile. The "Undefined variable" symptom appeared **only** on `match FileSystem.read_to_string(p) { Ok(s) => s, ... }`, because `read_to_string` codegened to `i64 0` (bug (a)): `bind_pattern_values`' `TupleVariant` arm is gated on a `StructValue` scrutinee (`pattern_binding.rs:388`), so an `IntValue` scrutinee silently skips binding registration → "Undefined variable". The original entry's tail-vs-block framing compared two *different* scrutinees (`ws.recv_text()`'s real Result, which works, vs `read_to_string`'s i64, which didn't) and wrongly attributed the difference to binding position. Fixing (a) resolves the symptom; no `control_flow_match.rs` change was needed. Regression guards `test_ir_match_tail_binding_real_result_ok` / `test_ir_match_block_binding_real_result_ok` in `tests/codegen.rs` pin that both binding positions compile on a real `Result`.

- [x] **Completion wins cancellation. Holds by construction; verified 2026-06-06.** A branch is only cancellable cooperatively — `execute_task` (`runtime/src/lib.rs`) checks the cancel flag **only at task pickup**, never mid-run, so a task already running runs to completion (the comment there already named this "completion-wins at branch granularity"). Combined with the codegen cooperative checks (`emit_branch_cancel_check` polls the flag only at effect boundaries), a branch past its last check has no place left to observe the flag and finishes naturally; nothing ever rewrites a completed branch's result to `Cancelled`. So "real work is never retroactively converted to Cancelled" is satisfied by construction — no new code needed. Regression-locked by `par_run_running_branch_completes_despite_cancel` (`lib.rs`): a branch that flips its own region's cancel mid-body still runs to its end. **Scope-boundary exposure note:** the spec's "a late `Ok` appears in the `collect_all` result vector" half is **not** independently observable until `collect_all` lands (phase-6 line 485 — result collection from branch slots is still void at the runtime, `karac_par_run`); fail-fast `par` already returns the source-earliest `Err` regardless, so the completed `Ok` is correctly not surfaced there. See design.md § Parallel Failure and Cleanup — "Completion wins cancellation".

- [x] **Cascading cooperative cancellation across nested `par` regions. Shipped 2026-06-06.** Previously a nested `par` got a fresh, unlinked cancel flag (`emit_par_branch_fn` *replaces* `branch_cancel_ptr` with the inner branch's own flag; the runtime gave each nested `karac_par_run` an independent `ParCall.cancel`), so an inner branch never observed the outer cancel — it could run to completion and *escape* cancellation, and an unbounded inner effectful loop would hang the outer cancel forever. **Fix:** `karac_par_run` gains a `parent_cancel: *const AtomicBool` param (codegen passes the enclosing branch's `branch_cancel_ptr`, or `ptr null` at the top level — `src/codegen/par_blocks.rs`); the join's work-help loop (`par_join_wait`, `runtime/src/lib.rs`) polls it and, when the parent has cancelled, flips *this* region's `cancel`, which the inner branches observe at their next effect-boundary check → inner fail-fast → join returns → the outer branch observes its own cancel. This is the **same cooperative mechanism, no special cross-scope machinery**, and gives the spec's *sum-of-effect-boundary-distances along the nesting path* latency (the nested wait uses a ≤1ms `wait_timeout` so a busy inner branch that never signals can't stall the poll; the top-level call keeps the plain blocking wait — no overhead). **Caveat (within the cooperative model):** if the pool is exhausted and the join's caller is itself forced to *execute* an unbounded inner task, it can't poll until that task yields — the same "cooperative, not hard-preemption" limit the spec already calls out (tight loops without effect boundaries aren't cancellable). Tests: `par_join_wait_propagates_parent_cancel_into_region` (runtime propagation), `test_nested_par_passes_enclosing_branch_cancel_as_parent` (codegen passes the enclosing cancel ptr nested / `ptr null` top-level). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm`, runtime units, par_codegen (108). See design.md § Parallel Failure and Cleanup — "Cancellation cascades into nested regions".

- [x] **`karac query concurrency`.** Return parallelization decisions with reasoning. Moved from Phase 5 — requires concurrency analysis to be implemented first.

- [x] **Parameterized-resource distinctness rules.** Conservative collapse: two parameterized resources `R[a]` and `R[b]` are treated as distinct only when `a` and `b` are distinct string/integer literals at the call site, or are variables provably bound to different values (e.g., different function parameters). When distinctness is ambiguous (computed values, aliases, runtime-determined keys), the compiler conservatively collapses to the same resource and serializes. The rule is intentionally strict: if the programmer cannot predict the outcome without running the compiler, they'll reach for `seq { }` — which is the correct escape hatch, not a failure mode. Future extension: `#[distinct]` annotation to assert distinctness when the compiler can't prove it.

- [x] **Effect-boundary cooperative cancellation (mid-branch).** Shipped 2026-04-28 with conservative over-approximation. `Codegen::branch_cancel_ptr` is set inside `emit_par_branch_fn`; `emit_branch_cancel_check` runs at the head of every `compile_call` and `compile_method_call`. The cancel block drains `scope_cleanup_actions` and returns void from the branch fn. Effectful-narrowing follow-up landed 2026-04-28 (next entry). 2 IR-level tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs` pin both the cancel-check emission and the non-par no-emit guarantee.

- [x] **Mid-branch cancellation follow-up: narrow checks to effectful calls only.** Shipped 2026-04-28. Spec narrows the cancel-check from "every call" to "calls whose callee carries `reads` / `writes` / `sends` / `receives`" (`design.md § Effect-boundary cooperative cancellation`). New `Program.callee_effectful: HashMap<String, bool>` side-table populated by `Pipeline::effectcheck` (helper `build_callee_effectful_table` walks `inferred_effects` ∪ `declared_effects`); copied into `Codegen` at `compile_program` entry, mirror of `Program.question_conversions`. A callee is effectful iff its set carries any of the four resource verbs; `Polymorphic` / `PolymorphicWithFixed` are conservatively `true` (a monomorphization may pick up any effect). `emit_branch_cancel_check` now takes `callee: Option<&str>`; `Some(false)` short-circuits the atomic load, `None` / `Some(true)` / unknown name fall back to the conservative MVP path. `compile_call` recovers the callee key from the AST (`Identifier(n)` → `n`, two-segment `Path` → `seg0.seg1`); `compile_method_call` passes `None` (receiver type isn't known until method resolution). 3 new par_codegen tests pin: effectful helper still fires the check, pure helper elides it (only entry-time check remains), mixed pure+effectful par block emits exactly one check per effectful call. Tests run the full analysis pipeline (`ir_for_with_pipeline`) so the side-table is populated before codegen. **Method-call narrowing follow-up shipped 2026-04-28** (round 2 — see git history `ba2dc9a`): typechecker populates `TypeCheckResult.method_callee_types: HashMap<SpanKey, String>` directly during `infer_method_call` (kept in a separate map rather than reusing `expr_types` because the parser sets `MethodCall.span == receiver.span`, so the receiver-type and method-return-type insertions race at the same key); lowering forwards it to `Program.method_callee_types`; `compile_method_call` derives `Type.method` keys at the call site and consults `callee_effectful`. 2 par_codegen tests added (`test_ir_par_branch_skips_method_check_for_pure_callee` and `test_ir_par_branch_emits_method_check_for_effectful_callee`). No remaining open follow-ups on this entry. Files (round 1): `src/ast.rs`, `src/cli.rs`, `src/codegen.rs`, `tests/par_codegen.rs`. Files (round 2): `src/ast.rs`, `src/typechecker.rs`, `src/lowering.rs`, `src/codegen.rs`, `tests/par_codegen.rs`.

- [ ] **`collect_all { }` language syntax.** Gather-all-errors variant of `par { }`. All branches run to completion (no fail-fast); returns `Vec[Result[T, E]]` with one entry per branch. Needs: parser support for `collect_all` keyword, runtime gather mode (no cancel-on-error), result struct ABI in codegen.

- [x] **`Never` type inference rules — `LUB(Never, T) = T` + order-independent metavar binding. Shipped 2026-06-06.** Ground-truth probe at implementation time showed substeps (1) and (2) were **already satisfied**: branch joins pre-filter `Never` arms (`infer_match` picks the first non-`Never` arm and skips `Never` in the fold; `if`/`if let` short-circuit a `Never` arm before `join_branch_types`), and an all-`Never` metavar already solved to `Never` because `unify_types` bound it directly. The **one real gap was substep (3), the mixed case, and it was order-dependent**: `unify_types` (`src/typechecker/inference.rs`) resolved a `Never`-bound var to `Never` *before* matching, so a diverging argument seen *first* (`pick(panic(), 42)`) pinned `T = Never` and a later concrete `42` could not upgrade it — `pick(42, panic())` worked, `pick(panic(), 42)` wrongly inferred `Never`. **Fix:** a raw top-level metavar is intercepted before resolution and bound via `unify_type_var`, which treats `Never` as the bottom type — a concrete constraint *upgrades* a tentative `Never` binding (either argument order), and a `Never` constraint never demotes a concrete one; an all-`Never` var stays `Never`. **Substep (4) diagnostics: N/A under this approach** — there is no distinct "`Never`-fallback" event to surface (the var solves to `Never` by direct binding, not a finalize-time fallback). **Substep (5):** 8 tests in `tests/typechecker.rs` (`never_*`) using a `bool`-slot discriminator — both `pick` orders → `i64`, three-arg diverging-first → `i64`, all-diverging / single-diverging → `Never`, `if`/`match` one-diverging-arm → `i64`, `let x: () = todo()` accepted. Gate green: typechecker (1473), full non-llvm suite (0 failed), clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm`, fmt. **Original spec (for reference):** Spec lives at design.md § Type Inference (v60 item 30). Sub-steps: (1) LUB algorithm — extend the LUB function in the typechecker so that `LUB(Never, T) = T` and `LUB(T, Never) = T` for every type `T`. The rule is rule 0 (matches before identical-types), so an if-else with one diverging arm and one concrete-typed arm joins to the concrete type; an if-else with both arms diverging joins to `Never`. (2) Inference fallback — when a metavariable's only solving constraint is a value of type `Never` (a generic call whose only concrete argument has type `Never`, a diverging closure body, a `vec![panic!()]`-style construction with a single `Never`-typed element), solve the metavariable to `Never` rather than letting it remain unsolved or defaulting to `()`. The mechanic: when the substitution-finalize step finds a metavariable with no concrete-type constraints but with a `Never <: ?T` subsumption record, `?T := Never`. (3) Mixed-constraint case unchanged — when a metavariable has both `Never <: ?T` and `Concrete <: ?T` constraints, the LUB rule from (1) already produces the concrete type; no special fallback logic needed for this path. (4) Diagnostics — `karac explain` includes the metavariable's chosen value in inference traces; the `Never`-fallback case is identified explicitly so a programmer reading the trace sees "T solved to Never (no concrete constraint)". (5) Test plan: `let y = id(panic!())` with `fn id[T](x: T) -> T` — assert `y : Never`; closure `|| panic!()` — return type `Never`; `vec![todo()]` — element type `Never`; `pick(42, panic!())` — joins to `i64` (LUB rule, not fallback); `pick(panic!(), panic!())` — joins to `Never` (LUB collapses to identical-types case after rule 0); `let x: () = panic!()` — accepted via existing Never-coerces-to-any rule (annotation present, fallback doesn't fire); `if cond { panic!() } else { 5 }` — type `i64` via LUB rule. (Phase 5.2 — touches the LUB algorithm and metavariable substitution-finalize; both already exist in the typechecker, so the work is rule additions and targeted test coverage, not new infrastructure.)

- [ ] **`if let` / `while let` / `let...else` scrutinee temporary scope. `while let` + `let...else` lowering (codegen + interpreter) landed 2026-06-06; remaining: scrutinee-temp dedicated scope (slice 3), MutexGuard drop-order tests (slice 4).** The checklist originally framed this as "verification + targeted lowering placement; no new IR or codegen," but that premise did not hold: **two of the three constructs were not codegen'd at all** (empirically confirmed by IR probe, then by building+running real native binaries on `main`) — they have since been lowered. **History:** A **fail-loud safety fix** landed first (2026-06-06) — `while let` / `let…else` were made to hard-error at codegen instead of silently no-op'ing (they had fallen through the `compile_expr` `_ => Ok(i64 0)` and `compile_stmt` `_ => Ok(())` catch-alls, so `karac build` emitted a clean binary that ran **wrong** with exit 0: `while let` dropped the whole loop body, and `let…else` with an *unused* binding skipped the scrutinee + else-divergence and fell straight through). That closed the silent-miscompile class. **Slices 1 + 2 (the actual lowering) then landed 2026-06-06**, superseding the fail-loud arms with real codegen:

- **Slice 1 — `let … else` lowered.** `compile_let_else` (`src/codegen/control_flow.rs`), called from `compile_stmt`'s `StmtKind::LetElse` arm. Evaluates the scrutinee, tests the pattern (`compile_pattern_condition`), and branches: match edge binds the pattern's names into the **enclosing** scope (`bind_pattern_values`) and falls through to the following statements; else edge runs the divergent block (no merge). Typechecker fix (`src/typechecker/items.rs` LetElse arm): route pattern binding through `check_pattern_against` (not `bind_pattern_types`, whose `TupleVariant` arm bound payloads to `Type::Error`) so `let Some(x) = … else` types `x` from the variant payload and records `pattern_binding_types` for codegen; the else block is inferred *before* the bind so the pattern's names aren't in scope there.
- **Slice 2 — `while let` lowered.** `compile_while_let` (`src/codegen/control_flow.rs`), called from `compile_expr`'s `ExprKind::WhileLet` arm. Structurally `compile_while` with a pattern-test condition: the header re-evaluates the scrutinee each iteration and tests it; on a match the body runs in a per-iteration scope-cleanup frame (pattern bindings + body temporaries drop at iteration exit before the next scrutinee eval). Typechecker fix (`src/typechecker/exprs.rs` WhileLet arm): bind the pattern in the body scope via `check_pattern_against`, mirroring `if let` (previously the pattern was ignored, leaving the binding un-typed).
- **Tests:** `test_ir_while_let_emits_loop_not_noop` / `test_ir_let_else_emits_branch_not_noop` (IR-level, archive-independent — assert the loop/branch blocks emit, not a no-op); `test_e2e_while_let_drains_and_binds` / `test_e2e_let_else_binds_then_else_diverges` (run native, assert correct output incl. per-iteration binding and the else-diverges edge); `asan_while_let_per_iteration_heap_local_freed` / `asan_let_else_binding_and_else_heap_clean` (`tests/memory_sanitizer.rs` — per-iteration drop + both let-else edges leak/UAF-clean, exercising `Option[String]`). Gates green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm`, non-llvm suite, codegen (1238), memory_sanitizer (95).

**Remaining work (item stays `[ ]`):** (c) **`if let` — lowered, but scrutinee-scope is a latent gap.** `compile_if_let` (`src/codegen/control_flow.rs`) evaluates the scrutinee into the **enclosing** frame with no scope frame pushed around it, so the spec'd scoping (else-edge drop *before* the else body; then-arm drop at body exit) does **not** hold structurally. `compile_while_let` / `compile_let_else` likewise evaluate the scrutinee into the enclosing frame (consistent with `if let`). Not observable today because no *droppable* scrutinee temp is tracked (no `MutexGuard`; method-chain temps untracked — see line 491's caveat). **So the remaining slices are:** **(3)** place the `if let`/`while let`/`let…else` scrutinee temps in a dedicated scope so they drop on the non-matching edge / at then-arm exit / per-iteration; **(4)** the canonical drop-order tests need a `MutexGuard` type (`mutex.kara` is type-shape-only) — or any user-`Drop` type — to *observe* drop order; **(5 — done 2026-06-06)** interpreter parity — `while let` now evaluates in the tree-walk interpreter (`eval_expr_inner`'s `ExprKind::WhileLet` arm in `src/interpreter/eval_expr.rs`, modeled on the `For` loop: re-evaluate scrutinee each iteration, `try_match_pattern` as the loop condition, per-iteration `push_scope`/`bind_pattern`/`pop_scope` with `break`/`continue`/label handling). `let…else` was already handled (`eval_stmt_cf`'s `LetElse` arm in `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs` — the earlier "likewise unhandled" claim was wrong; only `while let` panicked). Both now have interpreter regression tests (`tests/interpreter.rs`: `test_while_let_drains_and_binds` / `_break` / `_continue`, `test_let_else_match_and_diverge`) whose expectations mirror the codegen E2E tests. Katas run via `karac run` / `karac test` now support both constructs. (Note: an *orthogonal* interpreter gap surfaced while testing — `Vec.remove` isn't dispatchable on a `mut ref` receiver, `method_call.rs:843` — unrelated to this item; the regression tests drive `while let` via `Vec.pop()` instead.) **Original spec (for reference):** Spec lives at design.md § `if let` and `let...else` (v60 item 29). Sub-steps: (1) NLL/drop-placement pass — verify that scrutinee-expression temporaries (anonymous intermediates produced by the right-hand side of `=` in `if let PAT = SCRUT { … } else { … }`, `while let PAT = SCRUT { … }`, `let PAT = SCRUT else { … };`) have a live range scoped to the matching arm: in the `then` arm of `if let`, the temporaries live through the entire body and drop at arm exit (because pattern-bound names may borrow into them); in the `else` arm of `if let` / `else if let` / `let...else`, the temporaries have already been dropped *before* the arm body begins; in `while let`, per-iteration drop at body exit before the next iteration's scrutinee is evaluated. (2) Code-path verification — verify the code path that lowers `if let` / `let-else` / `while let` to control flow places the scrutinee-temp drops on the *non-matching* edge before the else-arm code (rather than placing them at the join point after both arms). The lowering pattern: evaluate scrutinee → match against pattern → on miss, drop temps then jump to else; on hit, bind names then enter then-arm body, drop temps at body exit. (3) Pattern-binding interaction — pattern-bound names (`value` in `if let Some(value) = ...`) are local bindings of the arm, NOT temporaries; their drop follows the standard `let`-binding rules and is unaffected by this item. The rule covers only the anonymous intermediates of the scrutinee expression. (4) Deferred composition — the future `if let` chains feature (deferred to Phase 5+) will apply the same rule per-link: each link's temporaries drop before the next link is evaluated (on success) or before the else arm runs (on failure). (5) Test plan: lock-in-scrutinee `if let Some(v) = mu.lock().get(k) { ... } else { log(...) }` — assert via instrumented destructors that the MutexGuard's `Drop` fires before the else block runs; `let Ok(config) = parse(mu.lock().as_str()) else { return Err(...) };` — guard drops before the divergent else block; `while let Some(item) = mu.lock().pop_front() { process(item) }` — per-iteration lock release verified by instrumented drop order across iterations; pattern-bound name lifetime in then-arm holds borrows into scrutinee temps without dangling. (Phase 4 / Phase 5.2 — touches the existing live-range placement and pattern-match lowering paths; no new IR or codegen, just verification + targeted lowering placement.)

- [x] **Tail-expression temporary scope — drop before block locals. Holds by construction; verified 2026-06-06.** The ordering is structural, not a special case: a block's `let`-bindings and the materialized temp of its tail expression are pushed onto **one** scope-cleanup frame in program order — the lets first, the tail-expr temp last (it is later in source order) — so the LIFO drain (`emit_scope_cleanup`, `src/codegen/runtime.rs`) frees the tail-expr temp **before** every block-local `let`. This is the same unified-stack mechanism already pinned at IR level by `test_ir_defer_drop_interleave_emission_order` (`tests/codegen.rs`) for the defer/drop interleave. Substep (2) move-out: a tail value moved out of the block is returned with no in-scope drop (`compile_tail_final_expr`, `src/codegen/stmts.rs`) — already exercised clean by `asan_ref_arg_function_return_string_freed`. Substep (3) statement-position `;` temporaries are unchanged. **Scope caveat (honest):** the only mid-expression temporary codegen tracks today is the `ref T` Vec/String call-arg materialization (the `asan_ref_arg_*` family); **general** owned-temp tracking does not exist, so an *untracked* tail temp does not drop at all — but that is a **leak** gap (general temp tracking), not a drop-*ordering* gap, and is out of this item's scope. The canonical `mu.lock().get(k).clone()` *drop-order* observation from the spec's test plan awaits a `MutexGuard` type (`mutex.kara` is type-shape-only) + method-chain temp tracking. **New regression:** `asan_tail_expr_temp_coexists_with_block_local_let` (`tests/memory_sanitizer.rs`) puts a tracked ref-arg heap temp in tail position alongside a heap block-local `let v` and asserts ASAN-clean (a hoist to the outer scope, wrong-cap free, or double-free against `v` would surface). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm`, memory_sanitizer suite. **Original spec (for reference):** Spec lives at design.md § Drop ordering within a branch (v60 item 28). Sub-steps: (1) NLL/drop-placement pass — verify that a temporary created inside a block's tail expression has a live range ending immediately after the tail expression finishes evaluating (including borrow uses chained off it), and that its drop is pushed onto the unified LIFO drop+defer stack *after* every `let` binding's drop in the same block. The rule is implicit in the existing program-order-LIFO design (the tail expression is later in source order than every `let`, so its temporaries push last and pop first), but the verification is required to catch any code path that hoisted tail-expression temporaries to the block's outer scope (the pre-Rust-2024 behavior). (2) Move-out exception — when the tail expression's value (the temporary itself) is moved out of the block, its live range escapes; no drop is inserted in this scope. The standard NLL move-out rule already covers this; verify the tail-expression case shares the code path. (3) Statement-position temporaries (an expression-statement ending in `;`) continue to drop at the `;` — unchanged from the existing design. (4) Test plan: lock-in-tail pattern (`mu.lock().get(k).clone()`) — assert that the MutexGuard's `Drop` runs before any preceding `let` binding's `Drop` via instrumented destructors that record drop order; tail expression that moves out a temporary (`fn make_guard(mu) -> MutexGuard { mu.lock() }`) — no drop inserted in this scope; nested blocks (`{ let x = …; { let y = …; tail_expr() } }`) — inner-block tail-temp drops before inner `y`, both before outer `x`; tail expression that uses a borrow into a let-binding — the borrow's source binding stays live until the tail expression's drop fires (otherwise the borrow would dangle). (Phase 4 / Phase 5.2 — touches the existing live-range placement code; no new IR or codegen, just a verification pass on the existing NLL output.)

- [ ] **Panic semantics at the FFI boundary — `extern "C"` auto-abort + `extern "C-unwind"` propagation.** Spec lives at design.md § Panic Semantics at the FFI Boundary (v60 item 27). Sub-steps: (1) Codegen — for every `pub extern "C" fn` defined in Kāra, emit two LLVM symbols: (a) the bare Kāra-callable function (mangled by the standard rules unless `#[unsafe(no_mangle)]` overrides) and (b) a separate exported wrapper symbol with the C-facing name that wraps the call in a `catch_panic`-equivalent landing pad and routes any caught panic to `std.process.abort()`. Kāra-internal calls go through the bare symbol with no overhead; C-side calls go through the trampoline. The trampoline's abort path writes the panic message + source location to stderr before calling `abort()`. (2) Codegen elision — under `panic = "abort"` build profile, the trampoline is a no-op (every panic is already abort); emit only the bare symbol with the C-facing name (or the wrapper as a tail-call that just forwards). (3) Build-profile gate — `extern "C-unwind"` definitions and imports are rejected at parse under `panic = "abort"` profiles with `error[E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE]`. The same gate already rejects `catch_panic` calls under abort profiles (per item 26's checklist entry); both rejections share the diagnostic surface. (4) Typechecker — `pub extern "C-unwind" fn` definitions whose body's inferred effects include `panics` MUST declare `panics` in the signature; otherwise emit `error[E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_PANICS]` with a suggested-fix span adding `with panics` to the signature. `pub extern "C" fn` definitions MAY declare `panics`; the declared effect describes Kāra-side calls (the boundary trampoline is invisible to the effect system). (5) Effect-system integration — no new rules needed beyond (4); the existing inference and propagation machinery handles all four cases (import/export × C/C-unwind) uniformly because the trampoline is a codegen-only artifact. (6) FFI absorption pattern — the design recommends wrapping the body in `catch_panic` to surface errors to C as error codes rather than relying on auto-abort; the auto-abort trampoline is the safety net for panics that escape the user-written catch (e.g., panic during the panic-handler logic). Test plan (when codegen lands): `pub extern "C" fn double(x: i32) -> i32 { x.checked_mul(2).unwrap() }` called from a C harness with overflowing input → process aborts with the panic message on stderr; same function called from Kāra → panic propagates normally; `pub extern "C-unwind" fn parse_or_throw(...)` called from a C++ harness with a `try { } catch (...) { }` block → exception caught on the C++ side; `pub extern "C-unwind" fn` body that may panic but signature omits `with panics` → typecheck rejection; under `kernel` profile, `extern "C-unwind"` declaration → parse rejection; round-trip via `catch_panic` inside `pub extern "C" fn` → no abort, returns C-shaped error code. (Phase 7 — depends on LLVM unwinding substrate from item 26; trampoline emission is a codegen pattern, not a typechecker change.)

- [ ] **`catch_panic[T]` panic-absorption primitive.** Spec lives at design.md § Catching Panics: `catch_panic[T]` (v60 item 26). Sub-steps: (1) Typechecker — recognise `catch_panic` as a `#[compiler_builtin]` with the special signature `fn catch_panic[T, with E](f: Fn() -> T with E) -> Result[T, PanicInfo] with (E - panics)`. The `(E - panics)` arithmetic is closed-form in the compiler — it is not a user-writable pattern. At every call site, the result type's effect ceiling is the closure's effect set with `panics` removed; if the closure does not have `panics`, `karac lint` flags the call as a likely mistake but the call remains legal (always returns `Ok`). (2) Build-profile gate — under `panic = "abort"` (kernel/embedded/ISR profiles), `catch_panic` calls are rejected at typecheck with `error[E_CATCH_PANIC_REQUIRES_UNWIND]: catch_panic is unavailable under panic = "abort"; remove the call or change the build profile`. The same gate rejects `extern "C-unwind"` declarations under abort builds. (3) Stdlib — `PanicInfo` (with `message`, `location`, `kind`, `thread_name`, `backtrace`), `PanicKind` (`#[non_exhaustive]` enum: `Explicit`, `Unwrap`, `Indexing`, `IntegerOverflow`, `DivisionByZero`, `ContractViolation`, `Foreign`, `DropDuringUnwind`), `SourceLocation` types in the prelude (paired with `catch_panic` and the panic-hook surface). `PanicInfo` is `Send + Clone`. (4) Codegen (Phase 7) — lower `catch_panic(closure)` to LLVM's `invoke` instruction with a landing pad that catches the unwind, captures `PanicInfo` from the runtime panic-payload, and routes to the `Err(...)` arm. The runtime side maintains a thread-local "in-flight panic" tag; `process.exit()` sets the tag to `Exit` rather than `Recoverable`, and the catch-frame inspects the tag and re-raises rather than producing `Err(PanicInfo)` (per the design.md/process.exit interaction rule, originally pinned in deferred.md). (5) Auto-concurrency interaction — `catch_panic` does not extend the panic-domination rule for parallel scopes; a panic absorbed inside a single branch produces `Ok(Err(PanicInfo))` from that branch, the parallel scope sees a successful result, no peer cancellation. The structured-concurrency machinery already does its own internal panic-isolation at task boundaries; `catch_panic` is the user-facing surface of the same primitive. (6) Drop-time interaction — destructor panics during the closure's normal scope-exit produce `Err(PanicInfo { kind: DropDuringUnwind, ... })`; destructor panics *during* an in-flight unwind that `catch_panic` is already absorbing become double-panics and abort the process (no double-panic protection). (7) FFI integration — panics that crossed an `extern "C-unwind"` ABI boundary surface as `PanicKind.Foreign`; the absorption pattern from the FFI section uses `catch_panic` directly. Test plan (when codegen lands): explicit `panic!` inside closure → `Err` with `Explicit`; out-of-bounds index → `Err` with `Indexing`; `process.exit(2)` propagates through (verified via subprocess test); double-panic during catch → process-aborts; `catch_panic` under `panic = "abort"` profile → typecheck error; closure carrying `with reads(Db) writes(Cache) panics` produces a `Result` whose result-type's effect ceiling is `with reads(Db) writes(Cache)` (panics stripped, others passed through). (Phase 7 — depends on LLVM unwinding substrate; typechecker stub work can land in Phase 5.2 to gate the build-profile rejection diagnostics.)

- [x] **Scheduler minimum invariants (language-level, cross-scheduler). Implemented:** The Phase 6 scheduler and any future runtime profile must satisfy five invariants that programs written against language-level rules rely on: (1) **no lost work** — a completed branch's `Ok` result is never silently discarded (it reaches the scope return, a `collect_all` result, or at minimum its `defer`/mutations still run); (2) **cancellation eventually observed** — every branch either completes or observes cancellation in bounded time after a triggering event; (3) **cancellation cascades** into nested regions; (4) **termination** — programs without pure tight loops terminate when all branches finish or cancel; (5) **scheduler deadlock-freedom** — the scheduler itself must not introduce deadlock beyond what user-level locks can create. Backpressure under overload, fairness between unrelated regions, and scheduler-specific cancel optimizations are **not** in this invariant set — they are per-profile concerns deferred to runtime chapters, and programs that depend on them must declare the dependency in their build profile. See design.md § Scheduler-layer concerns and minimum invariants.

- [ ] **Cost-model specification (v1.x).** Feature 5 currently uses a degenerate cost model: parallelize whenever distinctness allows it and `ParallelGroup.is_trivial` is false; trivial pure-computation groups go sequential. The full v1.x cost-model spec — per-call cost heuristic (cheap/medium/expensive based on body shape: pure arithmetic vs. allocation vs. I/O vs. effect class), fork threshold (sum-of-costs vs. scheduling overhead), loop-body parallelization rule (whether iterations of a `for` over a pure body fork), distinctness-policy when parameterized-resource keys are dynamic — is deferred until Parallax-lite (the same workload that grounds Item 7's Cumulative Cost Surface measurement, see roadmap.md Phase 8) provides empirical numbers to tune against. Specifying a model without measurement risks locking in numbers that turn out to be wrong. **Determinism requirement:** cost-model decisions must be a pure function of (source, compiler version, target profile) — same inputs always produce the same parallelization graph; no runtime nondeterminism, no host-environment leakage. Cross-version improvements ride the Reported Behavior layer (changelog-itemized; tools that consume `karac query concurrency` tolerate version skew). See `design.md § Feature 5 > Cost Model — v1 Status`.

- [x] **State-machine body-splitter doesn't handle control flow — RESOLVED by the A2 LLVM-coroutine transform (default-on).** The §9 fork below was decided in favour of option **(A)** — see `docs/spikes/network-async-coroutine-transform.md`, specifically the A2 (LLVM coroutine intrinsics) variant — so LLVM's CoroSplit generates the state machine and control flow (`match`/`if`/`while`/`loop`) around yields is handled by construction (spike §7 slice 3, validated by `tests/coro_e2e.rs` loop/if handlers). The degenerate classifier described below is left emitted-but-dead. **Original diagnosis preserved below for history.** Surfaced 2026-05-30 by the `supervised_echo` kata (kara-katas). **Symptom:** a `fn` that calls a network-yielding stdlib method (`TcpStream.connect` / `accept` / `read` / `write` / `recv_*` / `send_*` — the `sends/receives(Network)`-seeded methods) and contains *any control flow* around it runs wrong. Minimal repro: `fn try_once(p: i64) { match TcpStream.connect(f"127.0.0.1:{p}") { Result.Ok(_) => { println("c"); } Result.Err(_) => { println("e"); } } } fn main() { try_once(19099); }` prints nothing, exits 0. **Contrast that isolates it:** the *same* `match TcpStream.connect(...)` written directly in `main` works (`main` is the entry, never state-machine-transformed; pins: `tests/tcp_stream.rs::test_tcp_stream_connect_err_is_connection_refused`); and a helper calling the *non*-network `TcpListener.bind` works (bind isn't a network yield, so the helper isn't transformed — the kata's `pick_port`). **Root cause — CONFIRMED via IR + sync/spawn repros (deeper and more pervasive than the original synchronous-only hypothesis).** A network-boundary fn gets a state-machine poll-fn (`@__kara_poll_<fn>`) generated by the body-splitting walker in `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (`emit_state_machine_poll_fn_for_key`). **That walker only classifies straight-line statements** — `BodySplitStmt` is just `FreeFnCall` / `MethodCall` / `Let` / `Assign`; any *control-flow* statement (`match` / `if` / `while` / `loop`) is silently skipped. So for `try_once` (body = one `match`) the emitted poll-fn is **degenerate**: `state_0` stores next-tag=1 + returns Pending; `state_1` returns Ready; **neither state runs the match / connect / println** (verified by dumping the module: `@try_once` is compiled normally with the full correct body, but the empty `@__kara_poll_try_once` is what the call-site intercept in `call_dispatch.rs` drives via `@__kara_state_new_try_once()` + a poll-loop — the normal `@try_once` is never called). **Both call shapes are affected:** (1) *synchronous* (`main` calls `try_once()`) → drives the empty poll-fn → silent no-op; (2) *spawned* (`tg.spawn(|| helper())`) → **HANGS**: the empty `state_0` returns Pending *without registering an fd*, so the dispatcher never wakes the task and `handle.join()` deadlocks (verified — a spawn+join repro of a network helper produced no output and never reached the post-join `println`). **Impact:** network code cannot be factored into ordinary helper functions at all. **The flagship demo pattern (`ws_idle_holder`'s `handle_connection` = `loop { let r = ws.recv_text(buf); match r { … } }`, spawned via `tg.spawn`) is exactly this shape and would hit the spawn-hang — re-verify Demo 1 against this finding.** **Fix scope — large (a real phase-6 feature, NOT a session-sized fix).** The correct fix extends the body-splitting / state-machine transform to handle control flow (`match` / `if` / `while` / `loop`) around yield points — essentially a CPS/coroutine transform over control flow, the core of the M:N scheduler story. A "call the normal fn instead" shortcut helps only the synchronous case and *cannot* help spawned tasks (M:N scheduling requires the pollable state machine; a normal call with thread-blocking inline parks would defeat 1M-connection scaling). This is the central remaining gap in effect-routed task parking (phase-6 line 17). Cross-ref: `supervised_echo` README (kara-katas) records the inline-in-`main` workaround; the sibling `return;`-in-`main` codegen bug is `[x]` in [`phase-7-codegen.md`](phase-7-codegen.md).

  **CONFIRMED demo-affecting + BROADER than control-flow — E2E repro 2026-05-30.** Built a demo-faithful TCP echo server (`main` binds + `loop { match accept() { Ok(s) => tg.spawn(|| handle(s)) } }`) and drove it with a real client. **Findings:** (1) handler logic *inline in `main`* (accept + `match s.read(buf)` + `s.write(reply)`) services the connection correctly (client receives the reply) — confirms the harness is valid and network I/O in `main` works; (2) the *same logic in a spawned helper* `handle(s: TcpStream)` — both with a `match` body AND a **straight-line** body (`let reply = …; s.write(reply.bytes())`) — **does NOT service the connection** (client gets RECV TIMEOUT; connection accepted but never serviced); (3) re-tested with the scheduler ON (default, no `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0`) — same failure, so it is **not** an auto-par artifact. **So the gap is broader than the control-flow diagnosis above:** even a *straight-line* spawned network helper (which the body-splitter's `Let` + `MethodCall` classification *should* handle) is mis-compiled, pointing at *additional* root causes beyond control flow — likely the captured-struct-arg threading (the `TcpStream s` passed into the spawned closure not reaching the handler's state-struct correctly) and/or the spawn-drive path, not only the body-splitter. **Demo-1 impact, concrete:** `ws_idle_holder`'s spawned `handle_connection` does **not** service its connection — connections are *accepted* (the `main` accept-loop works) and *held open* by the stuck/no-op spawned tasks (so a connection-COUNT headline can still hold at the accept level), but the per-connection recv/send handler is non-functional. Any per-connection *servicing* claim, and any per-conn-memory number measured assuming working handlers, needs re-validation. **Precise localization (body-split vs captured-arg-threading vs spawn-drive) is the first step of the fix and needs IR-level work** — deferred to the fix slice, which remains a large phase-6 undertaking.

  **PRECISE IR LOCALIZATION — 2026-05-30 (dumped the module for the straight-line spawned-helper repro).** The bug is **100% in the body-splitter's degenerate poll-fn** — the other two suspects are **confirmed correct**: (a) the spawn wrapper `@__spawn_wrap_0` loads the captured `s` from the closure env and `store`s it into the handler state-struct's arg-0 field (captured-arg threading WORKS), then drives a correct `kara.poll_loop` (`call @__kara_poll_handle`; loop while Pending with `@sched_yield`; free on done) — spawn-drive WORKS. (b) `@handle` itself is compiled normally with the full correct body (the `s.write`). The defect: `@__kara_poll_handle`'s `state_0`/`state_1` reload `s` + `reply` from the state-struct and write them back, but **never emit the `s.write(reply.bytes())` call** — the actual work is silently dropped. **Why the walker skips it:** the statement is `let _ = s.write(reply.bytes())`, and (1) the `let _ =` **wildcard** pattern isn't a `PatternKind::Binding`, so the walker's `Let` arm skips it; (2) even as a bare `MethodCall`, the arg `reply.bytes()` is a method-call expression outside `recognize_body_arg`'s recognised `BodyArg` set, so the call is dropped. So even "straight-line" network code falls outside the walker's coverage. **Architectural assessment — this is the real fork.** The current state-machine transform (slices 8h–8q) is an **incremental statement-shape *classifier*** (`BodySplitStmt` = a fixed menu of `Let`/`Assign`/`FreeFnCall`/`MethodCall` with a narrow `BodyArg` set); it can be widened shape-by-shape, but it **cannot cleanly reach arbitrary control flow** (`match`/`if`/`while`/`loop` around yields) — that's not a coverage gap, it's the wrong shape of solution. A correct, general fix is one of: **(A) a real CPS/coroutine transform** that splits *any* function body at its yield points (handles all statements + control flow by construction — the stackless-async model, a major rewrite of the state-machine codegen); or **(B) a stackful-coroutine / green-thread runtime** where each task gets its own (small, growable) stack, network-boundary functions run *normally* (no transform — `@handle` just runs its real body), and a "park" switches stacks (the Go-goroutine model — no body-splitter needed at all). Both are major undertakings and **(B) is a core language/runtime architectural decision**, not a contained code fix. Recommendation: do not pour effort into incrementally widening the classifier (band-aid that still can't service the demo's `loop`+`match` handler); pick the target model (A vs B) first.

  **DESIGN SPIKE — 2026-05-30 → recommend A via LLVM coroutines (option A2).** Full write-up: [`docs/spikes/network-async-coroutine-transform.md`](../spikes/network-async-coroutine-transform.md). Key result: a third path beats both A1 (hand-rolled CPS) and B (stackful) — **emit each network-boundary fn with its normal body + `llvm.coro.suspend` at each park, mark it `presplitcoroutine`, and let LLVM's CoroSplit pass generate the state machine.** It handles all control flow *by construction* (LLVM splits the CFG), stays **stackless** (preserves the per-conn density thesis B would surrender), and offloads the hardest sub-problem to a battle-tested LLVM pass instead of hand-rolling it (A1). **Proven feasible in Kāra's exact toolchain** (inkwell 0.9 / LLVM 18.1) via a probe: `presplitcoroutine` resolves, the `llvm.coro.*` intrinsics are findable, and a minimal coroutine survives `coro-early,coro-split,coro-cleanup` via `Module::run_passes` and is split into a `.resume` clone. Estimate: ~7–10 bounded slices (the runtime event-loop/dispatcher/fd-registration is reusable; the main correctness risk is drop-across-suspend, ASAN-gated). Reusable runtime + existing seams are mapped in the spike doc.

  **IMPLEMENTATION PROGRESS (A2).** *Slice 1 (done):* `coro-early,coro-split,coro-cleanup` runs unconditionally in `apply_optimization_passes` (a correctness pass at every opt level, incl. `-O0`) — pure no-op for non-coroutine modules. *Slice 2a (done):* the builder-path coro-emission is validated. inkwell 0.9 panics on the LLVM `token` type, so the token-typed coro intrinsics are emitted via raw `llvm-sys` interleaved with the inkwell body — new module `src/codegen/coro.rs` (`CoroIntrinsics` declare-once intrinsic table + `build_demo_coroutine`), unit test `builder_emitted_coroutine_splits` proves a coroutine emitted through the real codegen API survives CoroSplit (`.resume` clone) and re-verifies. Confirmed the inkwell⇄llvm-sys bridge is bidirectional with no memory round-trip (i8 `coro.suspend` result feeds an inkwell `build_switch` directly via `IntValue::new`), and moved `llvm-sys` onto the base `llvm` feature (`llvm = ["inkwell", "dep:llvm-sys"]`). *Slice 2b.1 (done):* the drive bridge. A read of the runtime + drive seams found the existing dispatcher drives any `KaracParkedTask { poll_fn, state }` unchanged (`(task.poll_fn)(task.state, &cancel)`, event_loop.rs ~2992), and the leaf already separates park from syscall — so a coroutine plugs in with **zero runtime changes**. `coro.rs` gains the drive intrinsics (`coro.resume/done/destroy`) + `emit_coro_resume_shim` → `__kara_coro_resume(ptr handle, ptr cancel)` built to the exact `KaracParkedTask.poll_fn` ABI (resume; on `coro.done` destroy + Ready, else Pending); test `resume_shim_lowers_alongside_coroutine` proves it lowers cleanly through the coro pipeline and re-verifies. *Slice 2b.2a (done):* leaf-suspend EMISSION de-risk. `coro.rs::build_demo_park_coroutine` emits the production leaf shape (frame-resident parked slot `{poll_fn=@__kara_coro_resume, state=hdl, token}`, `register_fd(fd, dir, &parked)` before `coro.suspend`, deregister+syscall on the resume edge); test `park_shaped_coroutine_splits_with_frame_resident_slot` proves CoroSplit lifts the parked slot into the coro frame (the pointer register_fd captures is a `%demo_park_coro.Frame` GEP — a stable address the dispatcher can deref while suspended, not a dangling ramp alloca), keeps the registration in the ramp, and lands the post-park syscall in the `.resume` clone (not dropped — the bug-C failure mode). The resume-edge token reload forces frame-residency. Also closed the spike-§8 self-borrow-across-suspend risk: Kāra structurally cannot hold a borrow across a park (call-statement-scoped borrows drained at scope exit; no reference-typed struct fields), so no coro frame is ever self-referential. *Drive-model correction (2026-05-31, spike § 6¾):* designing the 2b.3 drive found the original "sync resume-loop" sketch is **semantically wrong** — connection fds are non-blocking (listener `set_nonblocking(true)`; accepted fds inherit `O_NONBLOCK`), so `karac_runtime_tcp_read/accept/write` return `-EWOULDBLOCK` on an unready fd (the FFI doc says so). A caller that `coro.resume`s before the dispatcher signals readiness runs the syscall on an unready fd. **Corrected drive (design v2):** the *dispatcher* drives resume via the unchanged 2b.1 shim; the ramp self-allocates a `karac_runtime_park_slot_new()` (frame-resident) and returns it from the first suspend; the body `park_slot_signal`s + final-suspends on completion; the **call site only waits**: `slot=ramp(args); park_slot_wait(slot); park_slot_free(slot)` (no caller resume, no hidden param — and it's 2b.4's spawn shape minus the inline wait). Two consequences: (1) the 2b.2a `build_demo_park_coroutine` topology is split-correct but **drive-INCOMPATIBLE** — it `coro.free`s on the normal-completion path, which UAFs when the shim later does `coro.done`/`destroy`; the production topology must `coro.free` only on the *destroy* edge and final-suspend on completion (and not `ret` a frame-resident value from the freed-frame cleanup edge). (2) Drive-correctness is provable **only by a linked + executed + ASAN-clean run**, not CoroSplit-survival + IR grep — the topology has UAF traps that pass `module.verify()` and split cleanly yet fault at runtime. So 2b.3 is **re-rated 3–4** (was 2): emission scaffolding is small; iterating the frame-lifetime/return topology against the runtime+ASAN gate is the bulk. The gate strategy keeps the degenerate `emit_state_machine_poll_fn_for_key` as the default-off path (`Codegen.coro_enabled` setter, default off) so the ~60 existing poll-fn/drive tests stay green; flip-the-default + delete-degenerate-path is a later slice. *Slices 2b.2b + 2b.3 (done — green E2E + ASAN):* a network-boundary **free fn** now compiles + drives as a coroutine. Gate `Codegen.set_coro_enabled` (default off; `compile_to_object_with_coro` is the opt-in entry) → the ~60 poll-fn/drive tests + ASAN suite are untouched. `coro_fn_keys` = non-generic, non-`main`, non-dotted `state_struct_layouts` keys. Three toggles on `is_coroutine_compiled`: `declare_function` (`ptr` return + hidden trailing `ptr` slot param), `compile_function` (`emit_coro_ramp` + normal body + `emit_coro_finish`; returns routed to the completion block), `tcp.rs` leaf (`emit_coro_park_suspend`), call site (`slot=park_slot_new(); ramp(args,slot); park_slot_wait; park_slot_free` — dispatcher drives resume via the unchanged 2b.1 shim). **The design-v2 "ramp self-allocates + returns the slot" idea was itself corrected during implementation** (it forces a frame-resident return value that UAFs the freed-frame destroy clone, and a two-`coro.end` shape that LLVM rejects with *"Only one coro.end can be marked as fallthrough"*): final shape is **caller passes the slot in (hidden param), ramp returns `hdl`** through a **single** canonical `coro.end` that the cleanup edge branches into after `coro.free`. Both corrections were caught only by the runtime gate, exactly as the §6¾ note predicted. Gate: `tests/coro_e2e.rs` (functional + `-fsanitize=address`); bug C fixed E2E. The degenerate `emit_state_machine_poll_fn_for_key` is left emitted-but-dead for coro keys (DCE'd at -O). *Slice 2b.4 (done):* (a) **spawn** — a coroutine handler driven inside `spawn(\|\| handle(conn))` services a real connection E2E with **zero new codegen** (the `task_group.rs` spawn wrapper runs 2b.3's coro-drive on a pool worker, which the dispatcher unblocks; `join` returns on completion). Functionally correct but **thread-blocking** (one worker per concurrent handler) — density-optimal non-blocking spawn (wrapper ramps + returns, `TaskHandle` completion bound to the coroutine slot) is slice 5. (b) **method handlers** — dropped the free-fn-only restriction and added the coro ramp-drive to `method_call.rs`'s intercept (receiver = ramp `self` arg; impl methods are named by the dotted key via `make_impl_method_function`, so the toggles line up). Tests: `tests/coro_e2e.rs` `coroutine_spawned_free_fn_services_connection` + `coroutine_method_handler_services_connection`. *Slice 3 (done):* control flow around suspends **does** "just work" via CoroSplit — no codegen change. `tests/coro_e2e.rs` adds `coroutine_loop_handler_services_multiple_connections` (a `while` loop with one static `accept` suspend resumed across the back-edge, servicing 2 connections), `coroutine_loop_handler_under_asan` (same, ASAN-clean across iterations — frame re-registered + freed once), and `coroutine_if_branch_handler_services_connection` (park inside a taken `if` branch, post-join reachable on the resume edge). *Slice 4 (done):* drop-across-suspend correctness for heap locals (`Vec`/`String`/Map handle/RC box) live across a park. The completion path already dropped (body-end `emit_scope_cleanup` runs before the `coro_return` branch; the frame-resident buffer is freed on the resume edge). The gap + load-bearing trap was the **destroy/cancel edge**: after normal completion the coroutine parks at the *final* suspend, and the dispatcher's `coro.destroy` runs the destroy clone down *that* suspend's cleanup edge — so a single shared cleanup block reached by both the final suspend and the mid-flight parks would double-free (completion already dropped) or leak (no drops). Fix (Rust's per-suspend-point cleanup model): `emit_coro_park_suspend` routes each park's suspend-switch case-1 to a fresh per-park `kara.coro.destroy.N` block that **deregisters the fd** (else the event loop dangles a pointer into the about-to-be-freed frame) then drops the heap locals **live at that park** (`emit_coro_destroy_edge_drops` — a snapshot of the `scope_cleanup_actions` stack = the liveness oracle, skipping `UserDefer`/`UserErrDefer`), then branches to the shared free-only `cleanup_bb`; the **final** suspend's destroy edge stays free-only, so no value double-frees. The per-park destroy edge is **emitted-but-unreached** today (the only runtime `coro.destroy` is the dispatcher's post-completion one on the final suspend); a live cancel trigger is slice 5. Tests (`tests/coro_e2e.rs`): `coroutine_heap_local_across_park_services_connection` + `_under_asan` (a `Vec[i64]` live across the `accept` park, completion path, ASAN-clean — Linux `detect_leaks=1` is the leak gate), `coroutine_heap_local_freed_on_destroy_edge` (structural — the CoroSplit `.destroy` clone deregisters + `free`s the buffer on `kara.coro.destroy.0`; a non-heap contrast handler proves the free is tied to the live local). New public `compile_to_ir_with_coro_split` emits post-CoroSplit IR for the structural assertion. v1 limit: the destroy edge drops heap but does not run user `defer` (defer-on-cancel is slice-5c cancel semantics). *Slice 5a (done — density headline):* non-blocking spawn. The 2b.4 spawn was thread-blocking — the wrapper ran the coroutine's inline drive (`park_slot_new` + ramp + `park_slot_wait`) on a pool worker, pinning one OS thread per parked handler (the opposite of the per-conn-density thesis). New runtime `karac_runtime_spawn_coro(wrap_fn, env)` allocates a `KaracParkSlot` bound to the `KaracTaskHandle` and enqueues a worker that only **ramps** the coroutine (`wrap_fn(env, slot, cancel)` — register fd + suspend + return) and is **freed immediately**; the dispatcher drives the parked coroutine, whose body signals the slot at completion (its existing `emit_coro_finish` `park_slot_signal`). `karac_runtime_task_join` on a coro-handle waits on the bound slot, not the worker (`PENDING`-after-signal → COMPLETED; ramp-panic stores PANICKED + signals so the joiner still wakes; `free_handle` frees the slot). Codegen: `Codegen.coro_spawn_slot: Option<PointerValue>` flips the `is_coroutine_compiled` call-site intercept (`call_dispatch.rs` + `method_call.rs`) into "emit `ramp(args, slot)` and return — no `park_slot_new`/`wait`/`free`" for the wrapper-body compile; `task_group.rs::spawn_coro_tail_fn_key` detects a **tail free-fn coroutine call** (`spawn(\|\| handle(conn))`, directly or trivially block-wrapped), threads the wrapper's slot param through `coro_spawn_slot`, and calls `karac_runtime_spawn_coro`. **Tail free-fn closures only** (the ramp returns after the first suspend, so pre/post-call code would run while parked); method-handler / multi-statement / non-unit-tail shapes fall back to the 2b.4 blocking spawn. Gates: `runtime/src/scheduler.rs` — `spawn_coro_join_waits_on_completion_slot_not_worker` (join blocks ~60 ms on the slot while the ramp returned at once) + `spawn_coro_batch_larger_than_workers_all_complete` (64 ramps, no serialize/deadlock); `tests/coro_e2e.rs` — `nonblocking_spawn_uses_spawn_coro_ffi` (IR-structural), `coroutine_nonblocking_spawn_services_connection` + `_under_asan` (`tg.spawn(\|\| serve_one(listener))` services a real connection; TaskGroup-drop joins via the slot; ASAN-clean). `SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` += `karac_runtime_spawn_coro`. *Flip-default (done):* the A2 coroutine path is **on by default** for `karac build`/`run` (`compile_to_object_with_hot_swap`'s `coro_enabled` param; the test-facing `compile_to_object` chain stays on the degenerate path — convergence/retire-degenerate is a later slice). Flipping it on surfaced + fixed two coro×auto-par interactions (a coroutine body auto-parallelized → `coro.suspend` in a `__par_branch` referencing the outer frame; a spawn wrapper inside an auto-par'd group leaking the par-branch's `branch_cancel_ptr`). *WS-over-TLS (done):* `lower_websocket_io`'s `recv_text`/`send_text` already route through the coro park intercept; gated by `coro_e2e.rs::coroutine_ws_over_tls_handler_executes` (a real rustls `wss://` echo round-trip). *Concurrent accept-resume race (done):* `WebSocket.accept_tls` is self-waiting (drains the backlog into an async handshake pool + a 5 ms re-drain loop) — the codegen park-on-listener-readiness before it waited on the WRONG condition (a pending connection's handshake *completion* doesn't make the listener readable), wedging ~half of connections under load. Fix: `lower_websocket_accept_tls` drops the redundant park in the inline case (`coro_ctx` None — the accept loop runs on its own thread, so the function's correct self-wait blocks only that thread); gated by `coroutine_ws_over_tls_concurrent_handlers_all_execute`. *Slice 5c MECHANISM (done, `4186c3ac`):* resume shim checks `cancel` → `coro.destroy` (instead of resuming); the per-park destroy edge `park_slot_signal`s the slot so a cancelled coroutine's waiter wakes. Inert until a cancel flag is set; verified by `coroutine_cancel_mechanism_emitted`. *Slice 5c TRIGGER (done 2026-06-06):* per-task cancel routing (the flag lives on the registration — `FdState.cancel`, bound via `karac_runtime_event_loop_register_fd_cancel` from the coroutine's slot; the dispatcher hands each `poll_fn` that flag, null → global fallback) + the dispatcher cancel-sweep (`EventLoop::collect_cancelled`/`sweep_cancelled`, per-shard `sweep_requested` + `karac_runtime_request_cancel_sweep` from `taskgroup_cancel`, collect-then-invoke split to avoid the `fds`-lock-across-`poll_fn` deadlock) + the register-time park-vs-cancel race guard + the live mid-flight-cancel ASAN test. Keeping cancel on the registration (not in `KaracParkedTask` / the codegen parked record) left the record ABI unchanged across the coroutine and degenerate paths. Tests: `cancel_sweep_tears_down_idle_parked_task` (runtime unit), `coroutine_taskgroup_cancel_tears_down_idle_parked_handler` (+ `_under_asan`). RAII runs on cancel; user `defer`-on-cancel deferred (see the Open work front carve-out). *Remaining: 6 (EC2 per-conn density re-measure — user-run; local validation done + REPORT banner updated; task #19).* See spike § 6¾ + § 6⅞ + § 7.

  **BENCH STAKES (why landing A2 matters beyond correctness).** Bug C is the *direct* blocker for the `ws_idle_holder` density story: until a spawned handler actually executes + parks (2b.3/2b.4), the demo holds connections only as leaked-open fds, so the shipped per-conn density numbers (7.8 KB/conn, **3.55× vs Rust**, scale-invariance, x86 confirmation) were measured with **non-executing handlers** — they understate a working server and are not apples-to-apples with Rust (whose task holds its per-conn state). `bench/REPORT.md` now carries a ⚠️ provisional banner; full impact + repro in line 17 sub-bullet 2; the re-measure plan is `wip-bench-day.md` Phase 1.5 (gated on this work). Expected after A2 lands: per-conn-bytes ~7.8 → **~12–13 KB**, ratio → **~2–2.5×** (partly tunable via the demo's recv-buffer size). So 2b.3/2b.4 landing is the trigger to re-measure + correct REPORT.md / the M1·M3·x86 entries.
